Biographical Sources for Imam al-Bazdawi
Introduction to the biography and list of sources.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the key sources for the biography of Imam al-Bazdawi and explain their importance for Hanafi usul studies.

Core Idea
Knowing the sources of a scholar's biography situates his work within the Hanafi tradition.

This lesson introduces the biographical sources for Imam al-Bazdawi, the author of a foundational Hanafi usul text. The passage lists sources spanning four centuries, from al-Sam'ani to Ibn al-Hana'i. Understanding this list helps you connect the text of Usul al-Bazdawi to its historical chain of transmission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the earliest source
Find which source is mentioned first and note the author's death date. Al-Sam'ani (d. 562 AH) is the earliest – his direct proximity to al-Bazdawi makes his account valuable.
Al-Bazdawi died around 482 AH, so al-Sam'ani is only about a century later.
2
Trace the chronological chain
List the remaining sources in order of author death dates: Yaqut (626), al-Dhahabi (748), al-Qurashi (775), Ibn Qutlubugha (879), Tashkubri Zada (968), Ibn al-Hana'i (979). This shows continuous scholarly interest in preserving al-Bazdawi's legacy.
Each source belongs to a different era and genre – biographical dictionaries, tabaqat works, and encyclopedias.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمة الإمام البزدوي جاءت ترجمة الإمام البزدوي عند مترجميه مختصرة، غير مطولة، كعادتهم في كثير من تراجم الأئمة العلماء ، وقد جَمَعتُ ما كتبوه عنه ، إضافة ما وقفت عنه عَرَضاً في مقدمات كلام الأئمة شراح أصول البزدوي، ونحو هذا مما التقطته من الفوائد المنتثرة ، والدُرَرِ الكامنة. وإن أقدم من وقفتُ عليه ممن ذَكَرَ الإمام البزدوي وترجم له: هو الإمام السمعاني عبد الكريم بن محمد (ت٥٦٢هـ)، في كتابه: الأنساب ۲۰۱/۲، وأذكر فيما يلي بقية المصادر التي ترجمت له من المتقدمين والمتأخرين والمعاصرين : معجم البلدان لياقوت الحموي (٦٢٦هـ)، ٤٠٩/١. - سير أعلام النبلاء للذهبي (ت ٧٤٨هـ) ، ٦٠٢/١٨ . - الجواهر المضية في طبقات الحنفية للقرشي (ت٧٧٥هـ)، ٠٥٩٤/٢ تاج التراجم، لقاسم بن قطلوبغا (٨٧٩هـ) ، ص ٢٠٥ . مفتاح السعادة، لطاش كبري زاده (ت٩٦٨هـ)، ١٦٤/٢ . - طبقات الحنفية، لابن الحنائي (ت٩٧٩هـ).
Biography of Imam al-Bazdawi. The biography of Imam al-Bazdawi in the works of his biographers is brief, not lengthy, as is their custom in many biographies of scholar imams. I have collected what they have written about him, in addition to what I came across incidentally in the prefaces of the scholars who are commentators of the Usul of al-Bazdawi, and the like of what I have gleaned from scattered benefits and hidden pearls. The earliest one I have found who mentioned Imam al-Bazdawi and wrote his biography is Imam al-Sam'ani Abd al-Karim ibn Muhammad (d. 562 AH) in his book al-Ansab (2/201). I will mention below the remaining sources that wrote his biography from the earlier, later, and contemporary scholars: Mu'jam al-Buldan by Yaqut al-Hamawi (d. 626 AH), (1/409); Siyar A'lam al-Nubala' by al-Dhahabi (d. 748 AH), (18/602); al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya fi Tabaqat al-Hanafiyya by al-Qurashi (d. 775 AH), (2/594); Taj al-Tarajim by Qasim ibn Qutlubugha (d. 879 AH), p. 205; Miftah al-Sa'adah by Tashkubri Zada (d. 968 AH), (2/164); Tabaqat al-Hanafiyya by Ibn al-Hana'i (d. 979 AH).
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage introduces the biography of Imam al-Bazdawi, the author of the Usul text being edited. The editor notes that existing biographies are brief, so he has compiled information from various sources. He lists the earliest source as al-Sam'ani's al-Ansab, then provides a list of later biographical works including those by Yaqut, al-Dhahabi, al-Qurashi, Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, Tashkubri Zada, and Ibn al-Hana'i. This section is the beginning of a more detailed biographical sketch that follows in the book.

Key Terms
ترجمة (tarjama): In this context, 'biography' or 'biographical entry'.
أصول البزدوي (Usul al-Bazdawi): The usul al-fiqh text authored by Imam al-Bazdawi, one of the foundational works of Hanafi legal theory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, who is the earliest author to write a biography of Imam al-Bazdawi?
A) Yaqut al-Hamawi
B) Al-Sam'ani
C) Al-Dhahabi
D) Al-Qurashi

Key Takeaway
The biographical sources for Imam al-Bazdawi span four centuries, reflecting the enduring importance of his usul work.

Biography of Imam al-Bazdawi and Key Sources
Biographical introduction and annotated source list for Imam al-Bazdawi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the most important biographical sources for Imam al-Bazdawi and identify the earliest surviving work that mentions him.

Core Idea
Imam al-Bazdawi's life is known through layered biographical sources spanning centuries.

In this lesson, we explore the biographical tradition surrounding Imam al-Bazdawi, the author of Kanz al-Wusul. The passage presents a curated list of sources that preserve his life story. Understanding these sources equips you to locate primary and secondary material for studying Hanafi usul scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the earliest biographer
Find the first source mentioned: al-Sam'ani's 'al-Ansab'. Note the author's full name and death date (562 AH).
This is the earliest surviving biography of al-Bazdawi.
2
Recognize chronological range
Scan the list from earliest (6th century AH) to most recent (14th century AH). Observe the diversity of periods.
Sources span over 800 years.
3
Distinguish source types
Categorize each source: general biographical dictionaries (e.g., Siyar A'lam al-Nubala'), Hanafi-specific tabaqat (e.g., al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya), and modern reference works (e.g., al-A'lam).
Each type serves a different purpose.
4
Note page references
Observe the volume and page numbers given for each source. These allow direct access to the relevant sections.
Use these for efficient research.
5
Understand the compiler's method
The compiler collected from earlier brief notices and scattered benefits, not from a single comprehensive biography.
This explains why the list is curated, not exhaustive.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمة الإمام البزدوي
جاءت ترجمة الإمام البزدوي عند مترجميه مختصرة، غير مطولة، كعادتهم في كثير من تراجم الأئمة العلماء ، وقد جَمَعتُ ما كتبوه عنه ، إضافة ما وقفت عنه عَرَضاً في مقدمات كلام الأئمة شراح أصول البزدوي، ونحو هذا مما التقطته من الفوائد المنتثرة ، والدُرَرِ الكامنة. وإن أقدم من وقفتُ عليه ممن ذَكَرَ الإمام البزدوي وترجم له: هو الإمام السمعاني عبد الكريم بن محمد (ت٥٦٢هـ)، في كتابه: الأنساب ۲۰۱/۲، وأذكر فيما يلي بقية المصادر التي ترجمت له من المتقدمين والمتأخرين والمعاصرين :
معجم البلدان لياقوت الحموي (٦٢٦هـ)، ٤٠٩/١.
- سير أعلام النبلاء للذهبي (ت ٧٤٨هـ) ، ٦٠٢/١٨ . - الجواهر المضية في طبقات الحنفية للقرشي (ت٧٧٥هـ)،

مخطوط.
- الطبقات السنية، للتميمي (ت۱۰۱۰هـ)، رقم الترجمة (١٥٣٥). - الفوائد البهية في طبقات الحنفية، محمد عبد الحي اللكنوي ت ١٣٠٤هـ) ، ص ١٢٤ .
هدية العارفين أسماء المصنّفين للباباني البغدادي (ت١٣٣٩هـ)،
.٦٩٣/١
الفتح المبين في طبقات الأصوليين للمراغي (ت القرن الرابع عشر
الهجري)، ٢٦٣/١ .
الأعلام للزركلي (ت ١٣٩٦هـ)، ٣٢٨/٤.
المؤلفين ، لكحالة (ت ١٤٠٢هـ)، ١٩٢/٧ ـ معجم
Translation of Imam al-Bazdawi. The biography of Imam al-Bazdawi in his translators' works came concise, not lengthy, as is their habit in many biographies of notable imams. And I have collected what they wrote about him, in addition to what I came across incidentally in the prefaces of the words of the imams who commented on Usul al-Bazdawi, and the like of that which I picked up from scattered benefits and hidden pearls. And the earliest of those I came across who mentioned Imam al-Bazdawi and wrote his biography is Imam al-Sam'ani Abd al-Karim ibn Muhammad (d. 562 AH) in his book al-Ansab 2/201. And I mention below the remaining sources that wrote his biography among the early, later, and contemporary scholars: Mu'jam al-Buldan by Yaqut al-Hamawi (d. 626 AH) 1/409. - Siyar A'lam al-Nubala' by al-Dhahabi (d. 748 AH) 18/602. - al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya fi Tabaqat al-Hanafiyya by al-Qurashi (d. 775 AH) 2/594. Taj al-Tarajim by Qasim ibn Qutlubugha (d. 879 AH) p. 205. Miftah al-Sa'ada by Tash Kubri Zada (d. 968 AH) 2/164. - Tabaqat al-Hanafiyya by Ibn al-Hinnai (d. 979 AH). - Kata'ib A'lam al-Akhyar by al-Kafawi Mahmud ibn Sulayman (d. 990 AH), manuscript. - al-Tabaqat al-Saniyya by al-Tamimi (d. 1010 AH), biography no. 1535. - al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya fi Tabaqat al-Hanafiyya by Muhammad Abd al-Hayy al-Laknawi (d. 1304 AH) p. 124. Hadiyyat al-'Arifin Asma' al-Mu'allifin by al-Babani al-Baghdadi (d. 1339 AH) 1/693. al-Fath al-Mubin fi Tabaqat al-Usuliyyin by al-Maraghī (d. 14th century AH) 1/263. al-A'lam by al-Zirkili (d. 1396 AH) 4/328. Mu'jam al-Mu'allifin by Kahhala (d. 1402 AH) 7/192.
Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This is a biographical passage about Imam al-Bazdawi, the author of the famous Hanafi usul work 'Kanz al-Wusul ila Ma'rifat al-Usul'. The compiler of this edition introduces the biography by noting that earlier biographies were brief, and he has collected additional information from various sources. He lists the most important biographical sources, starting with the earliest: Imam al-Sam'ani's 'al-Ansab'. This is followed by a chronological list of works that contain al-Bazdawi's biography, including geographies, biographical dictionaries, and specialized works on Hanafi scholars. The list gives the author's name, death date, and volume/page references. This serves as an important research tool for students who wish to study the life of Imam al-Bazdawi in more depth.

Key Terms
البزدوي (al-Bazdawi): Imam Fakhr al-Islam 'Ali ibn Muhammad al-Bazdawi, a prominent Hanafi usul scholar (d. 482 AH/1089 CE), author of Kanz al-Wusul ila Ma'rifat al-Usul.
ترجمة (tarjama): Biography; a record of a scholar's life, teachers, students, and works.
طبقات (tabaqat): Biographical dictionaries arranged by generations or classes of scholars.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) al-Ansab by al-Sam'ani
C) al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya by al-Qurashi
D) Siyar A'lam al-Nubala' by al-Dhahabi

Key Takeaway
The biographical tradition for Imam al-Bazdawi begins with al-Sam'ani in al-Ansab and continues through specialized Hanafi tabaqat works.

Who was Fakhr al-Islam Ali al-Bazdawi?
Biographical entry on the author's name, lineage, nisbah, and birth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the full name, kunya, title, nisbah, birth year, and lineage of Imam Fakhr al-Islam Ali al-Bazdawi.

Core Idea
Fakhr al-Islam Ali al-Bazdawi: a giant of Hanafi usul from a golden chain of scholars in Transoxiana.

This lesson introduces you to the author of Kanz al-Wusul, one of the most important texts in Hanafi usul. Knowing his background helps you understand his authority and the scholarly tradition he represents.

Guided Path
1
Identify full name and lineage
Trace the seven-generation chain from Ali bin Muhammad back to Mujahid. Note the kunya Abu al-Hasan and Abu al-Usr.
The lineage establishes his connection to a scholarly family.
2
Note titles and kunyas
Recognise that 'Fakhr al-Islam' is a title shared by several scholars, but when unqualified it refers specifically to al-Bazdawi.
This avoids confusion with other scholars bearing the same title.
3
Locate the nisbah and its origin
Al-Bazdawi derives from Bazdah, a fortress six farsakhs from Nasaf on the road to Bukhara. The correct pronunciation has fatha on ba and dal, sukun on zay.
Understanding nisbahs helps in identifying geographical roots of scholars.
4
Recognise family prestige
His family is described as a 'golden chain' in fiqh, usul, hadith, and other sciences, with both father and grandfather being distinguished scholars.
This underscores the authority and reliability of his works.
5
Remember the birth year
He was born around 400 AH (approx. 1010 CE).
This places him in the classical period of Hanafi scholarship.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اسمه ونسبه وولادته :
علي بن محمد بن الحسين بن عبد الكريم بن موسى بن عيسى بن مجاهد، أبو الحسن المعروف بفخر الإسلام ، أبو العُسر البزدوي الفقيه الأصولي المحدث المفسر ، الإمام الكبير بما وراء النهر.
ولد في حدود سنة ٤٠٠هـ.
والبَرْدَوي: بفتح الباء المنقوطة بواحدة، وسكون الزاي، وفتح الدال المهملة وفي آخرها الواو ، هذه النسبة إلى بَزْدَه ، وهي قلعة حصينة على ستة فراسخ من نسف على طريق بخاری.
وفي تاج العروس للزَّبيدي : بَزْدَه ، ويقال : بَزْدَوَه، قد أهمله الجوهري، وهي بلدة من أعمال نَسف، وهي قلعة حصينة على ستة 101 فراسخ منها، والنسبة إليها: بَزْدِيُّ، وبَزْدَوِي.
- وفخر الإسلام لقب جماعة، وعند الإطلاق: يراد به صاحب الترجمة الإمام فخر الإسلام علي البزدوي.
وهو من بيت كبير عال في العلم والفضل والأدب، ومن سلسلة ذهب في الفقه والأصول والحديث وغيرها، وقد  أباً عن جد في علوم مختلفة
His name, lineage and birth: Ali bin Muhammad bin al-Husayn bin Abd al-Karim bin Musa bin Isa bin Mujahid, Abu al-Hasan known as Fakhr al-Islam, Abu al-Usr al-Bazdawi, the jurist, usuli, muhaddith, mufassir, the great imam of Transoxiana. He was born around the year 400 AH. Al-Bazdawi: with a fatha on the ba, sukun on the zay, fatha on the dal, and at the end a waw; this is the nisba to Bazdah, which is a fortified fortress six farsakhs from Nasaf on the road to Bukhara. In Taj al-Arus by al-Zabidi: Bazdah, and it is said Bazdawah; al-Jawhari neglected it; it is a town of the Nasaf district, a fortified fortress six farsakhs from it; the nisba to it is Bazdi and Bazdawi. - Fakhr al-Islam is a title shared by a group; when unqualified, it refers to the subject of this biography, Imam Fakhr al-Islam Ali al-Bazdawi. He was from a great family high in knowledge, virtue, and literature, and from a golden chain in fiqh, usul, hadith, and other fields; he was, father and grandfather, in various sciences.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage is a biographical entry about the author of Kanz al-Wusul, Imam Fakhr al-Islam Ali al-Bazdawi. It begins by giving his full name and lineage, tracing back seven generations to Mujahid. His kunyas are Abu al-Hasan and Abu al-Usr. He is known by the title Fakhr al-Islam, a title shared by several scholars, but when used absolutely it refers to al-Bazdawi. The passage explains the nisbah 'al-Bazdawi': it derives from Bazdah, a fortified fortress six farsakhs from Nasaf (in present-day Uzbekistan). The correct pronunciation is with a fatha on the ba, sukun on the zay, and fatha on the dal. He was born around 400 AH (approximately 1010 CE), making him a contemporary of other great Hanafi scholars. The biography emphasizes his noble lineage: he came from a family of scholars, a 'golden chain' in fiqh, usul, hadith, and other sciences, with his father and grandfather also being distinguished in various fields. This establishes his authority as a source of Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
البزدوي (al-Bazdawi): Nisbah referring to the town of Bazdah (or Bazdawah) near Nasaf in Transoxiana.
فخر الإسلام (Fakhr al-Islam): A title meaning 'Pride of Islam', used for several scholars but when unqualified refers to al-Bazdawi.
بَزْدَه (Bazdah): A fortified fortress six farsakhs from Nasaf on the road to Bukhara.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Where does the nisbah 'al-Bazdawi' come from?
A) A village near Bukhara called Bazdah
B) A street in Nasaf
C) A tribe in Transoxiana
D) A type of cloth

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Bazdawi, Fakhr al-Islam, was a towering Hanafi usuli from a distinguished scholarly family in Transoxiana, born around 400 AH.

Life of the Author

The Life and Lineage of Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi
Biographical introduction with lineage and family background

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the full name, lineage, titles, and scholarly family of Imam Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi.

Core Idea
Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi: the 'Glory of Islam' from a golden chain of Hanafi scholars.

Before diving into the usul text of al-Bazdawi, it is essential to know the author himself. This passage introduces us to his full name, his lineage connecting him to the great Hanafi tradition through Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, and his distinguished family. Understanding his background helps us appreciate the authority of his work and the scholarly environment that produced him.

Guided Path
1
Identify the full name and nisba
Extract his full name: Ali ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn... al-Bazdawi. Note the nisba refers to Bazdah, a castle near Nasaf.
The nisba 'al-Bazdawi' is key to locating him geographically.
2
Understand the title 'Fakhr al-Islam'
Recognize that this title is used absolutely for this Imam, though it can apply to others. It means 'Glory of Islam'.
When you see 'Fakhr al-Islam' in usul texts, it usually refers to al-Bazdawi.
3
Recognize the scholarly chain
Trace his grandfather's chain: Abd al-Karim took from al-Maturidi, from al-Juzjani, from Abu Sulayman, from Muhammad al-Shaybani. This connects al-Bazdawi directly to the founders of the Hanafi school.
This chain gives authority to his usul methodology.
4
Distinguish the two Bazdawi brothers
Note the two brothers: Fakhr al-Islam (Abu al-Usr) and Sadr al-Islam (Abu al-Yusr). Their titles reflect the difficulty or ease of their works.
This distinction is important for understanding their respective contributions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اسمه ونسبه وولادته :
علي بن محمد بن الحسين بن عبد الكريم بن موسى بن عيسى بن مجاهد، أبو الحسن المعروف بفخر الإسلام ، أبو العُسر البزدوي الفقيه الأصولي المحدث المفسر ، الإمام الكبير بما وراء النهر. ولد في حدود سنة ٤٠٠هـ.
والبَرْدَوي: بفتح الباء المنقوطة بواحدة، وسكون الزاي، وفتح الدال المهملة وفي آخرها الواو ، هذه النسبة إلى بَزْدَه ، وهي قلعة حصينة على ستة فراسخ من نسف على طريق بخاری.
وفي تاج العروس للزَّبيدي : بَزْدَه ، ويقال : بَزْدَوَه، قد أهمله الجوهري، وهي بلدة من أعمال نَسف، وهي قلعة حصينة على ستة فراسخ منها، والنسبة إليها: بَزْدِيُّ، وبَزْدَوِي.
- وفخر الإسلام لقب جماعة، وعند الإطلاق: يراد به صاحب الترجمة الإمام فخر الإسلام علي البزدوي.
وهو من بيت كبير عال في العلم والفضل والأدب، ومن سلسلة ذهب في الفقه والأصول والحديث وغيرها، وقد أباً عن جد في علوم مختلفة نالوا منها الحظ الوافر ، وسرى هذا في أولادهم وذريتهم، والله يعطي الفضل من يشاء. أما جده الأعلى : فهو عبد الكريم بن موسى البزدوي : كان إماماً فقيهاً محدثاً متكلماً، أخذ عن إمام الهدى أبي منصور الماتريدي (ت٣٣٣هـ) عن أبي بكر الجوزجاني عن أبي سليمان عن محمد بن الحسن الشيباني، رحمه الله. وحدَّث، وتوفي سنة ٣٩٠هـ وقد سمع و.
وأما صاحب الترجمة : فخر الإسلام أبو العسر، وأخوه صدر الإسلام أبو اليسر فإنهما كانا واسطتي عقد البيت البزدوي، وإليهما انتهت رئاستهم وبهما كَمُلت سيادتهم وهما المعروفان: بالصدرين البزدويين.
- وقد سُمِّي الأخ الأكبر فخر الإسلام بأبي العسر؛ لعسر تصانيفه، صدر الإسلام بأبي اليسر ؛ ليسر تصانيفه. وسمي وأخوه أبو اليسر هو : محمد بن محمد بن الحسين بن عبد الكريم البزدوي كان من فحول العلماء المناظرين، بل يقول تلميذه نجم الأئمة النسفي عمر بن محمد صاحب طلبة الطلبة»، و«المنظومة في الخلاف»، يقول عنه في كتابه: «القَند في ذكر علماء سمرقند»: كان إمام الأئمة على الإطلاق، والموفود إليه من الآفاق، ملأ الشرق
His name, lineage and birth: Ali ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn ibn Abd al-Karim ibn Musa ibn Isa ibn Mujahid, Abu al-Hasan known as Fakhr al-Islam, Abu al-Usr al-Bazdawi, the jurist, usuli scholar, hadith narrator, exegete, the great imam of Transoxiana. He was born around the year 400 AH. Al-Bazdawi: with fatha on the dotted baa, sukun on the zay, fatha on the dal, and at the end waw; this is the nisba to Bazdah, which is a fortified castle six farsakhs from Nasaf on the road to Bukhara. In Taj al-Arus by al-Zabidi: Bazdah, also said Bazdawah, al-Jawhari neglected it; it is a town in the district of Nasaf, a fortified castle six farsakhs from it, and the nisba to it is Bazdi and Bazdawi. Fakhr al-Islam is a title for a group, but when used absolutely it refers to the subject of this biography, Imam Fakhr al-Islam Ali al-Bazdawi. He was from a great household advanced in knowledge, virtue, and literature, and from a golden chain in fiqh, usul, hadith and other sciences; they obtained abundant fortune in various sciences, and this continued in their children and descendants, and Allah gives grace to whom He wills. As for his grandfather: He is Abd al-Karim ibn Musa al-Bazdawi: he was an imam, jurist, hadith narrator, theologian; he took from Imam al-Huda Abu Mansur al-Maturidi (d. 333 AH) from Abu Bakr al-Juzjani from Abu Sulayman from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, may Allah have mercy on him. He narrated hadith and died in the year 390 AH. As for the subject of this biography: Fakhr al-Islam Abu al-Usr, and his brother Sadr al-Islam Abu al-Yusr, they were the central figures of the Bazdawi household; to them their leadership ended and with them their mastery was completed; they are known as the two Bazdawi leaders. The elder brother Fakhr al-Islam was named Abu al-Usr because of the difficulty of his works; Sadr al-Islam was named Abu al-Yusr because of the ease of his works. His brother Abu al-Yusr is: Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn ibn Abd al-Karim al-Bazdawi; he was among the great debating scholars; rather his student Najm al-Aimma al-Nasafi Umar ibn Muhammad, author of Talbat al-Talaba and al-Manzuma fi al-Khilaf, says about him in his book al-Qand fi Dhikr Ulama Samarqand: He was the imam of imams absolutely, the one traveled to from all horizons, he filled the east.
Source pages p. 13

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to Imam Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi, the author of this usul text. It provides his full name, lineage, birth date, and explains the nisba 'al-Bazdawi' referring to a fortress near Nasaf. The text highlights that he came from a distinguished scholarly family, with his grandfather having studied from Imam al-Maturidi through a chain to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. It also introduces his brother Sadr al-Islam Abu al-Yusr, and explains the nicknames: Fakhr al-Islam was called Abu al-Usr (father of difficulty) because his works were difficult, while his brother was called Abu al-Yusr (father of ease) because his works were easy. The passage underscores the high status of the two brothers as the leaders of their household and their reputation as the 'two Bazdawis'.

Key Terms
فخر الإسلام (Fakhr al-Islam): Title meaning 'Glory of Islam', used for a group but specifically refers to Imam Ali al-Bazdawi when used absolutely.
أبو العسر (Abu al-Usr): Title meaning 'Father of Difficulty', given to Fakhr al-Islam because his works were difficult.
البزدوي (al-Bazdawi): Nisba referring to Bazdah, a fortified castle six farsakhs from Nasaf on the road to Bukhara.
صدر الإسلام (Sadr al-Islam): Title meaning 'Chest of Islam', given to Abu al-Yusr al-Bazdawi.
أبو اليسر (Abu al-Yusr): Title meaning 'Father of Ease', given to the brother of Fakhr al-Islam because his works were easy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi is the author of this usul text, from a distinguished Hanafi scholarly family with a direct chain to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.

The Scholarly Legacy of the Bazdawi Family
Biographical introduction of the author's family and scholarly achievements

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key figures of the Bazdawi family and explain their significance in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
The Bazdawi family's two leading scholars, al-Sadrain, shaped Hanafi usul through their writings and scholarly lineage.

This passage introduces us to the author of our usul text, Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi. Understanding his scholarly lineage helps us appreciate the authority of his work. We will meet his grandfather, his brother Abu al-Yusr, and his son, all part of a distinguished Hanafi-Maturidi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main figures
List the Bazdawi family members mentioned: the grandfather (Abd al-Karim), the two brothers (Fakhr al-Islam and Sadr al-Islam), and the author's son (al-Hasan).
Note the death dates where given.
2
Trace the scholarly chain
Follow the transmission from grandfather to al-Maturidi and further back to Muhammad al-Shaybani. This connects the family to the core of Hanafi fiqh.
Abd al-Karim studied from al-Maturidi, who studied from al-Juzjani, etc.
3
Understand the nicknames
Explain why Fakhr al-Islam was called Abu al-‘Usr and his brother Abu al-Yusr. The passage states it is due to the difficulty or ease of their writings.
Do not confuse with personal character.
4
Recognize the title 'al-Sadrain'
The brothers are collectively known as 'al-Sadrain' (the two Sadrs), indicating their leadership in the family and scholarship.
This is a title of high esteem.
5
Appreciate the broader significance
Reflect on how this lineage enhances the authority of al-Bazdawi's usul work, Kanz al-Wusul, as it comes from a family deeply rooted in Hanafi knowledge.
This is front matter that establishes credibility.

نالوا منها الحظ الوافر، وسرى هذا في أولادهم وذريتهم، والله يعطي الفضل من يشاء. أما جده الأعلى: فهو عبد الكريم بن موسى البزدوي: كان إماماً فقيهاً محدثاً متكلماً، أخذ عن إمام الهدى أبي منصور الماتريدي عن أبي بكر الجوزجاني عن أبي سليمان عن محمد بن الحسن الشيباني، رحمه الله. وحدَّث، وتوفي سنة ٣٩٠هـ. وأما صاحب الترجمة: فخر الإسلام أبو العسر، وأخوه صدر الإسلام أبو اليسر فإنهما كانا واسطتي عقد البيت البزدوي، وإليهما انتهت رئاستهم وبهما كَمُلت سيادتهم وهما المعروفان: بالصدرين البزدويين. وقد سُمِّي الأخ الأكبر فخر الإسلام بأبي العسر؛ لعسر تصانيفه، وصدر الإسلام بأبي اليسر؛ ليسر تصانيفه. وأخوه أبو اليسر هو: محمد بن محمد بن الحسين بن عبد الكريم البزدوي كان من فحول العلماء المناظرين، بل يقول تلميذه نجم الأئمة النسفي عمر بن محمد صاحب "طلبة الطلبة"، و"المنظومة في الخلاف"، يقول عنه في كتابه: "القند في ذكر علماء سمرقند": كان إمام الأئمة على الإطلاق، والموفود إليه من الآفاق، ملأ الشرق والغرب بتصانيفه في الأصول والفروع، وكان قاضي القضاة توفي ببخارى سنة ٤٩٣هـ. وأما ولد المترجم أبي العسر فهو الإمام الفقيه القاضي الحسن بن علي بن محمد البزدوي، المولود سنة ٤٧٦هـ، والمتوفى سنة ٥٥٧هـ، له ترجمة في الجواهر المضية للقرشي.
They attained abundant fortune, and this spread among their children and descendants, and Allah gives bounty to whom He wills. As for his highest grandfather: he is ‘Abd al-Karim ibn Musa al-Bazdawi: he was an imam, jurist, hadith scholar, theologian; he studied from Imam al-Huda Abu Mansur al-Maturidi from Abu Bakr al-Juzjani from Abu Sulayman from Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, may Allah have mercy on him. He narrated hadith and died in 390 AH. As for the subject of this biography: Fakhr al-Islam Abu al-‘Usr, and his brother Sadr al-Islam Abu al-Yusr, they were the two central figures of the Bazdawi household; to them leadership ended and with them their mastery was completed; they are known as the two Sadrs (al-Sadrain al-Bazdawiyayn). And the older brother Fakhr al-Islam was named Abu al-‘Usr because his writings were difficult (nasr), and Sadr al-Islam was named Abu al-Yusr because his writings were easy. And his brother Abu al-Yusr is: Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn ibn ‘Abd al-Karim al-Bazdawi, he was among the foremost debating scholars; indeed his student Najm al-A’imma al-Nasafi, ‘Umar ibn Muhammad, author of Tulbat al-Talabah and al-Manzumah fi al-Khilaf, said about him in his book al-Qand fi Dhikr ‘Ulama’ Samarqand: 'He was the imam of imams absolutely, the one journeyed to from all regions; he filled the East and West with his writings in usul and furu’; he was the chief judge; he died in Bukhara in 493 AH.' As for the son of the subject (Abu al-‘Usr): he is the imam, jurist, judge al-Hasan ibn ‘Ali ibn Muhammad al-Bazdawi, born in 476 AH and died in 557 AH; he has a biography in al-Jawahir al-Mudiyyah by al-Qurashi.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage provides biographical background for the author of our text, Fakhr al-Islam Abu al-‘Usr al-Bazdawi (d. 482 AH, but here his brother's death is 493, and author's son dies 557, so the author's death likely around 482? Actually the text doesn't give author's death here. But noted). The passage describes the Bazdawi family lineage, emphasizing that they were a scholarly family who attained great fortune in knowledge and transmitted it through generations. The grandfather, ‘Abd al-Karim al-Bazdawi, was a student of Abu Mansur al-Maturidi, linking the family to the Maturidi theological school. The author himself, along with his brother Abu al-Yusr, were known as 'al-Sadrain' (the two Sadrs). Their nicknames indicate the difficulty or ease of their works. The brother Abu al-Yusr was a prolific scholar praised by his student al-Nasafi. The author's son also became a notable judge. This front matter establishes the authority and scholarly heritage of the Bazdawi family, venerating their contributions to Hanafi usul and furu’.

Key Terms
صدران (al-Sadrain): The two prominent figures; here refers to Fakhr al-Islam Abu al-‘Usr and his brother Sadr al-Islam Abu al-Yusr, the leading scholars of the Bazdawi family.
فخر الإسلام (Fakhr al-Islam): Title meaning 'pride of Islam', given to the older brother Abu al-‘Usr al-Bazdawi.
أبو العسر / أبو اليسر (Abu al-‘Usr / Abu al-Yusr): Nicknames meaning 'father of difficulty' and 'father of ease', respectively, referring to the difficulty/ease of their scholarly works.

Biography of al-Hasan ibn Ali al-Bazdawi
Providing birth, death, and reference for the son of al-Bazdawi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the birth and death years of al-Hasan al-Bazdawi and identify his position as a Hanafi jurist and judge.

Core Idea
Al-Hasan al-Bazdawi continued his father's scholarly legacy in Hanafi usul.

This brief passage introduces an important figure in the transmission of Hanafi usul: al-Hasan ibn Ali al-Bazdawi, the son of the famous Fakh al-Islam al-Bazdawi. Knowing the timeline of scholars helps us understand the chains of transmission and the development of the madhhab. Even a short biographical entry like this one anchors the history of Hanafi thought.

Guided Path
1
Identify the person
Read the name: al-Hasan ibn Ali ibn Muhammad al-Bazdawi. He is the son of the earlier mentioned translator (Fakh al-Islam).
His lineage shows his connection to the Hanafi scholarly tradition.
2
Note the titles
He is described as Imam, faqih (jurist), and qadi (judge). These titles indicate his high scholarly rank and authority.
Titles like 'Imam' are significant in Hanafi biographical literature.
3
Record the birth and death
Born 476 AH, died 557 AH. This places him in the 12th century CE, roughly two generations after the founding of the school.
These dates help contextualize his works and teachers.
4
Identify the sources
The passage cites al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya by al-Qurashi and al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya for further biography.
These are standard Hanafi biographical dictionaries.

The Scholarly Praises of Imam Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi and the Term 'Tariqa'
Biographical praise and technical definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the identities of the scholars who praised al-Bazdawi, explain the meaning of 'tariqa' in Hanafi usul, and identify its significance for the study of usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Al-Bazdawi's 'tariqa' established the Hanafi method of debate and proof—the very backbone of usul studies.

This lesson introduces you to Imam Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi through the praises of later Hanafi masters. Understanding his stature and his methodological contribution—the 'tariqa'—is essential before studying his seminal work on usul al-fiqh. The term 'tariqa' here is a technical term for the Hanafi approach to argumentation, not a Sufi order.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholars and their praises
List al-Sam'ani, al-Saghnaqi, and al-Dhahabi, and note the key phrases they used (teacher of imams, jurist of Transoxiana, etc.).
Pay attention to the honorific 'Fakhr al-Islam'.
2
Understand the technical term 'tariqa'
Explain that in this context, 'tariqa' refers to the method of debate and inference (jadal and istidlal) established by the Hanafi imams, and that it later became a genre.
Do not confuse with Sufi orders.
3
Appreciate the significance
Recognize that this praise establishes al-Bazdawi's authority and the importance of his work, which is foundational for the study of Hanafi usul.
Consider how his work became the standard text for later commentaries.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثناء العلماء عليه لقد بلغ ثناء الأئمة العلماء على الإمام فخر الإسلام البزدوي أعلاه، ونال من المجد العلمي منتهاه، حيث وصف بأنه أستاذ الأئمة، وأي أئمة؟ أئمةُ قرن ذروة العلم، وهو القرن الخامس الهجري، فقد قال الحافظ السمعاني (ت ٥٦٢هـ) وغيره في وصفه: (1) الإمام فخر الإسلام البزدوي علي بن محمد، فقيه ما وراء النهر، وأستاذ الأئمة، وصاحب الطريقة على مذهب أبي حنيفة رحمه الله. اهـ ولفظ الطريقة يراد به الطريقة التي وضعها الأئمة لسلوك آداب طريق المناظرة والجدل والاستدلال والجواب، ثم أُطلقت هذه اللفظة على كل كتاب في هذا الباب. ووصفه الإمام الصغناقي (ت ٧١٤هـ) في «الكافي» شرح أصول البزدوي ۱۳۸/۱ بقوله: الإمام الزاهد المحقق، والحبر المدقق، ذي البركات الباهرة، والكرامات الظاهرة، فخر الإسلام البزدوي. اهـ * وقال عنه الإمام الذهبي (ت٧٤٨هـ) (٢) : (۱) الأنساب ۲۰۱/۲ (۲) سير أعلام النبلاء ٦٠٢/١٨.
Praise of the scholars upon him: The praise of the leading scholars reached the highest level for Imam Fakh al-Islam al-Bazdawi, and he attained the utmost scientific glory, as he was described as the teacher of the imams. And which imams? The imams of the century at the peak of knowledge, which is the fifth century Hijri. Al-Hafiz al-Sam'ani (d. 562 AH) and others said in his description: (1) 'Imam Fakh al-Islam al-Bazdawi Ali ibn Muhammad, the jurist of Transoxiana, the teacher of the imams, and the author of the method (al-tariqa) according to the school of Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him.' End quote. And the term al-tariqa refers to the method that the imams established for observing the etiquette of the path of debate, argumentation, inference, and response. Then this term was applied to every book in this field. And Imam al-Saghnaqi (d. 714 AH) described him in al-Kafi, commentary on Usul al-Bazdawi, 1/138, saying: 'The ascetic, verifying imam, the penetrating scholar, possessor of abundant blessings and manifest miracles, Fakh al-Islam al-Bazdawi.' End quote. And Imam al-Dhahabi (d. 748 AH) said about him: (2) (1) al-Ansab 2/201 (2) Siyar A'lam al-Nubala' 18/602.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage collects the tributes paid to Imam Fakh al-Islam al-Bazdawi by later scholars, establishing his towering status in the Hanafi school. It begins by stating that he was praised as 'the teacher of the imams' — a reference to the great scholars of the fifth century. Al-Sam'ani's description highlights his position as the leading jurist of Transoxiana and the originator of the 'tariqa' method, a technical term for the systematic approach to debate and inference in Hanafi jurisprudence. This method later became a genre of its own. Al-Saghnaqi, in his commentary on al-Bazdawi's own Usul work, adds accolades for his piety and miraculous deeds. Finally, al-Dhahabi's praise is referenced from his biographical dictionary Siyar A'lam al-Nubala'. This establishes the author's authority and the importance of his work, Kitab al-Usul.

Key Terms
الطريقة (al-tariqa): The method of debate and argumentation in Hanafi usul, established by the imams; later used to refer to any book on this subject.
فخر الإسلام (Fakh al-Islam): An honorific title meaning 'Pride of Islam' given to al-Bazdawi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Fakh al-Islam
B) Teacher of the imams
C) Jurist of Transoxiana
D) Author of al-Hidayah

Key Takeaway
The praises of al-Bazdawi establish his authority and highlight his development of the 'tariqa' – the foundational Hanafi method of usul argumentation.

The Stature of Imam al-Bazdawi and the Meaning of al-Ṭarīqah
Biographical introduction praising al-Bazdawi's scholarly stature

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key biographical details of Imam al-Bazdawi and explain the technical definition of 'al-Ṭarīqah' in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Al-Bazdawi is called the 'teacher of imams' and his method (al-Ṭarīqah) defines Hanafi usul debate.

This passage collects praises from major Hanafi scholars across centuries, establishing Imam al-Bazdawi as the foremost authority in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. Beyond the accolades, the text clarifies a key technical term: 'al-Ṭarīqah'. Understanding this term is essential to grasp Bazdawi's unique methodological contribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the quoting scholars
Make a mental list of the six scholars and their centuries: al-Sam'ani (6th), al-Sighnaqi (8th), al-Dhahabi (8th), al-Bukhari (8th), Sadr al-Shari'ah (8th), al-Babarti (8th).
This shows the continuous recognition of al-Bazdawi's authority for over two centuries.
2
Locate the key title
All scholars call al-Bazdawi 'Sahib al-Tariqah' (master of the method). Circle this title in your text.
This is his distinctive epithet.
3
Define 'al-Ṭarīqah' from the text
Read the definition given: 'the method that the imams laid down for observing the etiquette of debate, argumentation, inference, and response.'
This is a technical, juristic term, not a Sufi path.
4
Explain the significance
The praise establishes that al-Bazdawi systematized the Hanafi method of dialectical reasoning, which later became a genre of usul literature.
This emphasizes his role as the authority for 'al-Tariqah al-Bazdawiyyah'.

Praise of scholars for him: Indeed the praise of the leading scholars for Imam Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi has reached its peak, and he attained the utmost in scholarly glory, as he was described as the teacher of the imams. And what imams? The imams of the century that was the pinnacle of knowledge, which is the fifth century Hijri. Al-Hafiz al-Sam'ani (d. 562 AH) and others said in describing him: (1) 'Imam Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi, Ali ibn Muhammad, the jurist of Transoxiana, the teacher of the imams, and the author of the method (sahib al-tariqah) according to the school of Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him.' End quote. The term 'tariqah' here refers to the method that the imams laid down for observing the etiquette of debate, argumentation, inference, and response; then this term was applied to every book in this field. Imam al-Sighnaqi (d. 714 AH) described him in al-Kafi, a commentary on al-Bazdawi's Usul, 1/138, saying: 'The ascetic, verifying Imam, the penetrating scholar, possessor of brilliant blessings and manifest miracles, Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi.' End quote. * Imam al-Dhahabi (d. 748 AH) said about him (2): 'The shaykh of the Hanafis, the scholar of Transoxiana, Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn Abd al-Karim al-Bazdawi, the author of the method (sahib al-tariqah). Al-Sam'ani said: He only narrated from his companion Abu al-Ma'ali Muhammad ibn Nasr al-Khatib. He said: He was the imam of the companions (i.e., Hanafi scholars) in Transoxiana, and he authored magnificent works. He taught in Samarkand, and he was one of those held up as an example in memorization of the school.' End quote. Imam Abd al-Aziz ibn Ahmad al-Bukhari (d. 730 AH) described him in the introduction to his commentary on al-Bazdawi's Usul, Kashf al-Asrar, saying: 'The great shaykh, the venerated imam, the honored noble scholar, the pious, righteous, lordly scholar, the supporter of the Nu'mani school, the model of verifiers, the exemplar of scrutinizers, possessor of lofty stations and sublime miracles, the pride of mankind, Fakhr al-Islam Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn al-Bazdawi.' End quote. Imam Sadr al-Shari'ah Ubayd Allah ibn Mas'ud (d. 747 AH) described him in the introduction to his book Tanqih al-Usul, saying: 'The shaykh, the imam, the one followed by the great imams.' End quote. Imam al-Babarti (d. 786 AH) said in the introduction to al-Taqrir, a commentary on al-Bazdawi's Usul, 1/75: 'The great imam (al-qarm meaning the supreme leader), the energetic, the orbit of the planets of realities, the vessel (ship) of the sea of subtleties, the propagator of the precedence of transmitted and rational knowledge, the builder of the structures of subsidiary and foundational matters, the precisian of meanings, the establisher of principles, the model for mankind, Fakhr al-Islam.' End quote.
Source pages p. 16

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction praising Imam Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi, the author of the foundational text in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author collects encomiums from several major scholars spanning the 6th to 8th centuries Hijri, establishing al-Bazdawi's authority and the esteem in which he was held. The key title emphasized is 'Sahib al-Tariqah' (author of the method). The text clarifies that 'tariqah' here does not refer to a Sufi path but to a distinct method of debate and argumentation (adab al-munazara) that al-Bazdawi systematized for Hanafi usul. This method came to be known as 'al-Tariqah' and was applied to various works in this field. The various scholars—al-Sam'ani, al-Sighnaqi, al-Dhahabi, al-Bukhari, Sadr al-Shari'ah, and al-Babarti—each laud al-Bazdawi as a jurist, verifier, and teacher. Notably, al-Babarti uses the term 'al-Qarm' (السيد المعظم) to denote his supreme leadership. The passage serves to introduce the author and the text, underscoring that al-Bazdawi's work is the standard reference for Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
الطريقة (al-Ṭarīqah): The method of debate, argumentation, inference, and response (Ādāb al-Munāẓarah) as systematized by the imams, especially al-Bazdawi. It later became a genre term for works on this subject.
فخر الإسلام (Fakhr al-Islām): Title meaning 'Pride of Islam' awarded to al-Bazdawi by his contemporaries, reflecting his high status as a leading Hanafi jurist and usuli.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what does the term 'al-Ṭarīqah' refer to in the context of al-Bazdawi's work?
A) A Sufi spiritual path
B) A method of debate and argumentation in jurisprudence
C) A school of legal thought (madhhab)
D) A genre of biographical dictionaries

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Bazdawi is the central figure in Hanafi usul al-fiqh, and his methodological approach is known as 'al-Tariqah'.

Imam al-Bazdawi: A Hanafi Authority in Usul al-Fiqh
Biographical account with scholarly eulogies

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key scholarly praises of Imam al-Bazdawi and explain their significance for his authority in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Al-Bazdawi is celebrated as the 'Shaykh of the Hanafiyya' and a leading authority in both furu' and usul.

This lesson introduces you to Imam al-Bazdawi, the author of a foundational text in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. We will explore how later scholars described his stature, emphasizing his mastery of both transmitted and rational sciences. Understanding the weight of these endorsements helps you appreciate why his usul work became a central reference in the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the full name and lineage
State al-Bazdawi's complete name as given: Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn Abd al-Karim al-Bazdawi. Note his title 'Shaykh of the Hanafiyya' and his origin from Transoxiana.
This establishes his identity and regional prominence.
2
List the praising scholars and their key phrases
From the text, note each scholar (al-Sam'ani, al-Bukhari, Sadr al-Shari'a, al-Babarti, al-Kafawi, al-Ansari) and pick one characteristic phrase per scholar that highlights al-Bazdawi's excellence.
Focus on how each title (e.g., 'leader of the companions', 'exemplar of investigators') builds his scholarly profile.
3
Analyze the nature of the praises
Categorize the praises: some emphasize his mastery of fiqh (furu'), others his expertise in usul, and others his overall comprehensiveness. For example, al-Babarti mentions both 'transmitted and rational knowledge' and 'branches and principles'.
This shows the breadth of his authority.
4
Evaluate the significance of the teacher/student section
The text notes that al-Bazdawi's teachers are not named but he came from a scholarly family. It also mentions only one student by name. Reflect on why biographers might have omitted these details and what it implies about the preservation of his legacy.
The absence of named teachers does not diminish his stature; rather, it highlights his role as a transmitter of a family tradition.
5
Connect to usul al-fiqh
Explain that the praises establish al-Bazdawi's authority as a reliable source for usul al-fiqh. Later Hanafi scholars relied on his methodology (al-tariqa), and his work became a standard text. This justifies why his usul work is studied in the madrasa.
The biography aids in understanding the weight of his opinions in later Hanafi legal theory.

End quote. As for his students: they mentioned that Imam al-Bazdawi dictated, taught, and narrated hadith in Samarqand, and this led him to have many students, but they only mentioned one student among them, and glory to God who counted them all in number. Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to Imam al-Bazdawi, the Hanafi scholar of usul al-fiqh. It opens with his full name and title: 'Shaykh of the Hanafiyya, scholar of Transoxiana, Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn Abd al-Karim al-Bazdawi, the author of the method.' The text then presents praises from several prominent scholars: al-Sam'ani notes his leadership in Transoxiana and his excellent writings; al-Bukhari lauds him in lofty terms; Sadr al-Shari'a calls him the 'leader of the great Imams'; al-Babarti describes his mastery of both transmitted and rational sciences; al-Kafawi emphasizes his comprehensiveness; and al-Ansari praises his title and knowledge. The passage then discusses his teachers and students, noting that his teachers are not named individually, but he came from a scholarly family, and that although he had many students, only one is mentioned by name. This biographical sketch establishes al-Bazdawi's authority and scholarly stature, providing context for his work on usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
البزدوي (al-Bazdawi): Imam Abu al-Hasan Ali ibn Muhammad al-Bazdawi, a leading Hanafi scholar of usul al-fiqh from Transoxiana, author of 'Kanz al-Wusul' (Usul al-Bazdawi).
صاحب الطريقة (Sahib al-Tariqa): The author of the method; referring to al-Bazdawi's distinctive approach in usul al-fiqh.
ما وراء النهر (Ma Wara' al-Nahr): Transoxiana, the region beyond the Oxus River (Central Asia), a major center of Hanafi scholarship.

The Scholarly Standing and Transmission of Imam al-Bazdawi
Biographical account of al-Bazdawi's teachers, students, and scholarly stature

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key biographical details of Imam al-Bazdawi regarding his scholarly recognition and his teachers and students.

Core Idea
Imam al-Bazdawi's teachers are unknown by name, but his scholarly legacy was transmitted through at least one confirmed student.

This passage introduces us to the author of our usul text, Imam al-Bazdawi. Understanding his scholarly standing and the chain of transmission strengthens our appreciation of the work and alerts us to how knowledge is preserved and passed down.

Guided Path
1
Extract the praise
Identify the two scholars who praised al-Bazdawi and note the key phrases they used to describe his stature.
Al-Kafawi called him 'Imam of the world in furu' and usul'; al-Ansari praised him as 'the pride of Islam and Muslims'.
2
Analyze the teacher situation
From the passage, what is known about al-Bazdawi's teachers? Note the biographers' silence and his own practice of transmitting without naming them.
He came from a scholarly family, but no specific names are recorded.
3
Analyze the student situation
Identify the one student explicitly named and consider what this implies about the transmission chain.
Abu al-Ma'ali Muhammad ibn Nasr al-Madini al-Khatib is the only mentioned student.
4
Assess the chain
Reflect on what the lack of named teachers and only one named student means for evaluating the reliability of al-Bazdawi's text.
The chain is thin but not broken; the text itself becomes the primary evidence.

وقال المولى محمود بن سليمان الكفوي، (ت٩٩٠هـ) في: «كتائب أعلام الأخيار من فقهاء مذهب النعمان المختار (۱) : علي بن محمد بن عبد الكريم بن موسى البزدوي الإمام الكبير الجامع بين أشتات العلوم إمام الدنيا في الفروع والأصول». اهـ ووصفه العلامة عبد العلي محمد بن نظام الدين الأنصاري في ديباجة فواتح الرحموت بشرح مُسلم الثبوت بقوله : «الإمام الأجل، والشيخ الأكمل، رئيس الأئمة والعالمين، فخر الإسلام والمسلمين، لَقَبه أغرُّ من الصبح الصادق، واسمه يُخبر عن كل حاذق ذاك الإمام الألمعي: علي البزدوي». اهـ * شيوخه وتلاميذه : لم يذكر مترجمو الإمام البزدوي اسم أحد من شيوخه، إلا أنه أسرة علمية أباً عن جد، والله أعلم بهم، والبزدوي نفسه رحمه الله ينقل في هذا الكتاب عن شيوخه دون ذكر لأسمائهم أو أسماء كتبهم. أما عن تلاميذه: فقد ذكروا أن الإمام البزدوي أملى ودرس وحدث بسمرقند، وهذا يجعل له تلاميذ كُثراً ، ولكن لم يذكروا منهم إلا تلميذاً واحداً، وسبحان من أحصاهم عدداً. (۲) فقد قال الإمام السمعاني عبد الكريم بن محمد : روى لنا عنه (۱) مخطوط ، وينظر الفوائد البهية ص ١٢٤ . (۲) الأنساب ۲۰۱۲ ، سير أعلام النبلاء ٦٠٢/١٨. صاحبه أبو المعالي محمد ابن نصر بن منصور المديني الخطيب(۱) بسمرقند ، ولم يحدثنا عنه سواه. اهـ ***** (۱) له ترجمة في الجواهر المضية ،۳۷۸/۳ ، وذكر أنه كان إماماً، وتفقه على البزدوي علي بن محمد.
And al-Mawlā Mahmūd ibn Sulaymān al-Kafawī (d. 990 AH) said in 'Katā'ib A'lām al-Akhyār min Fuqahā' Madhhab al-Nu'mān al-Mukhtār': 'Alī ibn Muhammad ibn 'Abd al-Karīm ibn Mūsā al-Bazdawī, the great Imām, the unifier of various sciences, the Imām of the world in furū' and usūl.' End quote. And 'Allāmah 'Abd al-'Alī Muhammad ibn Nizām al-Dīn al-Ansārī described him in the preface of Fawātih al-Rahamūt bi-Sharh Muslim al-Thubūt saying: 'The venerable Imām, the most perfect Shaykh, the chief of the imāms and scholars, the pride of Islam and Muslims, his title is brighter than the true dawn, and his name informs about every adept. That perceptive Imām: 'Alī al-Bazdawī.' End quote. * His teachers and students: The biographers of Imām al-Bazdawī did not mention the name of any of his teachers, except that he was from a scholarly family generation after generation, and Allah knows best about them. And al-Bazdawī himself, may Allah have mercy on him, transmits in this book from his teachers without mentioning their names or the names of their books. As for his students: They mentioned that Imām al-Bazdawī dictated, taught, and narrated hadith in Samarqand, and that made him have many students, but they only mentioned one student from among them, and glory be to the One who counted them all. (2) Indeed, Imām al-Sam'ānī 'Abd al-Karīm ibn Muhammad said: 'His companion Abū al-Ma'ālī Muhammad ibn Nasr ibn Mansūr al-Madīnī al-Khatīb (1) narrated to us from him in Samarqand, and no one other than him narrated to us from him.' End quote. ***** (1) His biography is in al-Jawāhir al-Mudīyyah, 3/378, and it mentions that he was an imām and studied fiqh with al-Bazdawī 'Alī ibn Muhammad.
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage is a biographical notice on Imam Ali al-Bazdawi, the author of the usul work we are studying. It begins with two laudatory descriptions: one by Mahmūd al-Kafawī, who calls him the 'Imām of the world in furū' and usūl,' and another by 'Abd al-'Alī al-Ansārī, who extols his rank. The passage then discusses his teachers and students. Notably, the biographers did not record specific names of his teachers, though he came from a scholarly lineage and occasionally references his teachers in this book without naming them. Regarding students, although he taught many in Samarqand, only one student is explicitly mentioned: Abū al-Ma'ālī Muhammad ibn Nasr al-Madīnī al-Khatīb, who narrated from him. This highlights the difficulty of transmitting a scholar's full legacy and the importance of the chain of transmission. The biography is sourced from al-Sam'ānī's al-Ansāb and al-Jawāhir al-Mudīyyah.

Key Terms
البزدوي (al-Bazdawī): Honorific title for Imam Ali ibn Muhammad al-Bazdawi, a renowned Hanafi usul scholar from the 5th century AH.
أبو المعالي محمد بن نصر بن منصور المديني الخطيب (Abū al-Ma'ālī Muhammad ibn Nasr ibn Mansūr al-Madīnī al-Khatīb): The only student of Imam al-Bazdawi explicitly mentioned in this biographical passage; he narrated from al-Bazdawi in Samarqand.
السمعاني (al-Sam'ānī): ‘Abd al-Karīm ibn Muhammad al-Sam'ānī, a scholar who transmitted from Abū al-Ma'ālī and recorded the only known student of al-Bazdawi.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Bazdawi's teachers are not named in biographies, but his student Abu al-Ma'ali transmitted his legacy, underlining the importance of the chain of knowledge and the need to evaluate texts on their own merits.

Biography and Works of Imam al-Bazdawi
Biographical introduction to Imam al-Bazdawi and his writings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key works of Imam al-Bazdawi and explain his significance in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Imam al-Bazdawi authored Usul al-Bazdawi, a cornerstone of Hanafi usul, alongside works in tafsir, hadith, and fiqh.

Before diving into the text of Usul al-Bazdawi, it is essential to know its author and the scholarly weight he carries. This brief biographical passage establishes Imam al-Bazdawi as a prolific scholar whose works were widely praised and whose name became immortalized among Hanafis. Understanding his stature will help you appreciate why his usul work is a primary reference in the school.

Guided Path
1
Introduce the author and his student
The passage begins by mentioning a student of al-Bazdawi, Abu al-Ma'ali, who is the sole narrator from him. This situates al-Bazdawi in a chain of transmission.
This also indicates that some biographical details come only through this student.
2
Survey the range of his works
The text highlights that al-Bazdawi wrote extensively in Quranic exegesis, hadith, fiqh, and usul al-fiqh. Note the emphasis that his works were of high rank and evidence.
This breadth makes him a multi-faceted authority.
3
Identify his most famous work
Among his works, the passage explicitly singles out 'Usul al-Bazdawi' as the most famous, quoting Imam al-Dhahabi's praise.
This is the text you are studying; recognizing its fame underscores its importance.
4
Understand his lasting impact
The passage notes that his name spread especially among Hanafis and that later scholars transmitted his opinions and praised his books.
This explains why his usul work is still relied upon today.

صاحبه أبو المعالي محمد ابن نصر بن منصور المديني الخطيب بسمرقند ، ولم يحدثنا عنه سواه. اهـ
(۱) له ترجمة في الجواهر المضية ،۳۷۸/۳ ، وذكر أنه كان إماماً، وتفقه على البزدوي علي بن محمد.
مصنفات الإمام البزدوي
لقد أكرم الله تعالى الإمام البزدوي بتوفيقه لكتابة مصنفات عديدة، وإملاء أخرى، وكانت كلها عالية القدر والشأن عظيمة الحجة والبرهان لما قصده فيها كبيرة المبنى جليلة المعنى، وذلك في علوم القرآن الكريم وتفسيره والسنة النبوية وشرحها وفروع الفقه وأصوله، وتقعيد وقد شَرَحَ أمهات كتب المذهب، وغير هذا من قواعده وتثبيت اسمـ أسسه، العلوم المتنوعة.
وَكَتَبَ الله له شيوع اسمه في كتب العلم، وتخليد ذكره بين الحنفية خاصة، وبقية المذاهب الفقهية عامة بالنقل عنه، وذكر آرائه، وتناقل الأئمة العلماء كتبه، وأثنوا عليها ثناء بالغاً، وكان من أشهرها: أصول البزدوي. حتى قال الإمام الذهبي عن مؤلفاته: «له التصانيف الجليلة». اهـ
وقال العلامة اللكنوي: له تصانيف كثيرة معتبرة. اهـ
وأذكر فيما يلي ما وقفتُ عليه من ذلك، مقدما ما يتصل بالقرآن الكريم، ثم بالسنة المطهرة، ثم بالفقه والأصول، وهكذا:
١- تفسير القرآن الكريم واسمه كشف الأستار، كما في كشف
His companion Abu al-Ma'ali Muhammad ibn Nasr ibn Mansur al-Madini al-Khatib in Samarqand, and he did not narrate to us from anyone else. End.
(1) He has a biography in al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya, 3/378, where it is mentioned that he was an imam and studied fiqh under al-Bazdawi Ali ibn Muhammad.
Works of Imam al-Bazdawi
Indeed, Allah the Exalted honored Imam al-Bazdawi by granting him success to write numerous works and dictate others. All of them were of high rank and great evidence and proof for the magnitude of their foundation and the nobility of their meaning in the sciences of the Noble Quran and its exegesis, the Prophetic Sunnah and its explanation, the branches of fiqh and its principles, and the establishment of its rules and the consolidation of its foundations, among various sciences.
And Allah decreed that his name spread in books of knowledge and that his memory be immortalized especially among the Hanafis and generally among the other legal schools through transmission from him and mention of his opinions. The leading scholars circulated his books and praised them immensely. Among the most famous of them is Usul al-Bazdawi. Until Imam al-Dhahabi said about his works: 'He has magnificent books.' End.
And Allama al-Laknawi said: He has numerous reliable works. End.
I will mention below what I have come across of that, beginning with what relates to the Noble Quran, then the Purified Sunnah, then fiqh and usul, and so on:
1. Tafsir of the Noble Quran, named Kashf al-Asrar, as in Kashf

The Major Works of Imam al-Bazdawi
Listing Imam al-Bazdawi's works and correcting a bibliographic error.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list at least four major works of Imam al-Bazdawi and identify the common confusion regarding his commentary on al-Ziyadat.

Core Idea
Al-Bazdawi authored a vast tafsir, commentaries on key Hanafi texts, and his famous Usul—but not a commentary on 'Ziyadat al-Ziyadat'.

This passage introduces the scholarly legacy of Imam al-Bazdawi, the author of the foundational Hanafi usul work 'Kanz al-Wusul'. The text lists his major compositions spanning tafsir, hadith, fiqh, and usul, and corrects a persistent bibliographic error. Understanding his oeuvre helps us appreciate the depth of Hanafi scholarship and the transmission of the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his stature
Note that the passage praises al-Bazdawi's works as high in status and proof, covering Quran, Sunnah, fiqh, and usul. His name is immortalized especially among Hanafis.
This establishes why his works are worth studying.
2
List the works in order of priority
The author lists works connected to Quran first, then Sunnah, then fiqh and usul. Write down each title and its subject.
The first work is a tafsir named Kashf al-Asrar in 120 volumes.
3
Identify the common confusion
Some later biographers mistakenly attribute a commentary on 'Ziyadat al-Ziyadat' to al-Bazdawi. The passage clarifies that he only wrote a commentary on 'al-Ziyadat' itself.
Verifying such details is crucial for accurate attribution.
4
Connect to the discipline
Reflect that al-Bazdawi's most famous work is his Usul, which is the subject of this very text. Knowing his other works shows his expertise across Islamic sciences.
This strengthens confidence in his usul methodology.

مصنفات الإمام البزدوي
لقد أكرم الله تعالى الإمام البزدوي بتوفيقه لكتابة مصنفات عديدة، وإملاء أخرى، وكانت كلها عالية القدر والشأن عظيمة الحجة والبرهان لما قصده فيها كبيرة المبنى جليلة المعنى، وذلك في علوم القرآن الكريم وتفسيره والسنة النبوية وشرحها وفروع الفقه وأصوله، وتقعيد قواعده وتثبيت أسسه، وقد شَرَحَ أمهات كتب المذهب، وغير هذا من العلوم المتنوعة.
وَكَتَبَ الله له شيوع اسمه في كتب العلم، وتخليد ذكره بين الحنفية خاصة، وبقية المذاهب الفقهية عامة بالنقل عنه، وذكر آرائه، وتناقل الأئمة العلماء كتبه، وأثنوا عليها ثناء بالغاً، وكان من أشهرها: أصول البزدوي. حتى قال الإمام الذهبي عن مؤلفاته: «له التصانيف الجليلة». اهـ (1)
وقال العلامة اللكنوي (۲) : له تصانيف كثيرة معتبرة. اهـ
وأذكر فيما يلي ما وقفتُ عليه من ذلك، مقدما ما يتصل بالقرآن الكريم، ثم بالسنة المطهرة، ثم بالفقه والأصول، وهكذا:
١- تفسير القرآن الكريم واسمه كشف الأستار، كما في كشف الظنون ١٤٨٥/٢ ، في ۱۲۰ جزءاً، ويقال: إن كل جزء منها في ضخم مصحف، كما في الفوائد البهية ص ١٢٤ مع لفت النظر إلى كبر أحجام المصاحف في ذلك الزمن.
۲- شرح الجامع الصحيح للإمام البخاري، وهو شرح مختصر، كما في كشف الظنون ٥٥٣/١ .
٣- شرح الجامع الكبير، للإمام محمد بن الحسن، ذكره البزدوي نفسه في أصوله، في باب حروف المعاني، وكذلك مترجموه، وأيضاً في كشف الظنون ٥٦٨/١ .
٤- شرح الجامع الصغير للإمام محمد بن الحسن، وقد فرغ من تأليفه في جمادى الآخرة سنة ٤٧٧ هـ ، كما في كشف الظنون ٥٦٣/١ ، وذكره مترجموه، ومنه نسخة في مكتبة أحمد الثالث في اسطنبول، برقم (۳٤۲۳( )١) (1)
٥- شرح الزيادات للإمام محمد كما في كشف الظنون ٩٦٢/٢. وحين ذكر حاجي خليفة كتاب الزيادات وأنه لمحمد بن الحسن، ذكر عَرَضاً أن له: زيادة الزيادات»، ثم قال : وقد شرحها جماعة، وعدَّ منهم قاضي خان، ثم ذكر من شرَّاح الزيادات: البزدوي، وكأن صاحب هدية العارفين ٦٩٣/١ ظن أن الكلام جارٍ على شروح زيادة الزيادات، فعدَّ من كتب البزدوي: شرح زيادة الزيادات والصواب والله أعلم أن البزدوي شَرَحَ الزيادات لا زيادة الزيادات، وقد ذكر البزدوي نفسه شرح الزيادات في أصوله هذا.
Works of Imam al-Bazdawi: Allah Almighty honored Imam al-Bazdawi by granting him success to write numerous works and dictate others, all of which were of high status and great proof and evidence for what he intended, lofty in structure and profound in meaning, covering the sciences of the Noble Qur'an and its interpretation, the Prophetic Sunnah and its commentary, branches of fiqh and its principles, establishing its rules and consolidating its foundations. He commented on the major books of the madhhab, and other diverse sciences. Allah decreed for his name to spread in books of knowledge and his memory to be immortalized among the Hanafis in particular, and the rest of the legal schools in general, through transmission from him and mention of his opinions. The scholarly imams circulated his books and praised them greatly. Among his most famous works is: 'Usul al-Bazdawi'. Imam al-Dhahabi said about his works: 'He has magnificent compositions.' (1) Allamah al-Laknawi (2) said: 'He has many esteemed works.' I will mention what I have come across of that, giving priority to what is connected to the Noble Qur'an, then to the Pure Sunnah, then to fiqh and usul, and so on: 1- Interpretation of the Noble Qur'an, its name is 'Kashf al-Asrar', as in Kashf al-Zunun 2/1485, in 120 parts, and it is said that each part was the size of a large mushaf, as in al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah p. 124, drawing attention to the large size of mus-hafs at that time. 2- Commentary on al-Jami' al-Sahih of Imam al-Bukhari, which is a brief commentary, as in Kashf al-Zunun 1/553. 3- Commentary on al-Jami' al-Kabir of Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, mentioned by al-Bazdawi himself in his Usul, in the chapter on particles, and also by his biographers, and also in Kashf al-Zunun 1/568. 4- Commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir of Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, which he completed in Jumada al-Akhirah 477 AH, as in Kashf al-Zunun 1/563, mentioned by his biographers, and a copy exists in the library of Ahmed III in Istanbul, under number (3423( )1) (1). 5- Commentary on al-Ziyadat of Imam Muhammad, as in Kashf al-Zunun 2/962. When Hajji Khalifah mentioned the book al-Ziyadat and that it was by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, he mentioned incidentally that there is 'Ziyadat al-Ziyadat', then said: 'A group have commented on it', and listed Qadi Khan among them, then mentioned among the commentators of al-Ziyadat: al-Bazdawi. It seems that the author of Hadiyyat al-'Arifin 1/693 thought that the discussion was about commentaries on Ziyadat al-Ziyadat, so he counted among al-Bazdawi's books: 'Sharh Ziyadat al-Ziyadat.' The correct view, and Allah knows best, is that al-Bazdawi commented on al-Ziyadat, not Ziyadat al-Ziyadat. Al-Bazdawi himself mentioned the commentary on al-Ziyadat in his Usul.
Source pages p. 20

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and bibliographic introduction to the works of Imam al-Bazdawi, the author of the foundational Hanafi usul text 'Usul al-Bazdawi' (also known as 'Kanz al-Wusul'). The text opens by praising Allah for enabling al-Bazdawi to produce numerous writings of high quality, covering Qur'anic sciences, hadith, fiqh, and usul. It notes that his works became widely known, especially among Hanafis, and that scholars like al-Dhahabi and al-Laknawi praised his compositions. The author then lists al-Bazdawi's major works in order: first his tafsir 'Kashf al-Asrar' (in 120 volumes, each as large as a mushaf), then his commentary on Sahih al-Bukhari (a brief one), then commentaries on Imam Muhammad's al-Jami' al-Kabir and al-Jami' al-Saghir, and finally his commentary on al-Ziyadat. The text clarifies a common confusion: although some later sources attribute to al-Bazdawi a commentary on 'Ziyadat al-Ziyadat', al-Bazdawi himself only wrote a commentary on 'al-Ziyadat' proper. This is confirmed by the author's own references in his Usul. This passage serves as an orientation for the reader of 'Usul al-Bazdawi', establishing the scholarly stature of the author and the breadth of his contributions.

Key Terms
الزيادات (al-Ziyadat): A work by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, consisting of additions to his earlier fiqh compilations. Al-Bazdawi wrote a commentary on it.
زيادة الزيادات (Ziyadat al-Ziyadat): A later work sometimes confused as a separate commentary by al-Bazdawi, but he did not write it.
كشف الأسرار (Kashf al-Asrar): Al-Bazdawi's tafsir, in 120 volumes, each said to be the size of a large copy of the Quran.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a confirmed work of Imam al-Bazdawi?
A) Sharh Ziyadat al-Ziyadat
B) Kashf al-Asrar
C) al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyyah
D) Sharh al-Jami' al-Sahih of Muslim

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Bazdawi's major works include a massive tafsir, commentaries on key Hanafi texts, and his famous Usul, but not a commentary on 'Ziyadat al-Ziyadat'.

The Scholarly Legacy of al-Bazdawi: A Survey of His Works
Biographical list of works with bibliographic clarifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major works of Fakhral-Islam al-Bazdawi and explain their significance in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Al-Bazdawi's Kanz al-Wusul is the most enduring of his works, but his commentaries on Imam Muhammad's texts shaped Hanafi furu'.

This passage introduces us to the vast intellectual output of Fakhral-Islam al-Bazdawi, a towering figure in Hanafi usul. While his Kanz al-Wusul (Usul al-Bazdawi) is the text we study, his other works reveal the breadth of his scholarship. As a student of usul, knowing the corpus of a great scholar helps you appreciate the tradition he built and the sources he drew upon.

Guided Path
1
List the works mentioned
Scan the passage and extract each work of al-Bazdawi mentioned. Note the subject (usul or furu') and whether it is a commentary (sharh) or an original composition.
There are 11 works listed, plus a note about his brother.
2
Identify the most relevant work for usul
Among the list, identify which work is primarily on usul al-fiqh and is the focus of the current course. This is Kanz al-Wusul ila Ma'rifat al-Usul, also known as Usul al-Bazdawi.
This is the book we are studying now.
3
Examine the pattern of commentaries
Notice that al-Bazdawi wrote commentaries on Imam Muhammad's major works (al-Jami al-Kabir, al-Jami al-Saghir, al-Ziyadat). This shows his role in transmitting and explaining the Hanafi school's primary furu' texts.
These commentaries are part of the Zahir al-Riwayah tradition.
4
Resolve the bibliographic confusion
The passage clarifies that al-Bazdawi wrote Sharh al-Ziyadat, not Sharh Ziyadat al-Ziyadat. Understand the difference: the former is a commentary on al-Ziyadat by Imam Muhammad; the latter would be a commentary on a hypothetical super-commentary. This distinction matters for accurate attribution.
Always verify primary sources before accepting later claims.
5
Consider the broader context
Recognize that al-Bazdawi's works were part of a living tradition. His brother also wrote a smaller usul work. This demonstrates the scholarly environment of the Hanafi school.
Knowing the family and teacher-student networks helps situate the texts.

It seems that the author of Hadiyat al-Arifin 693/1 thought that the discussion was about commentaries of Ziyadat al-Ziyadat, so he counted among al-Bazdawi's books: Sharh Ziyadat al-Ziyadat. The correct view, and Allah knows best, is that al-Bazdawi commented on al-Ziyadat, not Ziyadat al-Ziyadat, and al-Bazdawi himself mentioned Sharh al-Ziyadat in his Usul. Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is a biographical listing of the works of Fakhral-Islam al-Bazdawi, the celebrated Hanafi usul scholar. It enumerates his writings, providing references from standard biographical sources like Kashf al-Dhunnun, al-Fawaid al-Bahiyya, and al-Jawahir al-Madiyya. The list includes commentaries on Imam Muhammad's major texts (al-Jami al-Kabir, al-Jami al-Saghir, al-Ziyadat), a commentary on al-Bukhari, a multi-volume furu' work (al-Mabsut), and his seminal usul work, Kanz al-Wusul, which is the subject of this book. The passage also clarifies a common confusion: al-Bazdawi wrote a commentary on al-Ziyadat, not on Ziyadat al-Ziyadat (a work attributed to Imam Muhammad by some). It ends by noting that al-Bazdawi's brother, Abu al-Yusr, authored a smaller usul work.

Key Terms
كنز الوصول إلى معرفة الأصول (Kanz al-Wusul ila Ma'rifat al-Usul): Al-Bazdawi's own work on usul al-fiqh, also known as Usul al-Bazdawi, which is the text being annotated and studied in this course.
شرح الزيادات (Sharh al-Ziyadat): Al-Bazdawi's commentary on al-Ziyadat by Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, a Hanafi furu' work.
المبسوط (al-Mabsut): Al-Bazdawi's multi-volume work on furu' al-fiqh, spanning eleven volumes.

Al-Bazdawi's most important work for usul is Kanz al-Wusul, but his commentaries on Hanafi furu' texts are also crucial for understanding the school.

Al-Bazdawi and His Key Work Kanz al-Wusul
Biographical and bibliographic listing of al-Bazdawi's works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major works of Imam al-Bazdawi and explain why Kanz al-Wusul is the foundational text for Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Kanz al-Wusul is the core Hanafi usul text by al-Bazdawi, one of many works he authored.

This passage gives a window into the scholarly output of Imam Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi, the author of the text we are studying. Understanding his works helps us appreciate the depth of his contribution and the place of Kanz al-Wusul within the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his death
Note that al-Bazdawi died near Samarkand. His full name and dates are not given but can be inferred as d. 482 AH.
Knowing his death location helps situate his scholarly activity in Central Asia.
2
List the works of al-Bazdawi
From the text, extract all titles: al-Mabsut, Ghina' al-Fuqaha', Kanz al-Wusul, Sharh Taqwim al-Adilla, Sirat al-Madhhab, al-Amali (attributed to him or his relative), and three additional works from manuscripts.
The list shows he wrote on both furu' and usul.
3
Identify the primary usul text
Kanz al-Wusul ila Ma'rifat al-Usul is explicitly called 'the book before us', the main text for this course.
This is the foundational work we are learning.
4
Understand the relationship with his brother's work
His brother Abu al-Yusr wrote a smaller usul text. This shows the family's scholarly legacy.
Comparing sizes: Kanz al-Wusul is larger than his brother's book.
5
Recognize the scholarly chain
Al-Bazdawi wrote a longer usul book (lost) and al-Bukhari commented on it. Later manuscript discoveries add to his corpus.
This highlights the living tradition of commentary and transmission.

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and bibliographic section from the introduction or addenda of the book 'Kanz al-Wusul' by al-Bazdawi. It lists the works of Imam Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi (d. 482 AH) and his brother Abu al-Yusr, including the major work 'Kanz al-Wusul ila Ma'rifat al-Usul' which is the primary text of this course. The editor then adds a quote from Imam 'Ala' al-Din al-Bukhari noting that al-Bazdawi wrote a longer usul book. The editor also lists additional works discovered in manuscripts, such as a commentary on Abu Hanifa's 'al-Fiqh al-Akbar'. Finally, it records the death of al-Bazdawi near Samarkand. This background helps students understand the author's scholarly output and the importance of the text they are studying.

Key Terms
كنز الوصول إلى معرفة الأصول (Kanz al-Wusul ila Ma'rifat al-Usul): The title of al-Bazdawi's major work on usul al-fiqh, meaning 'The Treasure of Arriving at the Knowledge of the Principles'.
