Imam al-Bazdawi: His Life and Works
Biographical summary and works listing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the full name of Imam al-Bazdawi, identify his major works, and recall the date and place of his death.

Core Idea
Imam al-Bazdawi authored Kanz al-Wusul and several other usul works; he died in 482 AH near Samarkand.

Before diving into the text of Kanz al-Wusul, it is essential to know the author behind it. This passage provides a glimpse into Imam al-Bazdawi's scholarly output and his final days. Understanding his biography helps appreciate the authority of his usul work within the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his primary text
Note that the passage is about Imam al-Bazdawi, the author of 'Kanz al-Wusul' (also known as 'Usul al-Bazdawi'), a foundational Hanafi usul text.
His full name is Fakhr al-Islam Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Muhammad al-Bazdawi.
2
List the additional works attributed to him
The passage mentions three other works: Sharh al-Fiqh al-Akbar, al-Muyassar fi al-Kalam, and Zallat al-Qari'. Note the manuscript locations provided.
These are less known but show his breadth.
3
Recall the date and place of death
The text specifies that he died on Thursday, 5 Rajab 482 AH, near Samarkand, and was buried at the door of a mosque in Samarkand.
This date is critical for historical chronology.
4
Reflect on his personal reflection about the grave
Al-Bazdawi wrote poetically about the grave as a garden or pit, indicating his spiritual mindset. This shows the integration of theology in his usul work.
This reflection appears in his usul book.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال الإمام علاء الدين البخاري في مقدمة شرحه لأصول البزدوي «كشف الأسرار»: وقد صنف الشيخ ـ أي البزدوي ـ في أصول الفقه كتاباً أطول من هذا الكتاب ـ أي كنز الوصول ـ وبسط فيه الكلام بسطاً». اهـ
وذكر محقق «الكافي شرح أصول البزدوي، للصغناقي، د/فخر الدین سید محمد قانت ذكر كتباً أخرى للبزدوي، لم أرَ أحداً ذكرها له غيره، وقد اعتمد في ذلك على مخطوطات وقف عليها تُفيد ما ذَكَر، وأنا أوردها هنا؛ احتياطاً:
۱ - شرح الفقه الأكبر، للإمام أبي حنيفة، وذكر أن منه نسخةً خطية في جامعة الملك عبد العزيز بجدة برقم (۱۳۷۹)، و تاریخ نسخها (۱۰۸۲هـ) ، في ٥٦ ورقة .
٢ - الميسر في الكلام، وذكر أن نسخة منه في الجامعة الإسلامية بالمدينة المنورة، برقم (۱۵۱۹) ميكروفيلم في ۱۱۸ ورقة، وكذلك في جامعة الملك سعود بالرياض، برقم (٢٥٧٨).
٣- زلة القارئ، وذكر أن منها نسخة في مكتبة كوبرلي في اسطنبول، برقم ٣ ، وكذلك في دار الكتب القطرية، في قطر، برقم (۸۱۷). وأسأل الله أن يهيئ لكتبه من يحييها، ويخرج كنوزها وفوائدها الغالية.
وفاته :
وهكذا بعد عُمْرٍ طويل عامرٍ بنشر العلم والنفع الخاص والعام كانت وفاة الإمام البزدوي رحمه الله قرب سمرقند وحمل تابوته إليها، ودفن في سمرقند قند على باب المسجد، وذلك يوم الخميس، خامس رجب، سنة ٤٨٢ هـ (١) ، أعلى الله مقامه، وجعله في عليين، مع الذين أنعم عليهم الأنبياء والصديقين والشهداء والصالحين.
ونرجو من الله سبحانه أن يُحقق للإمام البزدوي ما كان يرجوه من ربه جل وعلا، فقد قال رحمه الله وهو يتكلم في هذا الكتاب عن أقسام الأحكام، وأنواع أحكام الآخرة (٢): «لأن القبر للميت : كالرَّحِم للماء، والمهادِ للطفل، وُضِعَ فيه لأحكام الآخرة؛ روضة دار أو حفرة نارٍ، فكان له حكم الأحياء، وذلك كله بعد يمضي عليه في هذا المنزل الابتلاء في الابتداء؛ تنزيهاً لشأنه، ومباهاةً له على أخدانه، وأقرانه، ونرجو الله تعالى أن يُصيّره لنا روضةً بكرمه وفضله». اهـ. اللهم آمين له ولنا ولأحبابنا وللمسلمين أجمعين.
Imam 'Ala' al-Din al-Bukhari said in the introduction to his commentary on Usul al-Bazdawi, 'Kashf al-Asrar': 'Indeed the Shaykh — i.e., al-Bazdawi — authored in Usul al-Fiqh a book longer than this book — i.e., Kanz al-Wusul — and expanded the discussion extensively.' End. And the editor of 'al-Kafi Sharh Usul al-Bazdawi' by al-Sighnaqi, Dr. Fakhr al-Din Sayyid Muhammad Qanit, mentioned other books by al-Bazdawi that I have not seen anyone else mention besides him, and he relied in that on manuscripts he came across that support what he mentioned. I present them here as a precaution: 1. Sharh al-Fiqh al-Akbar of Imam Abu Hanifa; he mentioned that a manuscript copy exists at King Abdulaziz University in Jeddah, no. 1379, copied 1082 AH, 56 folios. 2. al-Muyassar fi al-Kalam; he mentioned a copy at the Islamic University in Medina, no. 1519 microfilm, 118 folios, and also at King Saud University in Riyadh, no. 2578. 3. Zallat al-Qari'; he mentioned a copy in the Koprulu Library in Istanbul, no. 3, and also at the Qatar National Library in Qatar, no. 817. And I ask Allah to prepare for his books one who revives them and brings forth their treasures and precious benefits. His death: Thus after a long life filled with spreading knowledge and private and public benefit, the death of Imam al-Bazdawi, may Allah have mercy on him, occurred near Samarkand; his coffin was carried to it and he was buried in Samarkand at the door of the mosque, on Thursday, the fifth of Rajab, year 482 AH (1). May Allah elevate his rank and place him among the highest, with those whom He has blessed among the prophets, the truthful, the martyrs, and the righteous. And we hope from Allah Almighty to realize for Imam al-Bazdawi what he hoped from his Lord, for he, may Allah have mercy on him, said while speaking in this book about the divisions of rulings and types of rulings of the Hereafter (2): 'Because the grave for the dead is like the womb for water and the cradle for the child; placed therein for the rulings of the Hereafter; if a garden of Paradise or a pit of Hellfire, then it has the ruling of the living. And all that is after he passes through this abode of trial in the beginning; as a purification of his status and a boast to his companions and peers. And we hope from Allah Almighty to make it for us a garden by His generosity and bounty.' End. O Allah, Amen for him and for us and for our loved ones and for all Muslims.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage provides a biographical sketch of Imam al-Bazdawi, the author of the foundational Hanafi usul work 'Kanz al-Wusul'. It begins with a quote from Imam 'Ala' al-Din al-Bukhari's commentary, indicating that al-Bazdawi wrote a longer usul work besides the present one. The editor then lists three other works attributed to al-Bazdawi (Sharh al-Fiqh al-Akbar, al-Muyassar fi al-Kalam, and Zallat al-Qari'), with manuscript locations. The passage concludes with details of al-Bazdawi's death in 482 AH near Samarkand, and a personal reflection from al-Bazdawi about the grave as either a garden of Paradise or a pit of Hellfire, reflecting the Hanafi emphasis on the afterlife. The biography serves as a front matter, establishing the author's scholarly credibility and works.

Key Terms
البزدوي (al-Bazdawi): Imam Fakhr al-Islam Abu al-Hasan 'Ali ibn Muhammad al-Bazdawi, the author of 'Kanz al-Wusul', a foundational Hanafi usul text.
كنز الوصول (Kanz al-Wusul): The primary work of al-Bazdawi on usul al-fiqh, also known as 'Usul al-Bazdawi'.
شرح الفقه الأكبر (Sharh al-Fiqh al-Akbar): Al-Bazdawi's commentary on Abu Hanifa's creedal work 'al-Fiqh al-Akbar'.
الميسر في الكلام (al-Muyassar fi al-Kalam): A work by al-Bazdawi on theology (kalam), meaning 'The Easy [Work] on Kalam'.
زلة القارئ (Zallat al-Qari'): A work by al-Bazdawi on mistakes made by Qur'an reciters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Bazdawi, author of Kanz al-Wusul, died in 482 AH near Samarkand, leaving a legacy of multiple works spanning usul, theology, and Qur'anic recitation.

Imam al-Bazdawi's Death and His Grave Analogy
Biographical note with death date and author's analogy

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state Imam al-Bazdawi's death date and explain his analogy of the grave as the first station of the Hereafter in the context of his usul work.

Core Idea
The grave is the first abode of the Hereafter, determining one's final state—not merely a place of decay.

This brief passage from the editor's introduction records the death of Imam al-Bazdawi and includes a striking analogy from his own writings. Though biographical, the analogy ties directly to the usul discussion of akham (rulings) and the states of the Hereafter. Understanding this connection deepens our appreciation of how the imam viewed the grave as a decisive station.

Guided Path
1
Locate the date and details
Identify the death date (482 AH, 5th Rajab, Thursday) and location (near Samarqand mosque). This establishes the historical context of the author.
The phrase 'Samarqand قند' may be a textual corruption; the intended location is likely near a mosque in Samarqand.
2
Parse the analogy
Read the quote: 'the grave for the deceased is like the womb for water and the cradle for the child.' Break down each comparison—womb protects and nurtures the fetus, cradle prepares the infant for growth, so the grave houses the deceased for the Hereafter.
3
Connect to rulings of the Hereafter
Note that the grave determines 'a garden of Paradise or a pit of Hellfire.' This shows that the deceased is still subject to reward/punishment—hence 'rulings of the Hereafter' apply even in the grave.
4
Reflect on the supplication
The editor prays for the imam and all believers. Recognize the adab (etiquette) of honoring scholars by praying for them after mentioning their death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سمرقند قند على باب المسجد، وذلك يوم الخميس، خامس رجب، سنة ٤٨٢ هـ ، أعلى الله مقامه، وجعله في عليين، مع الذين أنعم عليهم الأنبياء والصديقين والشهداء والصالحين. من ونرجو من الله سبحانه أن يُحقق للإمام البزدوي ما كان يرجوه من ربه جل وعلا، فقد قال رحمه الله وهو يتكلم في هذا الكتاب عن أقسام الأحكام، وأنواع أحكام الآخرة : ما و لأن القبر للميت : كالرَّحِم للماء، والمهادِ للطفل، وُضِعَ فيه لأحكام الآخرة ؛ روضة دار أو حفرة نارٍ، فكان له حكم الأحياء، وذلك كله بعد يمضي عليه في هذا المنزل الابتلاء في الابتداء؛ تنزيهاً لشأنه، ومباهاةً له على أخدانه ،وأقرانه، ونرجو الله تعالى أن يُصيّره لنا روضةً بكرمه وفضله. اهـ. اللهم آمين له ولنا ولأحبابنا وللمسلمين أجمعين. (۱) الجواهر المضية ٥٩٤/٢ ، وغيره. (٢) ص ٧٤٠ .
Samarqand [؟] at the door of the mosque, on Thursday, the fifth of Rajab, year 482 AH. May Allah elevate his station and place him in the highest ranks, with those whom He has blessed among the prophets, the truthful, the martyrs, and the righteous. We ask Allah the Exalted to realize for Imam al-Bazdawi what he hoped from his Lord, for he, may Allah have mercy on him, said while speaking in this book about the divisions of rulings and types of rulings of the Hereafter: 'Because the grave for the deceased is like the womb for water and the cradle for the child; it is placed [in] the rulings of the Hereafter: either a garden of Paradise or a pit of Hellfire. So it has the ruling of the living, all that after he passes through this abode of trial in the beginning; to honor his status and to boast over his close friends and peers. We ask Allah the Exalted to make it a garden for us by His generosity and grace.' End. O Allah, grant this to him, to us, to our loved ones, and to all Muslims. (1) Al-Jawahir al-Mudi'ah 2/594, etc. (2) p. 740.
Source pages p. 24

Commentary
This passage is a biographical note recording the death date of Imam al-Bazdawi (482 AH) and a prayer for him. It then quotes his own words from this very book where he discusses the different types of rulings. The quote uses a powerful analogy: the grave is to the deceased as the womb is to water (i.e., the fetus) and the cradle is to the infant. The grave determines one's abode in the Hereafter—either a garden of Paradise or a pit of Hellfire. Thus, the deceased still has a kind of 'ruling of the living' in terms of being subject to reward or punishment. The author ends with a supplication. This material is from the editor of the text, providing contextual information about the author.

Key Terms
قبر (qabr): Grave; the first abode in the Hereafter according to the analogy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Like a prison cell
B) Like a womb for water and a cradle for a child
C) Like a house with rooms
D) Like a dark well

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Bazdawi's grave analogy teaches that the grave is the first station of the Hereafter, deserving of legal attention in usul al-fiqh.

Major Commentaries on Usul al-Bazdawi
Listing of commentaries on Usul al-Bazdawi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major commentaries on Usul al-Bazdawi, their authors, and distinguish between printed and manuscript works.

Core Idea
Usul al-Bazdawi's commentaries are essential references for Hanafi usul.

This passage lists the key commentaries written on Usul al-Bazdawi, a foundational text in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author, who is a later Hanafi scholar, provides a list arranged by death date, highlighting the importance of each commentary. Understanding this list helps you navigate the vast commentary tradition and locate the most authoritative explanations.

Guided Path
1
Understand the List's Purpose
The author lists commentaries to guide students to the most important works. Notice he arranges by death date and prioritizes printed ones.
2
Identify the Three Major Printed Commentaries
Focus on al-Kafi, Kashf al-Asrar (the greatest), and al-Taqrir. They are printed and verified.
3
Note Other Printed/Manuscript Works
Al-Shamil is the largest but unprinted; al-Shafi is verified at Medina. The rest are lesser-known or glosses.
4
Recognize the Importance of Personal Research
The author mentions he could not find volume one of al-Shamil, showing the need for diligent research.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
شَرَحَ أصول البزدوي جماعةٌ من كبار الأئمة الأعلام ، وأولوه خدمةً عظيمة من التوضيح والبيان لدقة ،ألفاظه وخفاء معانيه ؛ ليُخرجوا لطلبة العلم مكنون عباراته، ويكشفوا لهم أسرار رموزه وألفاظه، ويزيدوا على شأنه نوره نوراً، وما ذاك إلا لعظيم مكانته عندهم، ونفاسته ورفعة كتب أصول الحنفية، وأذكر فيما يلي ما وقفتُ عليه من ذلك، مقدماً ذكر المطبوع منها، ومرتباً لها بحسب أسبقية وفاة صاحبها:

١- شرح الإمام حسام الدين حسين بن علي الصغناقي الحنفي ت ٧١٤هـ)، وسماه: «الكافي»، وذكر في آخره: أنه فرغ من تأليفه في أواخر جمادى الأولى سنة ٧٠٤هـ ، وهو مطبوع محقق في خمس مجلدات.

۲- شرح الإمام علاء الدين البخاري عبد العزيز بن ت۷۳۰هـ)، وسماه «كشف الأسرار وشَرْحُه هذا هو أعظم الشروح، وأكثرها إفادةً وبياناً، كما في كشف الظنون ۱۱۲/۱، وهو مطبوع في أربع مجلدات كبار، بصفحات مرصوصة طباعياً، وهو محتاج بشدة إلى خدمة علمية وطباعية.

٣- شرح الإمام أكمل الدين محمد بن محمود البابرتي الحنفي (ت ٧٨٦هـ) ، وسماه : «التقرير » ، وهو مطبوع محقق في ثماني مجلدات.

٤- شرح الإمام أبي المكارم أحمد بن حسن الجار بردي الشافعي (٧٤٦هـ).

٥- شرح الإمام قوام الدين الكاكي ت٧٤٩هـ)، وسماه «بنيان الوصول»، وله عدة نسخ خطية، ذكرها محقق الكافي ٣٢/١ .

٦- شرح الإمام جلال الدين الخوارزمي الكرلاني (ت٧٦٧هـ)، صاحب الكفاية شرح الهداية، وسماه الشافي»، وقد حقق في الجامعة الإسلامية بالمدينة المنورة، كما ذكر هذا محقق الكافي ٣٢/١.

٧- شرح الإمام الأترازي أمير كاتب الإتقاني، (ت٧٥١هـ)، وسماه: الشامل»، وهو أكبر كتاب في أصول الفقه، حيث جاء مخطوطاً في عشر ،مجلدات وقد مُلئ أصولاً وفقها وفروعاً وأدلة ، وحقق غالبه في رسائل جامعية في جامعة الإمام محمد بن سعود في الرياض، ولم يُطبع. ولم أقف على المجلد الأول منه بعد بحث ومتابعة؛ لأنقل مقدمة مؤلفه، وأثبت ما أثنى به على أصول البزدوي.

- شرح الإمام أبي البقاء محمد بن أحمد بن الضياء المكي الحنفي، (ت ٨٥٤هـ ) .

۹ شرح الإمام عمر بن عبد المحسن الأرزنجاني (كان حياً سنة ۸۷۱هـ)، في مجلدين.

۱۰- ومن التعليقات المختصرة عليه : تعليقة الإمام حميد الدين علي بن محمد الضرير الحنفي، (ت٦٦٦هـ).

١١- وكذلك تعليقة لجلال الدین رسولا أحمد بن التباني الحنفي، (ت ۷۱۳ هـ).
A group of great leading imams explained Usul al-Bazdawi and devoted great service to it in clarification and elucidation due to the precision of its expressions and the hiddenness of its meanings, so that they might bring out for students of knowledge the hidden content of its phrases, and uncover for them the secrets of its symbols and expressions, and add light upon its light. That is only due to its great status with them, its preciousness and the high rank of the Hanafi usul books. I mention below what I have come across of that, giving priority to the printed ones, and arranging them according to the precedence of the death date of their author:

1. The commentary of Imam Husam al-Din Husayn ibn Ali al-Sighnaqi al-Hanafi (d. 714 AH), titled 'al-Kafi'. He mentioned at its end that he finished writing it in late Jumada al-Ula 704 AH. It is printed and verified in five volumes.

2. The commentary of Imam Ala al-Din al-Bukhari Abd al-Aziz (d. 730 AH), titled 'Kashf al-Asrar'. This commentary is the greatest of the commentaries and the most beneficial and clarifying, as in Kashf al-Zunun 1/112. It is printed in four large volumes with typeset compressed pages, and it is in severe need of academic and typographical service.

3. The commentary of Imam Akmal al-Din Muhammad ibn Mahmud al-Babarti al-Hanafi (d. 786 AH), titled 'al-Taqrir'. It is printed and verified in eight volumes.

4. The commentary of Imam Abi al-Makarim Ahmad ibn Hasan al-Jarbardi al-Shafi'i (d. 746 AH).

5. The commentary of Imam Qiwam al-Din al-Kaki (d. 749 AH), titled 'Binyan al-Wusul'. It has several manuscript copies mentioned by the verifier of al-Kafi 1/32.

6. The commentary of Imam Jalal al-Din al-Khwarizmi al-Karlani (d. 767 AH), author of al-Kifaya sharh al-Hidaya, titled 'al-Shafi'. It has been verified at the Islamic University in Medina, as mentioned by the verifier of al-Kafi 1/32.

7. The commentary of Imam al-Itrazi Amir Katib al-Itqani (d. 751 AH), titled 'al-Shamil'. It is the largest book in usul al-fiqh, as its manuscript comes in ten volumes. It is filled with usul, fiqh, branches, and evidences. Most of it has been verified in university theses at Imam Muhammad bin Saud University in Riyadh, but it has not been printed. I have not come across the first volume after research and follow-up in order to quote its author's introduction and record his praise for Usul al-Bazdawi.

8. The commentary of Imam Abi al-Baqa Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn al-Diya al-Makki al-Hanafi (d. 854 AH).

9. The commentary of Imam Umar ibn Abd al-Muhsin al-Arzinjani (alive in 871 AH), in two volumes.

10. Among the short glosses on it: the gloss of Imam Hamid al-Din Ali ibn Muhammad al-Darir al-Hanafi (d. 666 AH).

11. Also a gloss by Jalal al-Din Rasul Ahmad ibn al-Tabbani al-Hanafi (d. 713 AH).
Source pages p. 27

Commentary
This passage is a biographical listing of commentaries on the famous Hanafi usul work, Usul al-Bazdawi. The author begins by praising the work and the scholars who wrote commentaries on it, then proceeds to list eleven commentaries, some printed and some in manuscript. The list is arranged in order of the commentator's death date. The first three are described as printed and verified: al-Kafi, Kashf al-Asrar (the greatest), and al-Taqrir. The fourth and fifth are mentioned briefly. The sixth is al-Shafi, verified in Medina. The seventh is al-Shamil, the largest usul book but still unprinted. The eighth and ninth are mentioned without further detail. Finally, two short glosses are listed: one by al-Darir and one by al-Tabbani. The passage serves as a valuable reference for students of Hanafi usul who wish to identify the major commentaries on al-Bazdawi.

Key Terms
شرح (sharh): A commentary that expounds upon a foundational text (matn) by explaining its meanings and providing evidence.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Usul al-Bazdawi has been extensively commented, with three key printed works: al-Kafi, Kashf al-Asrar, and al-Taqrir.

Commentary Tradition of Usul al-Bazdawi
Bibliographic listing of works on Usul al-Bazdawi

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify key commentaries and scholarly works on Usul al-Bazdawi and explain their significance in the Hanafi usul tradition.

Core Idea
Usul al-Bazdawi attracted generations of Hanafi scholars who wrote commentaries, glosses, and takhrij works, enriching its transmission and understanding.

This passage introduces you to the rich scholarly tradition surrounding al-Bazdawi's foundational usul text. Rather than a single ruling or argument, it catalogs commentaries (shuruh), glosses (ta'liqat), and a takhrij work that together shaped how the text was studied and transmitted. Understanding this tradition helps you appreciate the dynamic nature of Hanafi usul scholarship and the importance of manuscript sources for critical editions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories of works listed
The passage mentions incomplete commentaries, complete commentaries, and manuscript glosses/notes. Distinguish between them and note any author names and dates.
Incomplete commentaries are those that cover only part of the base text.
2
Analyze the significance of manuscript glosses
The author emphasizes the value of marginalia written by scribes and owners. Consider how these glosses can aid in textual criticism and understanding historical interpretations.
Example: Khalil al-Rumi's gloss from 800 AH includes corrections and annotations.
3
Understand the role of takhrij
The passage highlights Qasim ibn Qutlubugha's takhrij, which traces and verifies hadiths cited in the text. Reflect on why such a work is important for usul al-fiqh.
Takhrij strengthens the evidentiary basis of the text.
4
Synthesize the scholarly engagement
Consider how these diverse works (commentaries, glosses, takhrij) collectively enhanced the study and transmission of Usul al-Bazdawi over centuries.
This reflects a live academic tradition, not a static text.

وعلى سبيل المثال: ما جاء في آخر نسخة سنة ٨٠٠هـ: والحمد لله على التمام، وعلى رسوله محمد أفضل الصلاة والسلام، كتبه وقَرَأه وصححه وحشاه العبد الفقير الحقير إلى رحمة ربه ومولاه: خليل الرومي البافي سنة ثمانمائة، الحمد لله الذي أمهلني على إتمامه، وسلم تسليماً كثيراً». اهـ
وهذا الأمر يحتاج لبال طويل ودقة وتأمل حتى يتم تفريغ تلك الحواشي المخطوطة التي كُتبت طولاً وعرضاً وبين السطور، مما ازدحمت به أطراف النسخ الخطية، وامتلأت بها.

12- Among the incomplete commentaries: the commentary of Imam ‘Ala’ al-Din ‘Ali ibn Muhammad, known as Musannifak (d. 775 AH), and he named it 'al-Tahrir'. 13- The commentary of Imam Shams al-Din Muhammad ibn Hamza al-Fanari (834 AH), which covers only its preface. 14- The commentary of Imam al-Mawla Muhammad ibn Framuz, known as Mulla Khusraw (d. 885 AH); had it been completed, seekers of guidance would have attained their goal through it. 15- A commentary by Mahmud ibn Muhammad al-Jawnpuri al-Faruqi al-Hindi (1062 AH), mentioned by the editor of al-Kafi by al-Sighnaqi 1/31. 16- A commentary by Sulayman ibn Ahmad al-Sindi, mentioned by the editor of al-Kafi, and a copy of it is preserved in the Egyptian National Library under number (Kh 69, ‘A 2063). 17- Among its commentaries are al-Muwaddih and al-Shafi, as in a gloss on Kashf al-Zunun 1/113. 18- Also, we can count among its commentaries and glosses: what the scribes and owners of the manuscript copies of Usul al-Bazdawi wrote in their margins and between the lines of its text, of which I have samples that I relied upon in editing the text; for through those copies many glosses on the book can be obtained, as well as many benefits and notes that one does not find elsewhere. For example, what appears at the end of a copy from the year 800 AH: 'And praise be to God for completion, and upon His Messenger Muhammad the best of prayers and peace. Written, read, corrected, and glossed by the poor and lowly servant, hoping for the mercy of his Lord and Master: Khalil al-Rumi al-Bafi, in the year eight hundred. Praise be to God who granted me respite to complete it, and peace be abundant.' End quote. This task requires great attention, precision, and contemplation to transcribe those manuscript glosses that were written lengthwise, crosswise, and between the lines, such that the margins of the manuscript copies are crowded and filled with them. Among the scholarly works based on Usul al-Bazdawi is what Imam Qasim ibn Qutlubugha al-Hanafi (d. 879 AH) wrote: a takhrij of its hadiths, and that is the book in our hands, and he included in it some precise corrections and useful remarks on the book.
Source pages p. 29

Commentary
This passage is a bibliographic survey enumerating various commentaries, glosses, and related works on al-Bazdawi's 'Usul al-Bazdawi', a foundational text in Hanafi usul al-fiqh. The author lists incomplete commentaries (nos. 12-14), complete ones (nos. 15-17), and notes the value of marginalia found in manuscript copies (no. 18). He also highlights the work of Qasim ibn Qutlubugha who wrote a takhrij (verification of hadith references) for the book. The list demonstrates the rich scholarly engagement with al-Bazdawi's text over centuries, from the 8th to the 11th century AH. The passage reflects the typical scholarly practice of producing commentaries (shuruh) and glosses (hawayish) to explain, expand, and correct the base text. The mention of manuscript glosses underscores the importance of these witnesses for critical editions.

Key Terms
شرح (sharh): A commentary explaining the base text of Usul al-Bazdawi
تعليقة (ta'liqa): A gloss or marginal note added to a manuscript
تخريج (takhrij): Tracing and verifying the sources of hadiths cited in the book

The extensive commentary tradition on Usul al-Bazdawi demonstrates the ongoing Hanafi scholarly effort to preserve, explain, and critique foundational usul texts.

Life of the Author

The Significance of Usul al-Bazdawi in Hanafi Usul al-Fiqh
Scholarly endorsements and description of author's methodology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key scholars who praised Usul al-Bazdawi and explain why it is considered a foundational text in Hanafi Usul al-Fiqh.

Core Idea
Usul al-Bazdawi is the standard reference for Hanafi Usul, praised for its depth despite its difficulty.

This lesson introduces you to the esteemed status of Imam al-Bazdawi's 'Usul al-Bazdawi' within the Hanafi school. By examining endorsements from major scholars like Ibn Khaldun and al-Laknawi, you will understand why this text remains central. We also explore the author's methodology, including his reliance on Zahir al-Riwaya and his openness to revising his own positions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key scholars quoted
Find the names of scholars who praised the book: Ibn Khaldun, al-Laknawi, and the author of Kashf al-Zunun. Also note the quote from Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Shaw'an.
2
Understand the nature of the endorsements
Each scholar highlights different strengths: Ibn Khaldun calls it the best Hanafi usul work; al-Laknawi calls it reliable; Kashf al-Zunun emphasizes its depth and difficulty.
3
Analyze al-Bazdawi's methodology
Note that he rarely cites sources, but when he does, he uses Zahir al-Riwaya and al-Muntaqa. He also engages with other scholars' views and was not afraid to change his positions.
4
Connect the book's significance to your own study
Recognize that Usul al-Bazdawi is a foundational text; many later commentaries and fatwas rely on its framework. Understanding its authority helps in evaluating arguments in Hanafi usul.

مَن عَرَفَ الكشاف للزمخشري ، وأصول البزدوي الكبير : عَرَفَ العلوم كلها، وكان رحمه الله له بهما معرفة تامة وكثيراً ما يدرسهما، ويَحلَّ مشكلاتهما، وكان أولاً تُشكل عليه مسائل في البزدوي، ثم بعد مدة ظهر له ذلك، واتضح له اتضاحاً بيناً». اهـ ما كان يُشكل عليه من جميع
وقال عنه صاحب كشف الظنون (ت ١٠٦٧هـ) ١/١١٢: وهو كتاب عظيم الشأن جليل البرهان، محتو على لطائف الاعتبارات بأوجز العبارات تأبى مرامه واستعصى على العلماء زمامه ، قد انغلقت ألفاظه، وخفيت رموزه وألحاظه ، فقام جمع من الفحول بأعباء ضيحه، وكشف خبيَّاته وتلميحه». اهـ
وقال الإمام اللكنوي (ت ١٣٠٤هـ) في الفوائد البهية» ص ١٢٤ : ) أصول البزدوي كتاب كبير ... معتبر معتمد». اهـ
هذا، وأما عن مصادر البزدوي في أصوله فالغالب على المؤلف أنه منشي لنص ألفاظه وعباراته، دون عزو لكتاب من كتب سابقيه إلا نادراً، ومما صرح بالنقل عن كتب ظاهر الرواية، للإمام محمد بن الحسن، والمنتقى للحاكم الشهيد، كما ينقل عن مشايخه دون ذكر لأسمائهم أو أسماء كتبهم. وكان ينقل آراء الإمام عيسى بن أبان والكرخي، والجصاص، ويتتبع أقوال الإمام الشافعي وينقلها ويناقشها كل ذلك دون تسمية لكتاب من كتب هؤلاء الأئمة الذين نقل عنهم.
ومن منهج الإمام البزدوي : أنه كان يُصرح بتغير آرائه واجتهاداته إن حصل له ذلك، كمسألة وجوب الأحكام على الصبي، ص ۰۷۱۳
The difficulty, its words have become closed, its symbols and hints hidden, and it contains from the principles secrets for which there is no revealer besides Allah, and it blazes in the branches with the lights of moons for which there is no eclipser in Allah's law. The difficulty. So see how these two scholars - meaning his teacher and his teacher's teacher - informed about the students' maturity from this book, and the students' stumbling in its arena. So I set out working for Allah, relying on Allah, seeking help from Allah in editing what I attempt and establishing what I discuss from authoring a concise commentary whose conciseness does not omit, and whose completion is achieved in the shortest time, revealing its hidden aspects, informing about its secrets, clarifying its implications, and specifying its innermost meanings. And I undertook to restrict its broad points, release its evidences, spread its benefits, and string its necklaces. And I named it 'Al-Taqrir li-Usul Fakhr al-Islam', and I asked Allah to benefit with it as He benefited with its original the students of Islam. End quote. And the scholar al-Qadi Ibn Khaldun (d. 808 AH) said in his Muqaddimah 2/226: 'As for the Usul of the Hanafis, they wrote much about it... and the best writing of the later ones in it is the composition of Sayf al-Islam al-Bazdawi, one of their imams, and it is comprehensive.' End quote. I say: thus Sayf al-Islam, and his fame is as Fakhr al-Islam, and the professor of professors in verification, the great professor Dr. Ibrahim Shabbuh, may Allah preserve him, kindly and rewardedly informed me in a phone call with him in Tunis that the four manuscripts he relied on in his verification of Ibn Khaldun are thus: Sayf al-Islam. And it came in the biography of the scholar Shaykh Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Shaw'an (d. 822 AH), student of al-Haddad author of al-Jawhara al-Nayyira, that he used to say: 'Whoever knows al-Kashshaf of al-Zamakhshari, and al-Usul al-Bazdawi al-Kabir, knows all the sciences.' And he had complete knowledge of both, and often studied them and solved their difficulties. At first some issues in al-Bazdawi were problematic for him, but later they became clear and manifestly evident to him. End quote. And the author of Kashf al-Zunun (d. 1067 AH) said about it 1/112: 'It is a book of great significance, magnificent proof, containing subtle considerations with the briefest expressions; its goal is inaccessible and its reins have been difficult for scholars; its words have closed and its symbols and hints hidden; so a group of eminent scholars undertook the burden of clarifying it and uncovering its hidden aspects and allusions.' End quote. And Imam al-Laknawi (d. 1304 AH) said in al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya p. 124: 'Usul al-Bazdawi is a great book... reliable and authoritative.' End quote. As for the sources of al-Bazdawi in his Usul, the author mostly composes the text of his words and expressions without attributing to previous books except rarely. He explicitly cites from the books of Zahir al-Riwaya of Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, and al-Muntaqa of al-Hakim al-Shahid. He also transmits from his teachers without mentioning their names or their books. He transmits the opinions of Imam 'Isa ibn Aban, al-Karkhi, and al-Jassas, and follows the statements of Imam al-Shafi'i, transmitting and discussing them, all without naming any book of those imams from whom he transmitted. And from the method of Imam al-Bazdawi: he would explicitly state changes in his opinions and ijtihadat if that occurred, such as the issue of the obligation of rulings upon a child, p. 713.
Source pages p. 33

Commentary
This passage is a collection of scholarly endorsements and a description of the book 'Usul al-Bazdawi'. It begins with a quote from the author himself about the difficulty of the original text, explaining that he wrote a commentary called 'Al-Taqrir li-Usul Fakhr al-Islam' to make it accessible. The author then quotes Ibn Khaldun, who praises al-Bazdawi's work as the best Hanafi usul text. The phrase 'Sayf al-Islam' is clarified as 'Fakhr al-Islam', the author's title. Next, a quote from Muhammad ibn Muhammad ibn Shaw'an states that knowledge of al-Bazdawi's usul and al-Zamakhshari's tafsir encompasses all sciences. Kashf al-Zunun praises the book's depth and difficulty, and al-Laknawi calls it reliable. The passage also describes al-Bazdawi's methodology: he rarely cites sources, but when he does, it is from Zahir al-Riwaya works of Imam Muhammad and al-Muntaqa. He also transmits from earlier Hanafi scholars like 'Isa ibn Aban, al-Karkhi, and al-Jassas, and engages with al-Shafi'i's views. Al-Bazdawi was not rigid; he openly changed his opinions when convinced, such as on the obligation of rulings for minors. This front matter establishes the book's authority and the author's scholarly standing.

Key Terms
فخر الإسلام (Fakhr al-Islam): Title of Imam al-Bazdawi, meaning 'Pride of Islam', used interchangeably with Sayf al-Islam 'Sword of Islam'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Usul al-Bazdawi is a masterwork of Hanafi usul, praised by Ibn Khaldun, al-Laknawi, and others; its depth and the author's rigorous methodology make it a foundational text.

The Merits and Methodology of al-Bazdawi's Usul al-Fiqh
Describing the features and significance of al-Bazdawi's Usul al-Fiqh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the key features of al-Bazdawi's Usul al-Fiqh and explain why its difficulty is a deliberate pedagogical feature to safeguard ijtihad for qualified scholars.

Core Idea
Al-Bazdawi's Usul al-Fiqh intentionally challenges readers to preserve ijtihad for the qualified.

Imam al-Bazdawi's work on usul al-fiqh is a cornerstone of the Hanafi school. This passage highlights its unique features: the author's reliance on core Hanafi sources and his deliberate choice of difficulty to prevent unqualified individuals from undertaking ijtihad. Understanding these features helps us appreciate the rigor required in usul studies and the respect owed to the classical masters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's sources and methodology
Examine how al-Bazdawi cites Zahir al-Riwayah, Nawadir, and earlier scholars, often anonymously ('One of our teachers said'). Note his concern with refuting the Mu'tazila.
This shows his reliance on the authoritative transmission of the school and his polemical focus.
2
Recognize the deliberate difficulty
The passage states that the book's difficulty is intentional—to ensure only those worthy of deriving rulings engage with it, weeding out pretenders.
This is a key pedagogical choice, not a flaw.
3
Understand its status within the Hanafi school
The book is described as a foundational work ('عمدة') respected by both early and later scholars.
Its high status underscores its importance in Hanafi usul.
4
Reflect on the warning against unqualified ijtihad
The passage warns against the ease with which some attempt ijtihad and tarjih, emphasizing proper training.
This reinforces the need for structured study under qualified teachers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويذهب إليه كالإمام محمد بن الحسن في كتبه ظاهر الرواية والنوادر، وينقل عن الإمام الحاكم الشهيد في المنتقى، وكذلك عن الإمام الكرخي والجصاص، وغيرهم، كما ينقل كثيراً عن مشايخه دون أن يسميهم، فيقول : قال بعض مشايخنا. يهتم بالرد على المعتزلة وأصولهم التي بنوا عليها مذهبهم. وبعد هذا كله وقبلَه : فهو كتاب عمدة عند السادة الحنفية، معتبر عند المتقدمين والمتأخرين من أئمة علماء أصول الفقه. يمتاز هذا الكتاب بأنه كتاب تراثي قديم عال، مبارك رفيع، لأستاذ أئمة السلف، ولإمام كبير من أئمة الدنيا في الفروع والأصول، وعليه فالعيش مع هؤلاء الكبار العظام يُنتج كباراً ، ودراسة مثل هذه المصنفات العالية، والدخول في أنوارها وبركاتها تولد همةً ونشاطاً، وتُورث بركةً وخيراً كبيراً. إذا ما علا المرء رام العُلا ويقنع بالدُّونَ مَن كان دُونا ولعل من مزايا هذا الكتاب صعوبة فهمه وتعسّر إدراك محتواه، وذلك حتى لا يستطيع الإقبال على علم قواعد استنباط الأحكام إلا من كان أهلاً لذلك، وحتى يخرج بذلك الأدعياء، ويعرف كل حده ليقف عنده، فالأمر ليس بهذه السهولة التي يُصوِّرها البعض للقيام بالاجتهاد والترجيح بين أقوال كبار الأئمة، فضلاً عن العمل، والتي جرأت الكثير للدخول في ذلك وهم لا يفقهون حديثاً، والله المستعان.
He follows it, like Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan in his books of Zahir al-Riwayah and al-Nawadir, and he transmits from Imam al-Hakim al-Shahid in al-Muntaqa, and also from Imam al-Karkhi and al-Jassas, and others, and he frequently transmits from his teachers without naming them, saying: 'One of our teachers said.' He is concerned with refuting the Mu'tazila and their principles upon which they built their madhhab. After all this and before: it is a major book according to the Hanafi masters, respected by the earlier and later imams of usul al-fiqh scholars. This book is distinguished as a high, blessed, and sublime ancient heritage book, by the master of the imams of the Salaf, and by a great imam among the imams of the world in furu' and usul. Therefore, living with these great ones produces greatness, and studying such high compositions and entering into their lights and blessings generates aspiration and activity, and bequeaths blessing and great good. When a person becomes high, he aims high, and the low one is content with lowliness. Perhaps among the merits of this book is its difficulty of understanding and the struggle to grasp its content, so that no one can engage in the knowledge of the rules of deriving rulings except one who is worthy of it, and thereby the pretenders are weeded out, and everyone knows their limit to stop at it. The matter is not as easy as some portray for carrying out ijtihad and tarjih among the statements of great imams, let alone action; this has emboldened many to enter into it while they understand not a hadith. And Allah is the source of help.
Source pages p. 36

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and evaluative description of Imam al-Bazdawi's usul work. It first describes the author's methodology: he follows the views of Imam Muhammad and others, referencing books of Zahir al-Riwayah and Nawadir, and often cites earlier scholars without naming them. He also refutes Mu'tazila principles. Then it praises the book as a foundational text for Hanafis, respected by all. The book is described as difficult to understand, intentionally, to prevent unqualified individuals from attempting ijtihad. The commentary notes the emphasis on the high caliber of the work and the importance of proper qualification in usul al-fiqh.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, etc.) which represent the transmitted basis of the Hanafi school.
النوادر (al-Nawadir): Rare transmissions from the Imams, not part of the six core books, often transmitted by Hasan ibn Ziyad and others.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Al-Bazdawi's Usul al-Fiqh intentionally demands rigorous study to preserve the integrity of ijtihad and prevent unqualified persons from deriving rulings.

Biographical Comparison: Al-Bazdawi vs Al-Sarakhsi
Comparing the lives and relative chronology of al-Bazdawi and al-Sarakhsi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to compare the lives and relative chronology of Imam al-Bazdawi and Imam al-Sarakhsi and determine which usul work was authored earlier.

Core Idea
Al-Sarakhsi began dictating his Usul in 479 AH, three years before al-Bazdawi's death.

Understanding the historical context of our classical texts is essential for appreciating their development and influence. This lesson compares the biographies of two giants of Hanafi usul al-fiqh: Imam al-Bazdawi and Imam al-Sarakhsi. By examining their lifespans and the dating of their major usul works, we can better appreciate the scholarly environment of the 5th century AH.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scholars and their works
Locate the names of the scholars mentioned: Imam al-Bazdawi, author of 'Usul al-Bazdawi' (Kanz al-Wusul), and Imam al-Sarakhsi, author of 'Usul al-Sarakhsi'. Note their full names if given.
Both are major figures in Hanafi usul.
2
Extract and compare key dates
From the text, note al-Bazdawi's birth (400 AH) and death (482 AH). For al-Sarakhsi, note that his birth is unknown and his death is around 490-500 AH. Also note the date al-Sarakhsi began dictating his Usul: Saturday, end of Shawwal 479 AH.
Al-Sarakhsi started his work while al-Bazdawi was still alive.
3
Determine priority of authorship
Since al-Sarakhsi began his Usul in 479 AH, three years before al-Bazdawi's death (482 AH), it is likely that al-Sarakhsi's work was started earlier. However, consider that al-Bazdawi's work may have been completed earlier or later; the text suggests further comparison is needed.
This challenges the assumption that al-Bazdawi's work is older.
4
Note geographic origins
Al-Bazdawi was from Bazda, a village near Nasaf in Transoxiana (Bukhara region). Al-Sarakhsi was from Sarakhs in Khorasan. This shows the wide geographical spread of Hanafi scholarship.
5
Reflect on implications for usul studies
Consider how knowing the chronology might affect understanding of influence between the two works. The author hints at a future study to explore which scholar influenced the other.

Al-Bazdawi and al-Sarakhsi: Two Hanafi Usul Scholars
Biographical comparison and textual observation of two Hanafi usul works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key biographical details of Imam al-Bazdawi and Imam al-Sarakhsi, identify the historical relationship between their respective Usul works, and explain the significance of the similarity in their introductions.

Core Idea
Al-Bazdawi and al-Sarakhsi were contemporaries whose Usul works share striking similarities, reflecting a common Hanafi tradition rather than direct copying.

The two foundational texts of Hanafi usul al-fiqh—the Usul of al-Bazdawi and the Usul of al-Sarakhsi—are remarkably similar, yet they were authored independently by two scholars of the same generation. This lesson explores their biographical trajectories, the chronology of their works, and the textual evidence that informs our understanding of their relationship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scholars
Name Imam al-Bazdawi and Imam al-Sarakhsi, and note their full names and eras (both 5th century AH).
Al-Bazdawi: 'Ali ibn Muhammad; al-Sarakhsi: Muhammad ibn Ahmad.
2
Compare their lifespans
Record al-Bazdawi's birth (400 AH) and death (482 AH); note al-Sarakhsi's death (around 490-500 AH, birth unknown). Observe that al-Bazdawi died earlier, but al-Sarakhsi began dictating his Usul in 479 AH.
Al-Sarakhsi started dictating three years before al-Bazdawi's death.
3
Locate their geographical origins
Identify al-Bazdawi from Transoxiana (Bazdah, near Nasf) and al-Sarakhsi from Khurasan (Sarakhs).
Both regions were centers of Hanafi scholarship.
4
Analyze the textual evidence
Read the introductions of both works as described: they show 'great similarity' and even identical phrases with the same evidence but slightly different order.
The passage does not claim copying, only similarity.
5
Draw a conclusion about influence
Based on the chronology, al-Sarakhsi's dictation predates al-Bazdawi's death. The similarity likely stems from a shared Hanafi tradition, not direct borrowing.
Further research may clarify the exact relationship.

The Dependence of al-Sarakhsi on al-Bazdawi and the Ethics of Attribution
Comparative analysis of two Hanafi usul works with reflection on citation ethics

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify textual similarities between Usul al-Bazdawi and Usul al-Sarakhsi, state the evidence for al-Bazdawi's precedence, and explain the two scholarly paths of attribution in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Al-Sarakhsi's Usul is largely a commentary on al-Bazdawi, yet he never cites him by name.

This lesson examines the relationship between two foundational Hanafi usul works: Usul al-Bazdawi by Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi and Usul al-Sarakhsi by Shams al-A’immah al-Sarakhsi. Through textual comparisons, the author demonstrates that al-Sarakhsi heavily borrowed from al-Bazdawi without explicit acknowledgment. The passage then reflects on the scholarly ethics of attribution, presenting two approaches: one that properly cites sources, and another that omits them, with a reminder to assume good faith. Understanding this dynamic helps us appreciate the cumulative nature of Hanafi usul scholarship and the importance of source criticism.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two works and their authors
Recognize that Usul al-Bazdawi by Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi (d. 482 AH) and Usul al-Sarakhsi by Shams al-A’immah al-Sarakhsi (d. ca. 483 AH) are both major Hanafi usul texts. Note the chronological proximity of their authors.
Al-Sarakhsi began dictating his Usul three years before al-Bazdawi's death.
2
Observe the textual comparisons given in the passage
The passage provides three specific comparisons: the discussion of 'acquired impediments' and travel, the choice of expiation for broken oaths, and the treatment of 'capacity for performance' (ahliyyat al-ada') and intellect. In each, al-Sarakhsi's wording closely follows al-Bazdawi's, sometimes verbatim, with some additions.
Compare the referenced pages: Usul al-Sarakhsi 1/123 vs Usul al-Bazdawi p. 775, and Usul al-Sarakhsi 2/341 vs Usul al-Bazdawi discussion on capacity.
3
Analyze the evidence for precedence
The author notes that al-Sarakhsi began his work three years before al-Bazdawi's death, suggesting al-Bazdawi's text was already in circulation. The extensive verbal overlap indicates al-Sarakhsi used al-Bazdawi's work as a base.
This is a preliminary judgment; the author acknowledges need for further comparison.
4
Understand the two scholarly paths on attribution
The passage describes two approaches: the norm (al-asl) is to attribute statements to their original authors (nisbat al-qawl li qa’ilihi). The second path is to omit mentioning the source altogether. The author urges not to investigate reasons for omission, given the known piety of early scholars.
This reflects a tension between academic rigor and charitable assumption.

Knowledge of legislated matters. And precision in knowing that by understanding the texts with their meanings, and linking the principles to their branches. Then acting upon that, for the completion of the objective is only after acting upon knowledge. And whoever is a memorizer of legislated matters without precision in knowledge: he is among the narrators, and after precision if he does not act upon what he knows: he is a jurist in one aspect, not in another. But if he acts upon what he knows, he is the absolute jurist... End. And by this the great agreement between them appears in the previous texts, with much similarity in expressions, proofs, and division of sciences, and this is very clear to anyone who studies them leisurely. 2- And likewise by comparing their texts in the discussion of acquired impediments, in the speech about gentleness and ease in the chapter of travel, and that the one who swears an oath and breaks it is given a choice between types of expiation due to gentleness he chooses, you will find the expressions compatible between them and unified in examples, with additions by al-Sarakhsi, see Usul al-Sarakhsi 1/123, and Usul al-Bazdawi p. 775 of this edition. 3- And by another comparison between the texts of the two books, Usul al-Bazdawi and Usul al-Sarakhsi 2/341, in the discussion of capacity for performance and its types, and that intellect is known by direct observation, and its deficiency is known by experience and examination... the reader finds that the expressions of al-Bazdawi in this discussion, his examples, and his divisions of the subject are present verbatim in al-Sarakhsi's words, with explanation, additions, and new phrasing. And thus after this delicate comparison of these and other examples, it appears, and Allah knows best, the priority of authorship of Usul al-Bazdawi and that al-Sarakhsi did not explicitly state that he took from it. Evidence for this is the date of al-Sarakhsi's beginning of dictating his Usul, which was three years before al-Bazdawi's death. It also appears that Imam al-Sarakhsi greatly benefited from Usul al-Bazdawi in his Usul; rather, it can be said that Usul al-Sarakhsi is like a commentary on many topics of Usul al-Bazdawi with additions in issues, branches, and examples on usul principles. And despite the above, this remains a preliminary judgment in this comparison, and the matter requires more comparison, and Allah knows best the truth. I say: Even if this is established, it does not diminish the status of the later scholar who takes from them at all, for this benefit obtained by the later from the earlier is very natural among the early imams and scholars in all disciplines; rather, it is a continuation of the academic journey required of every scholar. There is no doubt that there are innovators and originators among the earlier, and completers of them among the later, and builders upon their structure; rather, among the later are those who incorporate the work of the earlier entirely into their work. But the issue is the attribution of the statement to its speaker. The reality among scholars in this regard is on two paths: the first: attributing the statement to its speaker, which is the norm; the second: omitting the mention of the name of the one from whom he transmitted, and leaving out the name of the book that he deposited in his book or took from. And good opinion of the imams and scholars, and what has been transmitted of their sincerity, piety, god-fearing, great asceticism, knowledge, action, self-accountability, and the like, calls us not to delve into the reasons for omission, for each has a direction he is facing.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage is a comparative analysis between two foundational works of Hanafi usul al-fiqh: Usul al-Bazdawi by Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi and Usul al-Sarakhsi by Shams al-A’immah al-Sarakhsi. The author demonstrates through multiple comparisons that al-Sarakhsi's work closely follows al-Bazdawi's in structure, expression, and examples, sometimes verbatim. The passage argues for the chronological precedence of al-Bazdawi's work, noting that al-Sarakhsi began dictating his Usul three years before al-Bazdawi's death, implying that al-Sarakhsi had access to al-Bazdawi's work. Despite the extensive borrowing, al-Sarakhsi did not explicitly acknowledge his source. The author then discusses the scholarly practice of acknowledging sources (nisbah al-qawl li qa’ilih) versus omitting them, and urges good faith, suggesting not to probe into reasons for omission. This passage is from a modern critical edition or study, providing historical context and textual analysis of these classical usul works.

Key Terms
أصول البزدوي (Usul al-Bazdawi): The work on usul al-fiqh by Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi (d. 482 AH), considered a foundational text in Hanafi usul.
أصول السرخسي (Usul al-Sarakhsi): The work on usul al-fiqh by Shams al-A’immah al-Sarakhsi (d. ca. 483 AH), known for its extensive commentary and additions.
نسبة القول لقائله (nisbat al-qawl li qā’ilihi): The principle of attributing a statement to its original author; the norm in scholarly citation.
العوارض المكتسبة (al-‘awāriḍ al-muktasabah): Acquired impediments; conditions that arise after birth affecting legal capacity, such as travel or illness.
أهلية الأداء (ahliyyat al-adā’): Capacity for performance; the legal capacity to execute transactions and be held accountable for actions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary evidence the author uses to claim that al-Sarakhsi benefited from al-Bazdawi?
A) Al-Sarakhsi explicitly states his debt in a preface.
B) The close textual similarity and the chronological date of dictation.
C) Both works have identical titles.
D) Al-Bazdawi was al-Sarakhsi's teacher.

Key Takeaway
Al-Sarakhsi's Usul heavily relies on al-Bazdawi's work, demonstrating the cumulative nature of Hanafi usul, and the author advises against faulting later scholars for omitting citations given their piety and the natural flow of knowledge.

Evaluating Clarity Claims: Al-Bazdawi vs. Al-Sarakhsi's Usul
Biographical comparison with critical evaluation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to critically evaluate scholarly descriptions of Hanafi usul texts by comparing classical and modern assessments.

Core Idea
A text praised by moderns may be deemed obscure by its classical commentators.

In this passage, the author responds to a modern scholar's claim that Usul al-Bazdawi is 'easy and clear'. He contrasts this with the view of classical commentators who lamented its difficulty. This teaches us that evaluating a text's clarity requires context: who is judging and what standard they use. We will parse the arguments and evidence presented.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two works and their authors
Name the authors and their usul texts: Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi (Usul al-Bazdawi) and Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi (Usul al-Sarakhsi). Note their approximate death dates (both 483 AH).
2
Extract the claim made by Muhammad Abu Zahra
Abu Zahra described al-Bazdawi's Usul as 'easy in expression, concise, and the clearest book in the Hanafi method'. Al-Sarakhsi's Usul was said to be broader and more detailed.
3
Identify the author's counter-argument
The author finds Abu Zahra's description 'highly questionable' because earlier commentators explicitly noted the extreme difficulty, obscure phrases, and hidden symbols of al-Bazdawi's text.
4
Note the evidence from scholarly reception
Al-Bazdawi's work received many commentaries, whereas al-Sarakhsi's Usul had none. This suggests the latter may have been less influential or more straightforward, contradicting the idea that al-Bazdawi's is easy.
5
Assess the overall point about scholarly gratitude
The passage begins by quoting Abu Ubayd on gratitude for knowledge: acknowledge your sources. This frames the discussion as a matter of academic integrity.

هذا فالحق الواضح، والاعتراف بالفضل لأهله، والأمانة العلمية، والبركة في العلم تقتضي السير على ما رسمه الإمام الفقيه المحدث اللغوي البارع أبو عبيد القاسم بن سلام (ت٢٢٤هـ) حيث يقول :
من شكر العلم : أن تستفيد الشيء، فإذا ذكر لك: قلت: خفي عليَّ كذا وكذا، ولم يكن لي به علم، حتى أفادني منه فلان كذا وكذا، فهذا شكر العلم (١) وهكذا فإن الشيء بالشيء يُذكر، فقد جاءت في مقدمة السرخسي لكتابه «المبسوط» عبارات هي بعينها موجودة من كلام البزدوي في مقدمة أصوله ، فقد قال السرخسي :
الحمد الله بارئ النَّسَم، ومحيي الرَّمَم، ومُجزل القسم، مُبدع البدائع، وشارع الشرائع ديناً رضياً، ونوراً مُضياً ..... اهـ
وجاء في مقدمة أصول البزدوي:
الحمد لله خالقِ النَّسَم، ورازق القِسم مُبدع البدائع، وشارع الشرائع، ديناً رَضيَّاً، ونوراً مُضيَّاً، وذكراً للأنام، ومَطيَّةً إلى دار السلام». وبمناسبة المقارنة بين أصول البزدوي والسرخسي، فقد وقفت على كلمة في المقارنة بينهما للعلامة الشيخ محمد أبو زهرة (ت١٣٩٤هـ)، حيث يقول في كتابه أصول الفقه ص ۲۳ :
وجاء بعد هؤلاء فخر الإسلام البزدوي، المتوفى سنة ٤٨٣هـ، وألف كتابه المسمى أصول البزدوي ، وهو كتاب سهل العبارة موجزها ، ويُعَد بحقِّ أوضح كتاب ألف في طريقة الحنفية، ثم جاء السرخسي صاحب المبسوط، وألف كتاباً في الأصول، كان له مثل بيان كتاب البزدوي ولكنه أوسع عبارة، وأكثر تفصيلاً». اهـ
قلت هذا الوصف منه رحمه الله لأصول البزدوي فيه نظر جداً بعد ما تقدم من وصف الأئمة الفحول شراح أصول البزدوي لشدة صعوبة أصول البزدوي ، وإقرارهم بانغلاق عباراته، وخفاء رموزه، وأنه صعب المرام، أبي الزمام.
وفي كلامه رحمه الله تصريح بتقدم البزدوي على السرخسي التأليف.
وأنبه هنا أيضاً في المقارنة إلى نقطة أخرى، وهي أن أصول السرخسي لم يذكر المترجمون أي شرح له أو تعليق، أو حاشية ونحو هذا ويظهر هذا من مراجعة كشف الظنون (۱۱۲/۱ ، حيث ذكره ولم يذكر له أي شرح أو تعليق، وكذلك لم يذكر شيئاً من ذلك محققه الشيخ أبو الوفا الأفغاني رحمه الله في مقدمة تحقيقه له، وكذلك لم أقف في الفهارس على شيء من ذلك، والله أعلم.
- وأذكر هنا أنه تم تخريج أحاديث أصول السرخسي في هذا الزمن من قبل باحثين كريمين في مرحلة الدراسات العليا في جامعة أم القرى بمكة المكرمة، ولم يطبع عملهما بعد، يسر الله لهما ذلك.
This is the clear truth, acknowledging the merit of its people, scholarly honesty, and blessing in knowledge require following what the Imam, jurist, hadith scholar, linguist, and outstanding scholar Abu Ubayd al-Qasim ibn Sallam (d. 224 AH) set down, when he said: 'Gratitude for knowledge is: you learn something, and when it is mentioned to you, you say: Such-and-such was hidden from me, and I had no knowledge of it, until so-and-so taught me such-and-such. This is gratitude for knowledge.' Thus, things are remembered by other things. Indeed, in the introduction of al-Sarakhsi to his book al-Mabsut, there are expressions that are exactly found in the words of al-Bazdawi in the introduction of his Usul. Al-Sarakhsi said: 'Praise be to God, Creator of souls, Reviver of remains, and Apportioner of provision, Originator of wonders, and Legislator of laws – a pleasing religion and a radiant light...' And in the introduction of Usul al-Bazdawi: 'Praise be to God, Creator of souls, Provider of provision, Originator of wonders, and Legislator of laws – a pleasing religion, a radiant light, a reminder for mankind, and a mount to the abode of peace.' And on the occasion of the comparison between Usul al-Bazdawi and al-Sarakhsi, I came across a statement comparing them from the scholar Sheikh Muhammad Abu Zahra (d. 1394 AH), where he says in his book Usul al-Fiqh p. 23: 'After these came Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi, who died in 483 AH, and wrote his book called Usul al-Bazdawi, which is an easy expression and concise, and it is by right the clearest book written in the Hanafi method. Then came al-Sarakhsi, the author of al-Mabsut, and wrote a book on Usul, which was like the exposition of al-Bazdawi's book but broader in expression and more detailed.' I say: This description of his – may God have mercy on him – of Usul al-Bazdawi is highly questionable in light of what was mentioned from the great scholars, commentators on Usul al-Bazdawi, regarding the extreme difficulty of Usul al-Bazdawi, and their affirmation of its obscure expressions, hidden symbols, and that it is difficult of access, resisting control. And in his words – may God have mercy on him – there is an explicit statement that al-Bazdawi preceded al-Sarakhsi in authorship. And I also note here another point in the comparison: that the translators have not mentioned any commentary or gloss or footnote for al-Sarakhsi's Usul. This is apparent from reviewing Kashf al-Zunun (1/112), where it mentions it and does not mention any commentary or gloss, nor did its editor Sheikh Abu al-Wafa al-Afghani – may God have mercy on him – mention anything of that in the introduction of his edition. Nor have I found anything of that in the indexes. And God knows best. - And I mention here that the hadiths of al-Sarakhsi's Usul have been extracted in this era by two generous researchers at the postgraduate level at Umm al-Qura University in Makkah al-Mukarramah, but their work has not yet been published. May God facilitate that for them.
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and comparative introduction discussing two major Hanafi usul works: Usul al-Bazdawi by Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi (d. 483 AH) and Usul al-Sarakhsi by Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi (d. 483 AH). The author begins by quoting Abu Ubayd al-Qasim ibn Sallam on scholarly gratitude, emphasizing the importance of acknowledging one's sources. He then notes that al-Sarakhsi's introduction to his famous fiqh work al-Mabsut contains phrases very similar to those in al-Bazdawi's Usul, suggesting either borrowing or a common tradition. The author then cites Muhammad Abu Zahra, a modern scholar, who described al-Bazdawi's Usul as 'easy in expression and concise' and 'the clearest book' in the Hanafi method, while al-Sarakhsi's Usul is said to be broader and more detailed. However, the author strongly disagrees with this assessment, pointing out that earlier commentators on al-Bazdawi's Usul repeatedly noted its extreme difficulty, obscure phrases, and hidden symbols. He argues that Abu Zahra's description is questionable. The author then observes that al-Sarakhsi's Usul has received no commentaries or glosses, unlike al-Bazdawi's work, which had many. He concludes by noting a recent scholarly effort to extract the hadiths in al-Sarakhsi's Usul, which remains unpublished. This passage highlights the scholarly debate over the relative difficulty and clarity of these foundational texts.

Key Terms
فخر الإسلام البزدوي (Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi): A major Hanafi usul scholar (d. 483 AH), author of 'Usul al-Bazdawi' (Kanz al-Wusul ila Ma'rifat al-Usul).
شمس الأئمة السرخسي (Shams al-A'imma al-Sarakhsi): A prominent Hanafi jurist and usuli (d. 483 AH), author of 'Usul al-Sarakhsi' and 'al-Mabsut'.

Biography of Imam Qasim ibn Qutlubugha and His Scholarly Contribution
Biographical sketch of a Hanafi scholar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the scholarly profile of Imam Qasim ibn Qutlubugha and identify his primary contribution to Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Qasim ibn Qutlubugha was a polymath Hanafi scholar whose takhrij of hadith in Usul al-Bazdawi bridges hadith and usul.

This lesson introduces you to Imam Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, a multifaceted scholar whose work on verifying the hadith of Usul al-Bazdawi is a critical resource for understanding Hanafi usul. The passage provides a glimpse into his erudition and the scholarly efforts dedicated to his works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar
Read the passage and list the many titles given to Qasim ibn Qutlubugha (e.g., hafiz, muhaddith, faqih, usuli, etc.). This gives a sense of his breadth.
The passage uses a string of honorifics to establish his authority.
2
Recognize his main work
Locate the phrase 'صاحب تخريج أحاديث أصول البزدوي' – this is his primary contribution mentioned: verifying the hadith of al-Bazdawi's usul work.
Takhrij is a critical method in hadith sciences.
3
Understand the scholarly context
Note that later scholars wrote biographies about him, including a PhD dissertation and a recent edition introduction. This indicates ongoing academic interest.
4
Appreciate the editorial work
The author mentions his own work on serving Usul al-Bazdawi and appending the takhrij. Recognize that this passage is an editorial addition, not part of the original matn.
This distinction prevents confusion about source attribution.

ترجمة الإمام قاسم بن قطلوبغا صاحب تخريج أحاديث أصول البزدوي الشيخ الإمام العلامة الحافظ المحدث، الفقيه الحنفي الأصولي، المفسِّر ، الأديب المؤرخ ، المفنّن في علوم كثيرة، المحقق المدقق المبدع قاسم بن قطلوبغا. لقد كتبت عن الإمام قاسم بن قطلوبغا ترجمات عدة موسعة، جمعت حياته، وتتبعت مصنفاته، وذلك في مقدمات محققي كتبه، وإن من أجود هذه الترجمات ما كتبه الطالب محمد حسين تاجي بن قاسم، فيما قدمه في رسالة الدكتوراه في جامعة كراتشي عام ١٤١٦هـ، بعنوان: «الإمام الحافظ قاسم بن قطلوبغا الحنفي حياته وآثاره مع تحقيق كتابه: تخريج أحاديث أصول البزدوي. ومن آخر الترجمات الجيدة التي صدرت للعلامة قاسم: ما كتبه الدكتور عبد الله كحيلان في مقدمة تحقيقه لتخريج أحاديث أصول البزدوي وقد صدر سنة ١٤٣٤هـ ، في دار كنوز إشبيليا، الرياض، السعودية، وكنتُ قد انتهيتُ من خدمة أصول البزدوي، وتخريج أحاديثه للعلامة ،قاسم وإلحاق تخريج كل حديث منه بمحله من أصول البزدوي، ولم أكن قد دفعت بهما إلى المطبعة بعد.
Biography of Imam Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, author of the verification of hadith of Usul al-Bazdawi. The scholar, imam, allama, hafiz, muhaddith, Hanafi jurist, usuli, mufassir, adib, historian, versatile in many sciences, research scholar, meticulous, innovative: Qasim ibn Qutlubugha. Several extensive biographies have been written about Imam Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, collecting his life and tracing his works in the introductions of his books' editors. Among the most excellent of these biographies is what was written by the student Muhammad Husain Taji ibn Qasim in his doctoral dissertation at the University of Karachi in 1416 AH, titled: 'Imam al-Hafiz Qasim ibn Qutlubugha al-Hanafi: His Life and Works with an Edition of His Book: Takhrij Ahadith Usul al-Bazdawi.' And among the latest good biographies published about Allama Qasim is what was written by Dr. Abdullah Kahlan in the introduction to his edition of Takhrij Ahadith Usul al-Bazdawi, published in 1434 AH in Dar Kunuz Ishbiliya, Riyadh, Saudi Arabia. I had already finished serving Usul al-Bazdawi and verifying its hadith for Allama Qasim, and appending the verification of each hadith to its place in Usul al-Bazdawi, and I had not yet submitted them to the press.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage provides a biographical sketch of Imam Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, a prominent Hanafi scholar who specialized in hadith verification (takhrij) of the usul work of al-Bazdawi. The author lists his many titles: hafiz (master of hadith memorization), muhaddith, faqih, usuli, mufassir, adib, mu'arrikh, and more. The text then mentions several biographies written about him, including a doctoral dissertation by Muhammad Husain Taji and an introduction by Dr. Abdullah Kahlan. The author notes that he himself has completed work on serving the text of Usul al-Bazdawi and its hadith verifications but has not yet published them.

Key Terms
تخريج الحديث (takhrij al-hadith): The process of tracing a hadith back to its original sources and verifying its chain and grading.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Biography of Imam Qasim bin Qutlubugha
Introduces the life and lineage of the Hanafi scholar Qasim bin Qutlubugha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the full name, lineage, nisba, and significance of Imam Qasim bin Qutlubugha in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Qasim bin Qutlubugha: a Hanafi polymath whose takhrij of Usool al-Bazdawi is essential for verifying hadith proofs in usul.

This lesson introduces you to Imam Qasim bin Qutlubugha, a towering Hanafi scholar of the 9th century AH. He was a hafiz, muhaddith, faqih, usuli, and historian. His most famous work is the takhrij (source verification) of the hadith used in Usool al-Bazdawi, a foundational Hanafi usul text. Understanding his background helps you appreciate the reliability of his takhrij and the chain of transmission of Hanafi usul knowledge.

Understand his name: Qasim bin Qutlubugha bin Abdullah. Note the meaning of 'Qutlubugha' (blessed stallion) and the nisba 'al-Suduni al-Jamali' referring to his father's master.
3
Note his scholarly output and significance
His key work is the Takhrij Ahadith Usool al-Bazdawi, where he traces the sources of hadith used in al-Bazdawi's usul text.
4
Identify the key biographical sources
The primary source is al-Sakhawi's al-Daw' al-Lami'. Recent scholarly biographies are also cited.
5
Appreciate his place in Hanafi usul
His takhrij work is crucial for verifying the hadith proofs that underpin Hanafi usul principles, affecting their epistemological weight.

ترجمة الإمام قاسم بن قطلوبغا صاحب تخريج أحاديث أصول البزدوي. الشيخ الإمام العلامة الحافظ المحدث، الفقيه الحنفي الأصولي، المفسِّر، الأديب المؤرخ، المفنّن في علوم كثيرة، المحقق المدقق المبدع قاسم بن قطلوبغا. لقد كتبت عن الإمام قاسم بن قطلوبغا ترجمات عدة موسعة، جمعت حياته، وتتبعت مصنفاته، وذلك في مقدمات محققي كتبه، وإن من أجود هذه الترجمات ما كتبه الطالب محمد حسين تاجي بن قاسم، فيما قدمه في رسالة الدكتوراه في جامعة كراتشي عام ١٤١٦هـ، بعنوان: «الإمام الحافظ قاسم بن قطلوبغا الحنفي حياته وآثاره مع تحقيق كتابه: تخريج أحاديث أصول البزدوي». ومن آخر الترجمات الجيدة التي صدرت للعلامة قاسم: ما كتبه الدكتور عبد الله كحيلان في مقدمة تحقيقه لتخريج أحاديث أصول البزدوي وقد صدر سنة ١٤٣٤هـ، في دار كنوز إشبيليا، الرياض، السعودية، وكنتُ قد انتهيتُ من خدمة أصول البزدوي، وتخريج أحاديثه للعلامة قاسم وإلحاق تخريج كل حديث منه بمحله من أصول البزدوي، ولم أكن قد دفعت بهما إلى المطبعة بعد. إن مِن أوسع مَن عَرَفَ العلامة قاسم من المتقدمين المعاصرين له، عنه بتوسع بقلمٍ مُحِبُّ مُنصف: هو تلميذه الإمام السخاوي في الضوء اللامع، ١٨٤/٦، وكتابته هي أساس لكل ترجمة كُتبت عنه فيما بعد، ولهذا وبعداً عن التكرار فسأقتصر على ترجمة موجزة له، ومن أراد الزيادة فالأمر سهل ميسر، وبالله التوفيق. اسمه ونسبه ولقبه: الإمام زين الدين أو الزين أبو العدل قاسم بن قطلوبغا بن عبد الله السُّودُوني الجمالي، المصري القاهري مولداً ومنشأ ووفاةً، الحنفي مذهباً، ويُعرف بقاسم الحنفي. وجاء بخطه في آخر تخريج أصول البزدوي إضافة لفظ: محمد: قبل: قطلوبغا، فقد كتب: «علقه لنفسه راجي لطف ربه الخفي قاسم بن محمد قطلوبغا الحنفي». اهـ أما قُطلوبغا: فمركَّب من كلمتين باللغة التركية: قطلو: بمعنى المبارك أو الميمون، و بغا بمعنى الفحل وعليه يكون معنى قطلوبغا: الفحل المبارك، أو الفحل الميمون. وأما: السُّودُوني الجَمَالي: فنسبةً لمُعتق أبيه، وهو الأمير جمال الدين سُودُون بن عبد الله الفخري الشيخوني الجركسي، الذي كان نائب السلطنة في عصره في الديار المصرية، وكان أميراً جليلاً في دولة الملك الظاهر برقوق (ت ٨٠١هـ)، وكان الأمير سودون وقوراً معظَّماً عند الملوك خيراً
Translation of Imam Qasim bin Qutlubugha, author of Takhrij Ahadith Usool al-Bazdawi. The Shaykh, Imam, Allamah, Hafiz, Muhaddith, Hanafi jurist, Usuli, exegete, litterateur, historian, versatile in many sciences, the verifying, precise, innovative Qasim bin Qutlubugha. Many extensive biographies have been written about Imam Qasim bin Qutlubugha, collecting his life and tracking his works, in the introductions of the editors of his books. Among the finest of these biographies is what the student Muhammad Husain Taji bin Qasim wrote in his PhD dissertation at the University of Karachi in 1416 AH, titled: 'Imam al-Hafiz Qasim bin Qutlubugha al-Hanafi: His Life and Works, with an Edition of His Book Takhrij Ahadith Usool al-Bazdawi.' And among the latest good biographies published for Allamah Qasim is what Dr. Abdullah Kuhailan wrote in the introduction to his edition of Takhrij Ahadith Usool al-Bazdawi, published in 1434 AH, in Dar Kunuz Ishbiliya, Riyadh, Saudi Arabia. I had completed the service of Usool al-Bazdawi and the takhrij of its hadith by Allamah Qasim and attaching each hadith takhrij to its place in Usool al-Bazdawi, but I had not yet sent them to the press. Indeed, among the most extensive of those who knew Allamah Qasim from the early contemporaries, writing about him extensively with a fair and loving pen, is his student Imam al-Sakhawi in al-Daw' al-Lami', 6/184. His writing is the basis for every biography written about him afterward. Therefore, to avoid repetition, I will limit myself to a brief biography of him. Whoever wants more, the matter is easy and facilitated. And with Allah is success. His name, lineage, and title: Imam Zain al-Din or al-Zain Abu al-Adl Qasim bin Qutlubugha bin Abdullah al-Suduni al-Jamali, Egyptian of Cairo by birth, upbringing, and death, Hanafi in madhhab, known as Qasim al-Hanafi. It appears in his handwriting at the end of Takhrij Usool al-Bazdawi the addition of the word 'Muhammad' before 'Qutlubugha', for he wrote: 'Written for himself, hoping for the hidden kindness of his Lord, Qasim bin Muhammad Qutlubugha al-Hanafi.' End. As for Qutlubugha: it is composed of two words in Turkish: 'Qutlu' meaning blessed or auspicious, and 'Bugha' meaning stallion. Thus the meaning of Qutlubugha is the blessed stallion, or the auspicious stallion. As for al-Suduni al-Jamali: it is a nisba to the emancipator of his father, who is Amir Jamal al-Din Sudun bin Abdullah al-Fakhri al-Shaykhuni al-Jarkasi, who was the deputy of the sultanate in his time in Egypt, and was a great emir in the state of King al-Zahir Barquq (d. 801 AH). Amir Sudun was dignified and greatly respected by kings, good.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction (tarjama) of Imam Qasim bin Qutlubugha, a renowned Hanafi scholar. The text first praises his many titles: Hafiz, Muhaddith, Faqih, Usuli, Mufassir, Adib, Mu'arrikh, and Muhaddiq. It then notes that several extensive biographies have been written about him, citing two excellent examples: a PhD dissertation by Muhammad Husain Taji bin Qasim (1416 AH) and a recent edition by Dr. Abdullah Kuhailan (1434 AH). The author mentions that he himself had completed work on Usool al-Bazdawi and Qasim's takhrij but had not yet published it. He then quotes Imam al-Sakhawi's al-Daw' al-Lami' as the primary source for Qasim's biography. The passage gives Qasim's full name: Zain al-Din Qasim bin Qutlubugha bin Abdullah al-Suduni al-Jamali al-Misri al-Hanafi. It notes a variant in his name: he sometimes wrote 'Muhammad' before 'Qutlubugha', making his name Qasim bin Muhammad Qutlubugha. The meaning of 'Qutlubugha' is explained: 'Qutlu' means 'blessed' and 'Bugha' means 'stallion' in Turkish, so 'blessed stallion'. The nisba 'al-Suduni al-Jamali' refers to his father's master, Amir Jamal al-Din Sudun, a deputy sultan in Egypt under al-Zahir Barquq. This biography establishes Qasim's authority as a Hanafi scholar and explains his connection to the text Usool al-Bazdawi, for which he produced a takhrij (source verification) of its hadith.

Key Terms
تخريج (takhrij): The process of tracing and verifying the sources and chains of transmission of hadith used in a fiqh text.
قطلوبغا (Qutlubugha): Turkish compound name meaning 'blessed stallion'.
السُّودُوني الجَمَالي (al-Suduni al-Jamali): Nisba referring to his father's master, Amir Jamal al-Din Sudun.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) The great scholar
B) The blessed stallion
C) The Egyptian jurist
D) The hadith expert

Key Takeaway
Imam Qasim bin Qutlubugha is a crucial figure in Hanafi usul due to his takhrij of the hadith in Usool al-Bazdawi.

Biography of Qasim ibn Qutlubugha
Biography of the author

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the full name, lineage, and key biographical facts of Qasim ibn Qutlubugha and explain the significance of his biography for studying Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Qasim ibn Qutlubugha's commentary on Usul al-Bazdawi is foundational; his background as a Hanafi scholar in Mamluk Cairo shaped his work.

This passage introduces the author of the text we are studying. Knowing his background helps appreciate his method and status. The passage gives his name, lineage, and key life events, including the meaning of his Turkish name and his connection to notable figures of his time.

Guided Path
1
Extract the full name and titles
Identify the author's complete name, laqab (title), and nisbas from the first paragraph. Note that he is a Hanafi scholar from Cairo.
Look for the phrase: 'الإمام زين الدين أو الزين أبو العدل قاسم بن قطلوبغا بن عبد الله السُّودُوني الجمالي'.
2
Analyze the name 'Qutlubugha'
Break down the Turkish compound name: 'Qutlu' (blessed/auspicious) + 'Bugha' (stallion). Understand its meaning and why it is important for his identity.
The author himself added 'Muhammad' before 'Qutlubugha' in his handwriting, indicating his name could also be Qasim ibn Muhammad Qutlubugha.
3
Understand the nisba 'al-Suduni al-Jamali'
This nisba traces back to his father's freed master, Amir Jamal al-Din Sudun, a prominent Mamluk figure. This illustrates the social context of the author's family.
The nisba is a common way to indicate patronage or origin in the Mamluk period.
4
Identify key biographical milestones
Note his birth in 802 AH, his orphanhood, his early memorization of Quran, his sharp intellect, and his studies in various sciences, especially Hanafi fiqh and usul.
He became widely known and excelled in multiple disciplines.
5
Recognize the source of the biography
The passage states that his student al-Sakhawi wrote the most comprehensive biography in al-Daw' al-Lami'. This helps validate the information.
Al-Sakhawi is a famous historian and scholar.
