وكتب
إن مِن أوسع مَن عَرَفَ العلامة قاسم من المتقدمين المعاصرين له، عنه بتوسع بقلمٍ مُحِبُّ مُنصف : هو تلميذه الإمام السخاوي في الضوء اللامع ،١٨٤/٦ ، وكتابته هي أساس لكل ترجمة كُتبت عنه فيما بعد، ولهذا وبعداً عن التكرار فسأقتصر على ترجمة موجزة له، ومن أراد الزيادة فالأمر سهل ميسر، وبالله التوفيق.
هو
اسمه ونسبه ولقبه :
الإمام زين الدين أو الزين أبو العدل قاسم بن قطلوبغا بن عبد الله السُّودُوني الجمالي، المصري القاهري مولداً ومنشأ ووفاةً، الحنفي مذهباً ، ويُعرف بقاسم الحنفي.
وجاء بخطه في آخر تخريج أصول البزدوي إضافة لفظ : محمد : قبل: قطلوبغا، فقد كتب: «علقه لنفسه راجي لطف ربه الخفي قاسم بن محمد قطلوبغا الحنفي». اهـ أما قُطلوبغا : فمركَّب من كلمتين باللغة التركية : قطلو: بمعنى المبارك أو الميمون، و بغا بمعنى الفحل وعليه يكون معنى قطلوبغا: الفحل المبارك ، أو الفحل الميمون.
وأما : السُّودُوني الجَمَالي : فنسبةً لمُعتق أبيه، وهو الأمير جمال الدين سُودُون بن عبد الله الفخري الشيخوني الجركسي، الذي كان نائب السلطنة في عصره في الديار المصرية، وكان أميراً جليلاً في دولة الملك الظاهر برقوق (ت ٨٠١هـ) ، وكان الأمير سودون وقوراً معظَّماً عند الملوك خيراً ديناً ، محباً للعلماء، توفي سنة ٧٩٨هـ
وكان قطلوبغا والد العلامة قاسم من الفتيان الذين استقدمهم الأمير سودون من القوقاز للتجنيد في مصر، على العادة الجارية في ذلك الزمن. وقد ترجم السخاوي في الضوء اللامع ٢٢٣/٦ لقُطلوبغا والد العلامة قاسم باختصار، وقال في ترجمته: «يُقال: إنه كان من روؤس التُّوَب، ويُلقب بالزراف. اهـ
ووظيفة رأس النَّوبة : لقب يُطلق على الذي يتحدث على مماليك السلطان أو الأمير، وتنفيذ أمره فيهم، أو الحكم على المماليك السلطانية (٢).
(۲)
ولادته، وطلبه للعلم وأشهر شيوخه وتلاميذه :
ولد العلامة قاسم في شهر المحرم سنة ٨٠٢هـ، بالقاهرة في مصر، ومات أبوه وهو صغير ، فنشأ يتيماً، وحفظ القرآن، وبدأ بطلب العلم بهمةٍ عالية وجد ونشاط، مع ذكاء متقد، وحافظة قوية، وكان له حظوة عند شيوخه ؛ لما مَنَحَه الله تعالى من مواهب علمية نادرة، وهكذا استمر حتى شاع ذكره، وانتشر صيته.
وقد حفظَ كُتباً عديدة في فنون مختلفة، وعَرَضَ بعضها على شيوخه، و دَرَسَ التفسير وعلوم القرآن والحديث وعلومه، والفقه الحنفي وأصوله، وتبحر فيهما، بل أبدع في فنون شتى ، وبرع فيها ومهر، ونظر
And he wrote. Indeed, among the most comprehensive of those who knew the scholar Qasim from among the earlier contemporaries about him, in detail with a fair and loving pen, is his student Imam al-Sakhawi in al-Daw' al-Lami', 6/184. And his writing is the foundation for every biography written about him afterwards. Therefore, to avoid repetition, I will limit myself to a brief biography of him. Whoever wants more, it is easy and facilitated. And with Allah is success. He is: His name, lineage, and title: Imam Zain al-Din or al-Zain Abu al-'Adl Qasim ibn Qutlubugha ibn Abd Allah al-Suduni al-Jamali, Egyptian Cairene by birth, upbringing, and death, Hanafi in madhhab, and known as Qasim al-Hanafi. And it came in his own handwriting at the end of his takhrij of Usul al-Bazdawi, adding the word Muhammad before Qutlubugha. He wrote: 'Recorded for himself, hoping for the hidden grace of his Lord, Qasim ibn Muhammad Qutlubugha al-Hanafi.' End. As for Qutlubugha, it is composed of two words in Turkish: Qutlu meaning blessed or auspicious, and Bugha meaning stallion. Therefore the meaning of Qutlubugha is the blessed stallion or the auspicious stallion. And as for al-Suduni al-Jamali, it is a nisba to his father's emancipator, who is Amir Jamal al-Din Sudun ibn Abd Allah al-Fakhri al-Shaykhuni al-Jarkasi, who was the deputy of the sultanate in his time in Egypt, and he was a noble amir in the state of King al-Zahir Barquq (died 801 AH). And Amir Sudun was dignified, respected by kings, religious, loving scholars. He died in 798 AH. And Qutlubugha, the father of the scholar Qasim, was among the youths brought by Amir Sudun from the Caucasus for recruitment in Egypt, according to the custom of that time. And al-Sakhawi wrote a brief biography of Qutlubugha, father of the scholar Qasim, in al-Daw' al-Lami' 6/223, and said in his biography: 'It is said that he was among the heads of the Tub, and he was nicknamed al-Ziraf.' End. And the position of Ra's al-Nawbah is a title given to one who speaks on behalf of the slaves of the sultan or amir, executes his orders among them, or rules over the sultanic slaves (2). (2) His birth, pursuit of knowledge, and most famous teachers and students: The scholar Qasim was born in the month of Muharram in the year 802 AH in Cairo, Egypt. His father died while he was young, so he grew up an orphan. He memorized the Quran and began seeking knowledge with high aspiration, seriousness, and activity, with sharp intelligence and a strong memory. He was favored by his teachers because Allah had granted him rare scholarly gifts. Thus he continued until his reputation spread and his fame became widespread. He memorized many books in various disciplines, presented some of them to his teachers, and studied tafsir, Quranic sciences, hadith and its sciences, Hanafi fiqh and its usul, and became an expert in them, indeed excelled in various sciences, became proficient and skilled in them, and examined.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to the author of the book, the Hanafi scholar Qasim ibn Qutlubugha. It begins by noting that the most comprehensive biography of Qasim was written by his student al-Sakhawi in his work al-Daw' al-Lami'. Then it gives his full name: Zain al-Din or al-Zain Abu al-'Adl Qasim ibn Qutlubugha ibn Abd Allah al-Suduni al-Jamali, emphasizing his Hanafi affiliation. It explains that in his own handwriting, he added the name Muhammad before Qutlubugha. The text then analyzes the name Qutlubugha etymologically: it is Turkish, combining 'Qutlu' (blessed/auspicious) and 'Bugha' (stallion) to mean 'blessed stallion' or 'auspicious stallion'. The nisba 'al-Suduni al-Jamali' refers to his father's freed master, Amir Jamal al-Din Sudun, a prominent figure in the Mamluk state under Sultan Barquq. The passage explains that Qasim's father, Qutlubugha, was brought by Amir Sudun from the Caucasus as a recruit. It then notes that al-Sakhawi also wrote a short biography of the father, mentioning that he was among the 'heads of the Tub' (an obscure term, possibly a military rank) and nicknamed 'al-Ziraf'. The term 'Ra's al-Nawbah' is defined as a title for someone who supervises the sultan's or amir's slave soldiers. Finally, the passage details Qasim's birth in Muharram 802 AH, his orphanhood, memorization of Quran, his sharp intellect, and his extensive studies in tafsir, hadith, Hanafi fiqh and usul, indicating his scholarly excellence.

Key Terms
قطلوبغا (Qutlubugha): A Turkish compound name meaning 'blessed stallion' or 'auspicious stallion'.
السودوني الجمالي (al-Suduni al-Jamali): A nisba referring to Amir Jamal al-Din Sudun, the freed master of Qasim ibn Qutlubugha's father.
رأس النوبة (Ra's al-Nawbah): A title for the one who manages the Mamluk soldiers of the sultan or amir, conveying orders and overseeing them.

Key Takeaway
Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, a Hanafi scholar born in 802 AH, authored a commentary on Usul al-Bazdawi and his name reflects his Turkish origin.

Biography of Qasim ibn Qutlubugha: His Life and Teachers
Biographical sketch of the author's life, teachers, and students

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state key biographical facts about Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, including his birth year, prominent teachers, and students, and explain his significance in Hanafi scholarship.

Core Idea
Qasim ibn Qutlubugha was a Hanafi scholar born in 802 AH who studied under Ibn Hajar and Ibn al-Humam, and taught al-Suyuti.

This lesson introduces the life of Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, a prominent Hanafi jurist and scholar of usul al-fiqh. Understanding his biography helps contextualize his works and his role in the transmission of Hanafi knowledge. We will explore his early life, his teachers, his students, and his scholarly legacy.

Guided Path
1
Locate the subject
Identify the scholar Qasim ibn Qutlubugha and his father's background from the passage.

List the prominent scholars he studied under, especially Ibn Hajar and Ibn al-Humam.
He accompanied Ibn al-Humam for 36 years.
4
Identify his students
List notable students including al-Sakhawi and al-Suyuti.
5
Assess his legacy
Consider the breadth of his learning and his role as a teacher and mufti.

ديناً ، محباً للعلماء، توفي سنة ٧٩٨هـ وكان قطلوبغا والد العلامة قاسم من الفتيان الذين استقدمهم الأمير سودون من القوقاز للتجنيد في مصر، على العادة الجارية في ذلك الزمن. وقد ترجم السخاوي في الضوء اللامع ٢٢٣/٦ لقُطلوبغا والد العلامة قاسم باختصار، وقال في ترجمته: «يُقال: إنه كان من روؤس التُّوَب، ويُلقب بالزراف. اهـ ووظيفة رأس النَّوبة : لقب يُطلق على الذي يتحدث على مماليك السلطان أو الأمير، وتنفيذ أمره فيهم، أو الحكم على المماليك السلطانية (٢). (۲) ولادته، وطلبه للعلم وأشهر شيوخه وتلاميذه : ولد العلامة قاسم في شهر المحرم سنة ٨٠٢هـ، بالقاهرة في مصر، ومات أبوه وهو صغير ، فنشأ يتيماً، وحفظ القرآن، وبدأ بطلب العلم بهمةٍ عالية وجد ونشاط، مع ذكاء متقد، وحافظة قوية، وكان له حظوة عند شيوخه ؛ لما مَنَحَه الله تعالى من مواهب علمية نادرة، وهكذا استمر حتى شاع ذكره، وانتشر صيته. وقد حفظَ كُتباً عديدة في فنون مختلفة، وعَرَضَ بعضها على شيوخه، و دَرَسَ التفسير وعلوم القرآن والحديث وعلومه، والفقه الحنفي وأصوله، وتبحر فيهما، بل أبدع في فنون شتى ، وبرع فيها ومهر، ونظر (۱) له ترجمة في النجوم الزاهرة ١٥۱/۱۲ ، إنباء الغمر ٣٠٣/٣. (٢) كما في صبح الأعشى ١٨/٤، ٤٥٥/٥ . في كتب الأدب ودواوين الشعر، وحفظ منها شيئاً كثيراً. وعُرف بقوة الحافظة ،والذكاء وأشير إليه بالعلم، وأذن له غير واحد من مشايخه بالإفتاء والتدريس وأثنوا عليه وقد أخذ عن كثيرين من العلم في زمانه، وله منهم إجازات وهو في أول سني طلبه للعلم. * ومن أشهر شيوخه : أئمة الإمام الحافظ ابن حجر العسقلاني (ت ٨٥٢هـ)، والإمام الكمال ابن الهمام (ت ٨٦١هـ) ، وقد لازمه ٣٦ سنة، وذلك من عام ٨٢٥هـ، حتى توفي ابن الهمام رحمه الله والإمام ابن الجزري المقرىء (ت٨٣٣هـ)، والإمام السعد ابن الديري (ت ٨٦٧هـ ) ، والإمام السراج قارئ الهداية ت ۸۲۹ هـ). وغيرهم كثير ممن أخذ عنهم في القاهرة والإسكندرية، وفي غيرها من البلاد التي رحل إليها، كالحرمين الشريفين، فقد حجّ مراراً، وبيت المقدس وبلاد الشام. ومن أشهر تلامذته الذين أخذوا عنه في فنون كثيرة، وهم كثر، بل قال ابن العماد في شذرات الذهب ٣٢٦/٧ : (وأخذ عنه مَن لا يُحصى كثرة». اهـ، ومن أشهرهم: الإمام السخاوي محمد بن عبد الرحمن (ت۹۰۲هـ)، والإمام جلال الدين السيوطي (ت ۹۱۱ هـ)، والإمام يوسف بن تغري بردي (ت ٨٨٥هـ ) . ٨٧٤هـ)، والإمام البقاعي إبراهيم بن عمر
religious, lover of scholars, died in 798 AH. Qutlubugha, the father of the scholar Qasim, was among the youths brought by Prince Sudun from the Caucasus for military service in Egypt, according to the prevailing custom at that time. Al-Sakhawi briefly translated Qutlubugha in al-Daw' al-Lami' 6/223, saying in his translation: 'It is said that he was among the heads of the tub, and was nicknamed al-Ziraf.' End. The function of Ra's al-Nawbah is a title given to the one who speaks on behalf of the Sultan's or Prince's Mamluks, executes his orders among them, or rules over the sultanic Mamluks (2). (2) His birth, pursuit of knowledge, and most famous teachers and students: The scholar Qasim was born in Muharram 802 AH in Cairo, Egypt, and his father died while he was young, so he grew up an orphan. He memorized the Quran and began seeking knowledge with high ambition, diligence, and activity, with sharp intelligence and strong memory. He was favored by his teachers because of the rare scholarly talents Allah had granted him. He continued until his fame spread and his reputation became widespread. He memorized many books in various disciplines, presented some to his teachers, and studied tafsir, Quranic sciences, hadith and its sciences, Hanafi fiqh and its principles, mastering them both. He excelled in many fields, became proficient, and looked into (1) His biography is in al-Nujum al-Zahira 12/151, Inba' al-Ghumr 3/303. (2) As in Subh al-A'sha 4/18, 5/455. books of literature and poetry collections, memorizing a great deal. He was known for strong memory and intelligence, and was pointed to for knowledge. More than one of his teachers gave him permission to give fatwa and teach, and praised him. He studied under many scholars of his time and had authorizations from them while still in the early years of his seeking knowledge. Among his most famous teachers: Imam al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani (d. 852 AH), Imam Kamal Ibn al-Humam (d. 861 AH), whom he accompanied for 36 years from 825 AH until Ibn al-Humam died, may Allah have mercy on him, Imam Ibn al-Jazari al-Muqri' (d. 833 AH), Imam Sa'd Ibn al-Dayri (d. 867 AH), and Imam Siraj Qari' al-Hidayah (d. 829 AH). And many others from whom he took knowledge in Cairo, Alexandria, and elsewhere in the lands he traveled to, such as the two noble sanctuaries (Makkah and Madinah) — he performed Hajj many times — and Jerusalem and the Levant. Among his most famous students who learned from him in many disciplines, and they are many, indeed Ibn al-'Imad said in Shadharat al-Dhahab 7/326: 'Those who studied under him are countless.' End. Among the most famous: Imam al-Sakhawi Muhammad ibn Abd al-Rahman (d. 902 AH), Imam Jalal al-Din al-Suyuti (d. 911 AH), Imam Yusuf ibn Taghribirdi (d. 874/885 AH), and Imam al-Biqa'i Ibrahim ibn Umar.
Source pages p. 67

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to the life of the Hanafi scholar Qasim ibn Qutlubugha. It begins with a brief note about his father, Qutlubugha, who was brought from the Caucasus for military service in Egypt and held a position of 'Ra's al-Nawbah', overseeing the Mamluk troops. The main subject, Qasim, was born in Cairo in 802 AH (corresponding to 1399-1400 CE). He lost his father early and grew up as an orphan, which did not hinder his scholarly pursuits. He memorized the Quran and studied under prominent scholars of his time, including the famous hadith master Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani and the Hanafi jurist Kamal ibn al-Humam, whom he accompanied for 36 years. Qasim excelled in various Islamic sciences, particularly Hanafi fiqh and usul al-fiqh. He became a renowned teacher and mufti, with many students, including the famous historians and scholars al-Sakhawi and al-Suyuti. His strong memory and intelligence are highlighted. The passage also lists his teachers and students, emphasizing the breadth of his learning and his travels for knowledge.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Qasim ibn Qutlubugha was a prolific Hanafi scholar who studied under leading figures of his time and taught many notable students, leaving a lasting legacy in Hanafi jurisprudence.

Praises of Scholars for Qasim ibn Qutlubugha
Biographical praises establishing author's credentials

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the six scholars who praised Qasim ibn Qutlubugha and state the qualities they highlighted, recognizing the role of biographical praise in establishing scholarly authority in Hanafi usul.

Core Idea
Scholarly praises of Qasim ibn Qutlubugha confirm his expertise and authority as a Hanafi usul scholar.

This passage presents six praises from prominent scholars, including his teacher Ibn Hajar and his student al-Sakhawi, highlighting his mastery in hadith, fiqh, and usul. Understanding these credentials is valuable because they authenticate the usul text that follows, showing that the author was a trusted authority in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the praising scholars
List the six scholars who gave praises. Note their relationship to Qasim (teacher, student, contemporary).
Scholars: Ibn Hajar, Radwan, Ibn al-Dairi, al-Sakhawi (two quotes), Ibn Iyas.
2
Extract key qualities
For each praise, note the specific attributes mentioned (e.g., 'hafiz', 'faqih', 'unique', 'eloquent').
Focus on scholarly terms, not general character traits.
3
Assess the pattern
Observe the consistency of superlatives and the range of disciplines (hadith, fiqh, debate).
Multiple independent sources confirm his excellence.
4
Connect to usul work
Reflect on how these praises serve to establish the author's credibility for a text on usul al-fiqh.
A trusted author lends weight to the principles derived.

ثناءات العلماء عليه : كَثُرت الثناءات العالية السامية على المترجم من العلماء المعاصرين له، من شيوخه خاصة وممن بعدهم، وأقروا له بالفضل والعلم، ومن تلك الثناءات :
١- ما قاله عنه شيخه الإمام الحافظ ابن حجر العسقلاني (ت ٨٥٢هـ)، كما نقل عنه الإمام السخاوي: «الإمام العلامة المحدث الفقيه الحافظ». اهـ ووصفه أيضاً في مناسبة أخرى بقوله: «الشيخ الفاضل، المحدث الكامل الأوحد. قال: وكان قد قرأ علي الإيثار بمعرفة رواة الآثار قراءة وتحريراً، فأفاد ونبَّه على مواضع ألحقت في هذا الأصل، فزادته نوراً». اهـ قال السخاوي: وهو المعني بقول ابن حجر في خطبة هذا الكتاب: إن بعض الإخوان التمس مني فأجبته إلى ذلك مسارعاً، ووقفت عند ما اقترح طائعاً». اهـ
۲- وأثنى عليه الإمام المحدث الزين رضوان بن محمد (ت ٨٥٢هـ) في بعض مجاميعه بقوله: من حُذَاق الحنفية، كتب الفوائد، واستفاد وأفاد». اهـ
٣- ووصفه شيخه الإمام السعد ابن الديري بقوله: «الشيخ العالم الذكي». اهـ ينظر لغالب هذه الثناءات في الضوء اللامع ١٨٥/٦.
٤- وقال عنه تلميذه الإمام السخاوي: «وهو إمامٌ علامة، قوي المشاركة في فنون، ذاكر لكثير من الأدب ومتعلقاته، واسع الباع في استحضار مذهبه، وكثير من زواياه وخباياه، متقدم في هذا الفن، طَلْقُ اللسان قادر على المناظرة وإفحام الخصم، وكلامه أحسن من كونه غاية في التواضع، وطَرْح التكلف، وصفاء الخاطر، وحُسن المحاضرة، ولا سيما في الأشياء التي يحفظها ، وعدم اليبس والصلابة، والرغبة في المذاكرة للعلم وإثارة الفائدة والاقتباس ممن دونه مما لعله لم يكن أتقنه. وقد انفرد من علماء مذهبه الذين أدركناهم بالتقدم في هذا الفن، وصار بينهم من أجلة شأنه، مع توقف الكثير منهم في شأنه، وعدم إنزاله منزلته، وهكذا كان حال أكثرهم معه ؛ جرياً على عادة العصريين. وقصد بالفتاوى في النوازل والمهمات، فبلغوا باعتنائه غالباً، واشتهر بذلك». اهـ
٥- وقال عنه السخاوي أيضاً في الذيل التام على دول الإسلام ۲۸۳/۲ : العلامة الأوحد الحافظ، أحد الأعيان، ممن تصدى للعلم إقراء وتصنيفاً وإسماعاً، فكثرت طلبته وتصانيفه، واجتمع فيه من المحاسن ما يفوق فيه غيره ما تفرق في غيره)، وترجح على غيره من علماء مذهبه بهذا الشأن، وبالتوسع في الأدب، وحسن المحاضرة، مع تقدم من لم يبلغ شأوه عليه، والكمال لله». اهـ
٦- وقال عنه ابن إياس (ت ٩٣٠هـ) : «العلامة الشيخ قاسم بن قطلوبغا، كان عالماً فقهياً محدثاً ، كثير النوادر ، مفتياً من أعيان الحنفية، وكان نادرة عصره». اهـ
Praises of the scholars upon him: Numerous high and lofty praises were made upon the translated person by contemporary scholars, especially his teachers and those after them, and they acknowledged his virtue and knowledge. Among those praises:
1. What his teacher, al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani (d. 852 AH), said about him, as transmitted by al-Sakhawi: “The imam, the scholar, the muhaddith, the jurist, the hafiz.” End. He also described him on another occasion: “The virtuous shaykh, the complete and unique muhaddith. He said: He read to me ‘al-Ithar bi-Ma'rifat Ruwat al-Athar’ with reading and editing, and he benefited and pointed out places that were added to this original, increasing it in light.” End. Al-Sakhawi said: He is the one meant by Ibn Hajar in the preface of this book: “Some brothers requested from me, and I responded to that eagerly, and I stopped at what he proposed willingly.” End.
2. And praised him the muhaddith al-Zayn Radwan ibn Muhammad (d. 852 AH) in some of his collections: “He is among the clever Hanafis; he wrote benefits, benefited and was benefited.” End.
3. And described him his teacher al-Sa'd Ibn al-Dairi: “The knowledgeable, intelligent shaykh.” End. See most of these praises in al-Daw' al-Lami' 6/185.
4. And said about him his student al-Sakhawi: “He is an imam, a scholar, strong in participation in various disciplines, remembering much of literature and its related subjects, broad in capacity to recall his madhhab and many of its corners and secrets, advanced in this field, eloquent, capable of debate and refuting opponents; his speech is better than his character; he is utmost in humility, avoidance of artificiality, clarity of mind, good conversation, especially in things he memorized; lack of harshness and rigidity; desire to discuss knowledge, provoke benefit, and learn from those below him in what he perhaps had not mastered. He was unique among the scholars of his madhhab we met in advancement in this field, and became among them of high standing, although many of them hesitated about him and did not place him in his proper rank, and such was the case of most of them with him, following the habit of contemporaries. He was sought for fatwas in unprecedented matters and important issues, and they mostly achieved their aims through his care, and he became famous for that.” End.
5. And said about him al-Sakhawi also in al-Dhayl al-Tamm 'ala Duwwal al-Islam 2/283: “The unique scholar, the hafiz, one of the notables, who dedicated himself to knowledge through teaching, authorship, and dictation; his students and books became many, and he combined such virtues that surpass what is scattered in others; he excelled over other scholars of his madhhab in this regard, and in breadth of literature, and good conversation, despite the seniority of those who did not reach his level. Perfection belongs to Allah.” End.
6. And said about him Ibn Iyas (d. 930 AH): “The scholar, Shaykh Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, was a learned jurist, muhaddith, full of anecdotes, a mufti from the notable Hanafis, and was the rarity of his time.” End.
Source pages p. 69

Commentary
This passage is a biographical appendix collecting praises (ثناءات) of the scholar Qasim ibn Qutlubugha from several prominent scholars. It serves as an introduction or front matter to the usul work, establishing the author's scholarly credentials. The passage quotes six testimonies: from Ibn Hajar al-Asqalani (his teacher), Radwan ibn Muhammad, al-Sa'd ibn al-Dairi, al-Sakhawi (his student, with two quotes), and Ibn Iyas. Each emphasizes his mastery in hadith, fiqh, and usul, his eloquence, his ability in debate, and his unique position among Hanafis. The final note from Ibn Iyas calls him 'the rarity of his time'. This section is not part of the usul text itself but provides context about the author's authority.

Key Terms
ثناءات (thana'at): Praises or commendations from scholars about the subject's knowledge and virtue.
المترجم (al-mutarjam): The person whose biography is being given; here, Qasim ibn Qutlubugha.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The biographical praises of Qasim ibn Qutlubugha establish his scholarly credentials, affirming that his usul text rests on the authority of a recognized Hanafi master.

Imam Qasim ibn Qutlubugha: A Hanafi Polymath and Authority
Biographical praise of a Hanafi scholar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key scholarly contributions and authority of Imam Qasim ibn Qutlubugha within the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Imam Qasim ibn Qutlubugha was a leading Hanafi jurist, usuli, and muhaddith, whose works were relied upon by later authorities.

This passage collects testimonies from multiple scholars about Imam Qasim ibn Qutlubugha (d. 879 AH). Despite some contemporaries not fully recognizing his rank, his students and later Hanafi scholars praised him as a rare genius and even 'the seal of the mujtahids.' Understanding his background helps us appreciate why his works, especially his Fatawa and Sharh Mukhtasar al-Manar, are cited in later Hanafi legal and usul texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholar
Who is being described? Note his full name, dates, and madhhab affiliation.
Imam Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, d. 879 AH, Hanafi.
2
List the key testimonies
Identify the scholars who praised him: al-Sakhawi, Ibn Iyas, Ibn al-Himsi, Ibn al-Imad, Ibn Abidin, al-Laknawi.
Each testimony adds a different dimension.
3
Extract the qualities
What attributes are highlighted? (e.g., mastery of fiqh, hadith, literature, debate, humility)
Al-Sakhawi emphasizes wide knowledge and eloquence; Ibn Abidin emphasizes investigative rigor.
4
Note the works mentioned
What specific works are attributed to him?
Fatawa, Sharh Mukhtasar al-Manar, and many treatises.
5
Recognize the authority
Why does this biography matter for Hanafi fiqh and usul?
Later authorities like Ibn Abidin relied on his fatwas and considered him a mujtahid.

وذكره العلامة اللكنوي في الفوائد البهية ص ۹۹ فقال: «طالعتُ تصانيفه: فتاواه، وشرح مختصر المنار، ورسائل كثيرة، كلُّها مفيدة، شاهدة على تبحره في فن الفقه والحديث وغيرهما». اهـ
God, his pen. 4- His student Imam al-Sakhawi said about him: 'He is an imam, a scholar, strong in participation in various arts, knowledgeable in much of literature and its related fields, of wide capacity in recalling his madhhab and many of its subtleties and hidden aspects, advanced in this art, eloquent in speech, capable of debate and silencing opponents, and his speech is more beautiful than being utmost in humility, abandoning affectation, purity of mind, good lecturing, especially in things he memorized, lack of dryness and rigidity, desire for scholarly discussion and eliciting benefit and learning from those below him in what he may not have mastered. He was unique among the scholars of his madhhab whom we met in advancement in this art, and became among them of high standing, despite many of them hesitating about his status and not placing him in his proper rank, and such was the case of most of them with him, following the custom of contemporaries. People sought him for fatwas in calamities and important matters, and they mostly achieved their goals through his attention, and he became famous for that.' End quote. Then al-Sakhawi also said in al-Dhayl al-Tamm ala Duwal al-Islam 2/283: 'The unique scholar, the hafiz, one of the notable figures, who engaged in teaching, writing, and transmitting knowledge, so his students and works became numerous, and there gathered in him of virtues what surpasses others as scattered in others.' He outweighed others of his madhhab in this regard, and in breadth of literature and good lecturing, despite the advancement of those who did not reach his level, and perfection belongs to God. End quote. 6- Ibn Iyas (d. 930 AH) said about him: 'The scholar Shaykh Qasim ibn Qutlubugha was a jurist, a hadith scholar, full of rare knowledge, a mufti among the prominent Hanafis, and he was the rarity of his time.' End quote. 7- Shihab al-Din Ibn al-Himsi (d. 934 AH) said about him in Hawadith al-Zaman wa Wafayat al-Shuyukh wa al-Aqran 3/205-206: 'The shaykh, the imam, the scholar, the multi-disciplinary researcher, after him there was no Hanafi like him.' End quote. 6- The historian Ibn al-Imad said in Shadharat al-Dhahab 9/488: 'In short, he is among the blessings of the age.' End quote. Ibn Abidin said in passing in his Hashiyah ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar 1/210 (Bulaq ed.): 'The scholar Qasim mentioned this issue in his Fatawa... and adduced evidence for it in a manner that cannot be surpassed, and he investigated and scrutinized, as is his wont, may God have mercy on him.' End quote. He also said about him in 3/215: 'The scholar Qasim, the seal of the mujtahids.' End quote. Al-Laknawi mentioned him in al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya p. 99 and said: 'I have examined his works: his Fatawa, his Sharh Mukhtasar al-Manar, and many treatises, all beneficial, testifying to his deep knowledge in the field of fiqh and hadith and others.' End quote.
Source pages p. 70

Commentary
This passage is a collection of biographical testimonials about Imam Qasim ibn Qutlubugha (d. 879 AH), a leading Hanafi jurist and hadith scholar of the Mamluk period. His student al-Sakhawi emphasizes his mastery of multiple disciplines, his eloquence in debate, and his humility. Despite some contemporaries not fully recognizing his rank, he was widely sought for fatwas on major issues. Other historians like Ibn Iyas, Ibn al-Himsi, and Ibn al-Imad praise him as a rare scholar and even 'the seal of the mujtahids' according to Ibn Abidin. The later scholar al-Laknawi notes his key works: his Fatawa, a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Manar (a usul al-fiqh text), and numerous treatises. This biography establishes his authority as a Hanafi jurist and usuli, which is why his opinions are cited in later Hanafi works.

Key Terms
الحنفية (al-Hanafiyya): The Hanafi school of law, to which the scholar belonged.
العلامة (al-Allama): A title meaning 'most learned scholar' used repeatedly to describe the subject.

Allama Qasim: The Seal of the Hanafi Mujtahids
Biographical introduction praising the scholar and listing his works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key scholarly contributions of Allama Qasim and explain why he is considered a pivotal figure in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Allama Qasim, author of over 160 works, was called the 'seal of the mujtahids'—a testament to his authority in Hanafi fiqh and usul.

This introduction to a major Hanafi usul work presents the biography of Allama Qasim, a scholar whose vast output and high praise from later authorities underscore his importance. Understanding his stature helps us appreciate why his works, including commentaries on usul texts, carry weight in the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the praises
List the scholars who praised Allama Qasim and the specific qualities they attributed to him.
e.g., Ibn al-Himsi said 'no similar Hanafi was left'; Ibn Abidin called him 'the seal of the mujtahids'.
2
Note the range of his works
From the list of fields in which he wrote, identify the disciplines most relevant to usul al-fiqh.
Focus on 'usul al-fiqh', 'Hanafi fiqh', 'hadith', and 'takhrij'.
3
Assess his impact
Consider why the author of this usul text chose to include this biography. What does it tell us about the authority of the commentator or the work?
Biographies establish credibility; this suggests the commentator or editor is drawing on Qasim's legacy.

These magnificent works gained consideration and reliance, and received ample acceptance among great scholars. Allah facilitated the service of a number of them in this era through university theses and scientific research, and they have been verified and printed.

Commentary
This passage is a biography of Allama Qasim (likely Qasim ibn Qutlubugha, d. 879 AH/1474 CE), a towering Hanafi scholar from the 9th century AH. It opens with glowing testimonies from several renowned scholars. Shihab al-Din Ibn al-Himsi calls him the greatest Hanafi of his time. Ibn al-Imad declares him 'one of the wonders of the age.' Ibn Abidin, the great late Hanafi jurist, refers to him in his gloss on al-Durr al-Mukhtar, praising his thoroughness and calling him 'the seal of the mujtahids.' Al-Lakhnawi, a later Indian Hanafi scholar, testifies to the breadth and usefulness of his writings. The passage then details his early start in authorship: he began writing at age 18, around the year 820 AH. His output was prodigious—over 160 works—spanning a vast range of Islamic sciences: creed (aqida), tafsir, qira'at, hadith (including its sciences, rijal, jarh wa ta'dil), Hanafi fiqh and its principles (usul al-fiqh), sira, history, Arabic grammar and morphology, prosody, logic, and more. His expertise was especially marked in hadith and Hanafi fiqh/usul. His works gained wide acceptance and many have been edited and published in modern times through academic research. This biographical window serves as a front matter to a major Hanafi usul work, establishing the authority of the commentator or author.

Key Terms
خاتمة المجتهدين (khatimat al-mujtahidin): Title meaning 'seal of the mujtahids', indicating that Allama Qasim was considered the last great independent jurist capable of ijtihad.
العلامة قاسم (al-‘Allama Qasim): Refers to the Hanafi scholar Qasim ibn Qutlubugha (or a similar name), a prolific author and jurist.

Allamah Qasim: A Prolific Hanafi Scholar and Defender of the School
Biographical overview of the author's works and scholarly output

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the scope of Allamah Qasim's writings and explain how his works defend and develop Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Over 160 works across multiple sciences, Qasim's writings defend Hanafi positions with rigorous hadith and usul analysis.

This lesson introduces the scholarly output of Allamah Qasim, a Hanafi jurist and muhaddith. We'll see how his early start and broad expertise enabled him to produce works that correct, defend, and expand Hanafi fiqh and usul.

Guided Path
1
Note the author's timeline and output
Identify that Allamah Qasim began authoring at age 18 (born 802 AH, started 820 AH) and his total works exceed 160 books, ranging from small treatises to multi-volume collections.
This shows remarkable productivity for a young scholar.
2
Recognize the breadth of fields
Scan the list: creed, tafsir, qira'at, hadith, rijal, fiqh, usul al-fiqh, sirah, history, Arabic grammar, logic, etc. Note his particular excellence in hadith and Hanafi fiqh and usul.
His expertise was not limited to fiqh; he mastered multiple disciplines.
3
Identify the defensive nature of many works
Look at entries 2–5 in the list: they are responses to objections against Abu Hanifa or Hanafi usul. These show Qasim's role in defending the school against critics like Bukhari, Ibn Abi Shayba, and Ibn Jama'ah.
Such works are crucial for understanding how later Hanafis rebutted criticisms.
4
Examine the takhrij works
Entries 1, 10, 12–17 involve extracting hadith from key Hanafi or related texts (e.g., Ihya', Sharh al-Aqa'id, Tafsir Abi al-Layth). These provide hadith verification for arguments used in usul and fiqh.
Takhrij is a method that strengthens proofs by tracing ahadith to their sources.
5
Conclude the impact on Hanafi scholarship
Reflect on how these works collectively defend, refine, and propagate Hanafi usul and fiqh. Qasim's output serves as a resource for later scholars and modern researchers.
His works continue to be studied and cited in contemporary Hanafi research.

لقد كان العلامة قاسم لتقدمه في العلوم وذكائه وحفظه وما منحه الله من المواهب من المبكرين في السن حين بدأ بالتأليف، فقد قال تلميذه الإمام السخاوي في الضوء اللامع ١٨٦/٦ وهو يتكلم عن مصنفات العلامة قاسم : وأقبل على التأليف - كما حكاه لي ـ من سنة عشرين، وهلم جراً». اهـ أي كان عمره ه (۱۸) سنة ، حيث ولد سنة ٨٠٢هـ.
وقد بارك الله له في وقته، ووفقه لكتابة مصنفات كثيرة، مليئة بالعلم، فياضة بالفوائد النادرة مع التحقيق والتدقيق، والإبداع والاستدراك فيها على من قبله بل على مشايخه الأئمة الكبار.

وقد كتب لهذه المصنفات الجليلة الاعتبار والاعتماد، ونالت حظاً وافراً من القبول عند كبار العلماء، ويسر الله خدمة عدد منها في هذا الزمن، من خلال الرسائل الجامعية والبحوث العلمية وتم تحقيقها وطباعتها.
وأسرد فيما يلي عدداً من أهم مؤلفاته المتنوعة، ومن أراد استقصاءها لاگ ورد فالرجوع إلى ترجماته الموسعة سهل ميسر:
١ - إتحاف الأحياء بما فات من تخريج أحاديث الإحياء للعراقي.
- الأجوبة على اعتراضات البخاري على أبي حنيفة.
- الأجوبة عن اعتراضات ابن أبي شيبة على أبي حنيفة.
٤ - الأجوبة عن اعتراضات العز ابن جماعة على أصول الحنفية.
ه - الأجوبة عن اعتراضات ابن أبي العز على الهداية للمرغيناني.
٦ - أحكام القهقهة.
۷- اختصار «تلخيص المفتاح في المعاني والبيان، للسكاكي.
-۸ الأمالي على مسند أبي حنيفة.
٩- الاهتمام الكلي بإصلاح ثقات العجلي
١٠ - بغية الرائد في تخريج أحاديث شرح العقائد (النسفية).
١١ - تاج التراجم في طبقات الحنفية.
۱۲ - تخريج أحاديث الأربعين في أصول الدين للغزالي.
۱۳ - تخريج أحاديث بداية الهداية، للغزالي.
١٤ - تخريج أحاديث تفسير أبي الليث، للسمرقندي.
١٥ - تخريج أحاديث «جواهر القرآن»، للغزالي.

١٧ - تخريج أحاديث الشفا، للقاضي عياض.
His numerous works
Indeed, Allamah Qasim, due to his advancement in the sciences, his intelligence, his memory, and the talents God bestowed upon him, was among those who began authorship early in age. His student, Imam al-Sakhawi, said in al-Daw' al-Lami' (6/186), speaking about Allamah Qasim's works: 'He turned to authorship - as he narrated to me - from the year 820.' Meaning he was 18 years old, as he was born in 802 AH.
God blessed his time and enabled him to write many works, full of knowledge, overflowing with rare benefits with verification and precision, creativity, and corrections of those before him, even of his great Imam teachers.
His works exceeded 160 books; some are in small treatises but full of benefits and corrections, and some are in volumes, covering various fields: creed, tafsir and its sciences, qira'at, hadith and its commentaries and sciences, rijal and jarh wa ta'dil, hadith extraction, Hanafi fiqh and its branches, usul al-fiqh, prophetic biography, biographies, history, grammar, morphology, prosody, logic, and other sciences. He excelled particularly and clearly in the field of hadith and its sciences, and in Hanafi fiqh and its principles.
These important works gained esteem and reliance, and received ample acceptance among senior scholars. God facilitated the service of a number of them in this era, through university dissertations and academic research, and they were verified and printed.
I list below a number of his most important diverse works. Whoever wants to exhaust them, [the word 'laag ward' is unclear] then referring to his extensive biographies is easy and facilitated:
1. Ittihaf al-Ahya' bima Fata min Takhrij Ahadith al-Ihya' li al-'Iraqi.
2. al-Ajwibah 'ala I'tiradat al-Bukhari 'ala Abi Hanifah.
3. al-Ajwibah 'an I'tiradat Ibn Abi Shaybah 'ala Abi Hanifah.
4. al-Ajwibah 'an I'tiradat al-'Izz Ibn Jama'ah 'ala Usul al-Hanafiyyah.
5. al-Ajwibah 'an I'tiradat Ibn Abi al-'Izz 'ala al-Hidayah li al-Marghinani.
6. Ahkam al-Qahqahah.
7. Ikhtisar 'Talkhis al-Miftah fi al-Ma'ani wa al-Bayan' li al-Sakkaki.
8. al-Amali 'ala Musnad Abi Hanifah.
9. al-Ihtimam al-Kulli bi Islah Thiqat al-'Ijli.
10. Bughyat al-Ra'id fi Takhrij Ahadith Sharh al-'Aqa'id (al-Nasafiyyah).
11. Taj al-Tarajim fi Tabaqat al-Hanafiyyah.
12. Takhrij Ahadith al-Arba'in fi Usul al-Din li al-Ghazali.
13. Takhrij Ahadith Bidayat al-Hidayah li al-Ghazali.
14. Takhrij Ahadith Tafsir Abi al-Layth al-Samarqandi.
15. Takhrij Ahadith 'Jawahir al-Qur'an' li al-Ghazali.
16. Takhrij Ahadith Sharh al-Quduri li al-Aqta'.
17. Takhrij Ahadith al-Shifa' li al-Qadi 'Iyad.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to the author, Allamah Qasim. It highlights his early start in authorship at age 18, and his immense productivity resulting in over 160 works covering a wide range of Islamic sciences: creed, Qur'anic exegesis, readings of the Qur'an, hadith and its sciences, the science of narrators, Hanafi jurisprudence and its principles, prophetic biography, history, Arabic grammar and morphology, prosody, logic, and more. The author excelled particularly in hadith and Hanafi fiqh. The passage then lists 17 of his major works, many of which are responses to objections against Hanafi positions or compilations of hadith, showing his role in defending the school. This list is not exhaustive; the reader is directed to his comprehensive biographies for a full account.

Key Terms
تخريج الأحاديث (takhrij al-ahadith): The process of extracting and verifying hadith from a text, identifying their sources and chains of transmission.
اعتراضات (i'tiradat): Objections or criticisms, usually directed against a school's positions.
أصول الحنفية (usul al-hanafiyyah): The principles of Hanafi jurisprudence, including sources and methods of legal reasoning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Methodology of 'Allamah Qasim in Takhrij of Usul al-Bazdawi
Describes author's method, features, and sources of his takhrij

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key features of 'Allamah Qasim's takhrij methodology and explain its significance for Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Qasim's takhrij is concise yet includes critical usul insights and rare sources.

This passage introduces the methodology and distinctive features of 'Allamah Qasim's takhrij for al-Bazdawi's seminal Hanafi usul work. Understanding his approach helps students appreciate how later scholars verified and augmented the hadith evidence in foundational usul texts, a crucial skill for authenticating legal arguments.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's stated methodology
From the quoted introduction, note that Qasim composed his takhrij concisely, relying on al-Bazdawi's own attributions and, where absent, on the commentary of 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Bukhari.
This shows his method of supplementing gaps with established scholarly authority.
2
Recognize the chronological context
Qasim wrote the takhrij in 859 AH at age 57, indicating a mature scholar. Also note his claim of priority in this endeavor.
This gives historical weight to the work.
3
Analyze the arrangement and user-friendliness
The takhrij follows al-Bazdawi's chapter order, extracting all narrations per section for quick reference.
This structural choice aids efficiency.
4
Note the balance between conciseness and detail
Though generally concise, Qasim elaborates on key hadiths (e.g., al-'Usaylah, prohibition of dabb) and provides variant wordings.
This selectivity shows his prioritization of important legal evidence.
5
Evaluate the inclusion of usul insights and rare sources
Qasim interjects subtle usul corrections and uses rare works like al-Asl and Mukhtasar al-Karkhi, adding unique value.
This elevates the takhrij beyond mere hadith sourcing to a critical edition.

منهج العلامة قاسم في تخريج أحاديث أصول البزدوي ، وذكر مزاياه
١ - ذكر العلامة قاسم منهجه باختصار في مقدمة الكتاب، حيث قال:
«هذا تخريج ما ذُكر في كتاب البزدوي في أصول الفقه الأحاديث والآثار، علقته على وجه الإيجاز ،والاختصار، مُعَوِّلاً فيما لم يُصرح به الماتنُ على تصريح الشارح عبد العزيز البخاري رحمه الله، والله المستعان وعليه التكلان...». اهـ
وقد ألفه رحمه الله سنة ٨٥٩هـ، كما جاء بخطه في آخر نسخته، وله من العمر ٥٧ سنة، وقد تقدم في العلم ونضج.
-۲- ذكر العلامة قاسم كتابه هذا في ترجمة الإمام البزدوي في كتابه: تاج التراجم ص ٢٠٦ ، حين ذكر كتاب البزدوي أصول الفقه، فقال: قد خرَّجتُ أحاديثه ، ولم أُسبق إلى ذلك، والله الموفق». اهـ
اعتمد العلامة قاسم على ما صرح به الإمام البزدوي في ذكر الحديث أو الأثر في الاستدلال، وما لم يصرح به البزدوي: اعتمد ما صرح بنسبته كحديث أو أثر شارح الكتاب البخاري في شرحه: «كشف الأسرار»، كما تقدم في كلامه رحمه الله.
٤- رتَّب كتابه بحسب ترتيب كتاب البزدوي، فهو بعد ذكره لعنوان الباب في أصول البزدوي : يُخرج كل ما ورد فيه من أحاديث أو آثار، وبذا يجد القارئ بغيته بأسرع نظرة، مع ما يسر لي الله من خدمة أصول البزدوي معه وتحقيقه وطبعه في أعلى صفحات الكتاب، وربط كل تخريج بأصله.
٥- يُستفاد من مقدمة المؤلف أن تخريجه للأحاديث والآثار كان باختصار، وهذا فعلاً هو واقع الكتاب، بل أحياناً يحيل على تخريجه لأحاديث «الاختيار»، أو إلى غيره إلا في مواطن قليلة أطال فيها النفس في التخريج وتتبع الطرق لحاجة مهمة ، أرادها، وفائدة نادرة أداها، بل إنه في حديث العسيلة يقول: «قد تتبَّعتُ ألفاظ هذا الحديث جهدي...». اهـ، وكذلك حديث: نضر الله امرءا...»، فقد قال في آخر تخريجه له: انتهى ما علمت ألفاظه اهـ، وهكذا أطال في حديث تحريم أكل الضب، وحديث: لا وصية لوارث».
٦ - لم يُخل العلامةُ قاسم تخريجه للكتاب من بعض الفوائد الأصولية الدقيقة، والإشارات الاستدلالية اللطيفة التي استدرك بها على الإمام البزدوي، وقد بثها في مواضعها عند تخريجه لأحاديث الباب، ومعلومٌ تقدم العلامة قاسم وتبحره في علم الفقه وأصوله.
بل كان للعلامة قاسم دور في الاستدلال لمسائل عديدة في الكتاب. وأما مصادره في التخريج فكثيرة ومنها ما هو نادر، بل منها ما غیر مظنَّة لوجود الحديث أو الأثر فيها مثل كتاب «الأصل» لمحمد ابن الحسن، ومختصر الكرخي في الفقه الحنفي، حيث يروي الكرخي الأحاديث بسنده المتصل، وغيرهما.
وهذا من المزايا الدقيقة الرائعة البديعة التي انفرد بها العلامة قاسم في التخريج في هذا الكتاب وفي غيره من الكتب العديدة التي ألفها في
Methodology of 'Allamah Qasim in the takhrij of the hadiths of Usul al-Bazdawi, and mention of its merits. 1 - 'Allamah Qasim mentioned his methodology briefly in the introduction of the book, where he said: 'This is a takhrij of the hadiths and athars mentioned in the book of al-Bazdawi on usul al-fiqh. I wrote it concisely and briefly, relying, in what the author (al-Bazdawi) did not explicitly state, on the explicit statement of the commentator 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Bukhari, may Allah have mercy on him. And Allah is the Helper, and upon Him is reliance.' He authored it, may Allah have mercy on him, in the year 859 AH, as came in his handwriting at the end of his copy, and he was 57 years old, and he had advanced in knowledge and maturity. 2 - 'Allamah Qasim mentioned this book of his in the biography of Imam al-Bazdawi in his book Taj al-Tarajim, p. 206, when he mentioned al-Bazdawi's book Usul al-Fiqh, and said: 'I have extracted (kharrajtu) its hadiths, and I have not been preceded in that, and Allah is the Granter of success.' 4 - He arranged his book according to the arrangement of al-Bazdawi's book. So after mentioning the title of the chapter in Usul al-Bazdawi, he extracts every hadith or athar that occurs therein. Thus the reader finds his aim with the quickest glance, with what Allah facilitated for me of serving Usul al-Bazdawi along with it, verifying and printing it at the top of the pages of the book, and linking each takhrij to its source. 5 - It is understood from the author's introduction that his takhrij of hadiths and athars was concise, and this is actually the reality of the book. Rather, sometimes he refers to his takhrij of the hadiths of 'al-Ikhtiyar' or to others, except in a few places where he elaborated in takhrij and traced paths for an important need he intended, and a rare benefit he delivered. Rather, in the hadith of al-'Usaylah he says: 'I have traced the wordings of this hadith to the best of my effort.' Similarly, the hadith 'Naddara Allahu imra'an...' he said at the end of its takhrij: '...ended what I know of its wordings.' And likewise he elaborated in the hadith of prohibition of eating dabb (lizard) and the hadith 'No bequest to an heir.' 6 - 'Allamah Qasim did not leave his takhrij of the book free from some precise usul benefits and subtle inferential indications by which he corrected Imam al-Bazdawi. He scattered them in their places when extracting the hadiths of the chapter, and it is known the advancement of 'Allamah Qasim and his deep knowledge in fiqh and its principles. Rather, 'Allamah Qasim had a role in inference for many issues in the book. As for his sources in takhrij, they are many, among them are rare ones, and among them are what are not expected to contain hadith or athar, such as the book 'al-Asl' by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, and Mukhtasar al-Karkhi in Hanafi fiqh, where al-Karkhi narrates hadiths with his connected chain, and others. And this is among the precise, wonderful, and novel merits that 'Allamah Qasim uniquely possessed in takhrij in this book and in the numerous other books he authored in
Source pages p. 76

Commentary
This passage introduces the methodology and distinctive features of 'Allamah Qasim's takhrij (extraction of hadith and athar references) for al-Bazdawi's seminal Hanafi usul work, 'Kanz al-Wusul ila Ma'rifat al-Usul'. The author begins by quoting his own concise introduction from the book, where he states that his takhrij is brief and relies primarily on al-Bazdawi's own citations; where al-Bazdawi does not explicitly attribute a hadith, Qasim relies on the commentary of 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Bukhari in 'Kashf al-Asrar'. He wrote the takhrij in 859 AH at age 57, indicating his scholarly maturity. Qasim mentions this work in his biographical dictionary 'Taj al-Tarajim' under al-Bazdawi's entry, claiming priority in this undertaking. A key feature is the arrangement: Qasim follows al-Bazdawi's chapter order, extracting all narrations from each section, making it easy for the reader to find the source. Despite the overall conciseness, Qasim elaborates in a few important instances, such as the hadith of al-'Usaylah (regarding mutual consent in marriage annulment) and the hadith 'Naddara Allahu imra'an...' (on preserving knowledge), where he traces variant wordings. He also provides lengthy treatments for the hadith on eating dabb (lizard) and the prohibition of bequests to heirs. Importantly, Qasim includes subtle usul insights and corrections to al-Bazdawi, demonstrating his expertise. His sources include rare works like Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani's 'al-Asl' and al-Karkhi's 'Mukhtasar', which contain hadiths with connected chains, adding unique value.

Key Terms
تخريج (takhrij): The process of tracing hadiths and athars to their original sources, including citation of chains and references.
أصول البزدوي (Usul al-Bazdawi): The Hanafi usul work 'Kanz al-Wusul ila Ma'rifat al-Usul' by Imam Fakhr al-Islam al-Bazdawi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The commentary of 'Abd al-'Aziz al-Bukhari

D) The hadith collections of Bukhari and Muslim

Key Takeaway
'Allamah Qasim's takhrij methodology combines concise hadith sourcing with critical usul insights and rare references, making it a valuable tool for Hanafi usul scholars.

Allama Qasim's Takhrij Methodology in Hanafi Usul
Editorial methodology of Allama Qasim in takhrij

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe Allama Qasim's approach to takhrij and explain how his methodology contributes to the verification of hadiths in Hanafi usul al-fiqh.

Core Idea
Allama Qasim's takhrij corrects earlier scholars and enriches Hanafi usul by employing rare sources and precise istidlal.

This lesson introduces the editorial methodology of the Hanafi scholar Allama Qasim in his work on Usul al-Bazdawi. You will learn how he approached the verification of hadiths (takhrij), his use of rare sources, and how he often corrected the claims of other prominent mukhrijin. Understanding this methodology is crucial for appreciating the depth of Hanafi hadith criticism and its role in usul al-fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the context of the passage
Understand that this passage is a editor's preface describing his methodology in verifying hadiths for Usul al-Bazdawi, a key Hanafi usul text. It is not a ruling but a description of scholarly practice.
The passage is from the editor's introduction, not from the original matn.
2
Extract the key features of his takhrij approach
Note the tension between conciseness and expansion: he generally keeps takhrij brief, but expands for important or rare hadiths. Identify the examples given (hadith al-'asila, hadith of may Allah brighten, prohibition of dabb, no bequest to heir).
Expansion indicates the hadith's significance or the need to correct previous claims.
3
Recognize the role of istidrak (correction)
Allama Qasim does not only trace hadiths; he actively corrects Imam al-Bazdawi and other mukhrijin (e.g., those of al-Hidayah) when they claim a hadith has no basis. This is a central feature of his work.
Istidrak is a common scholarly practice in the Hanafi tradition.
4
Note the diversity of sources
He uses rare sources like Muhammad ibn al-Hasan's 'al-Asl' and Mukhtasar al-Karkhi, not typical for hadith collections. This shows his extensive reach and innovation in takhrij.
These sources are primarily fiqh works, not hadith compilations.
5
Connect to broader Hanafi usul practice
His takhrij serves the Hanafi school by providing proofs and refining usul arguments. The passage recommends consulting his takhrij works and Ibn al-Humam's Fath al-Qadir over other compilations.
This underscores the importance of authoritative takhrij in Hanafi scholarship.

What Allah has facilitated for me in serving the book Usul al-Bazdawi with it, its verification, and printing in the top pages of the book, and linking each takhrij to its source. 6 5- It is benefited from the author's introduction that his takhrij of hadiths and athar was concise, and this is indeed the reality of the book. Rather, sometimes he refers to his takhrij of the hadiths of 'al-Ikhtiyar' or to others except in a few places where he expanded in takhrij and traced paths for an important need he intended and a rare benefit he delivered. Indeed, in the hadith of al-'Asila he says: 'I have traced the wordings of this hadith as much as I could...' etc. And likewise the hadith: 'May Allah brighten a person...' He said at the end of its takhrij: 'This is what I know of its wordings,' etc. And likewise he expanded in the hadith of prohibition of eating the dabb, and the hadith: 'No bequest to an heir.' From 6- Allama Qasim did not leave his takhrij of the book without some precise usul benefits and subtle istidlal pointers by which he corrected Imam al-Bazdawi, and he scattered them in their places when extracting the hadiths of the chapter. And the advancement of Allama Qasim and his expertise in fiqh and usul are known. Rather, Allama Qasim had a role in deducing rulings for many issues in the book. His sources in takhrij are many, and among them are rare ones, indeed some that are not expected to contain hadith or athar, such as the book 'al-Asl' by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, and Mukhtasar al-Karkhi in Hanafi fiqh, where al-Karkhi narrates hadiths with his connected chain, and others. And this is among the precise, wonderful, and unique advantages that Allama Qasim was distinguished by in takhrij in this book and in other numerous books he authored in takhrij, such as Munyat al-Alma'i, and Ittihaf al-Ahya', and al-Ta'rif wa al-Ikbar bi Takhrij Ahadith al-Ikhtiyar, by which he corrected other major imams, muhaddithin, and hafiz mukhrijin, like the mukhrijin of the book al-Hidaya by al-Marghinani. For when they say about a hadith 'it has no basis,' often Allama Qasim comes forward and corrects them, saying that such and such has extracted it, which they had not come across. And glory be to the Bestower. He explains: Proposal for serving the books of Allama Qasim in takhrij: Based on this, it is necessary and emphatically for whoever wants to know the takhrij of the hadiths of the Hanafi books and their proofs to look into the books of Allama Qasim in takhrij, which are many, and also in the book of his teacher Imam Ibn al-Humam: 'Fath al-Qadir Sharh al-Hidaya,' and not to limit themselves to Nasb al-Rayah and al-Diraya. And I propose here that the works of Allama Qasim on takhrij be served, and all be printed within the covers of one book, linked by indexes, and be like an encyclopedia. For in that is a great and magnificent service to the Prophetic Sunnah, and important benefits and additions in the takhrij of hadiths and proofs that concern the student of fiqh, the deducer, and the students of the Prophetic Sunnah. And the number of his books on takhrij, between large in volume, medium, and small, reached (14) books, along with his works in many arts: in creed and principles of religion, tafsir, fiqh, fara'id, usul al-fiqh, prophetic biography, shama'il, purification of souls, and others. The number of hadiths and athars he extracted in this book in detail reached more than a thousand, which is a large number for a book in usul al-fiqh. As for his takhrij of the book 'al-Ikhtiyar,' which is a book for deducing branches, it reached number
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and methodological introduction to the editor's (Allama Qasim) work on Al-Bazdawi's Usul. It describes his takhrij (hadith verification) approach. The editor states that his takhrij is generally concise, but he expands on important or rare hadiths, such as 'hadith al-'asila', 'hadith naddara Allahu imra'an', and 'la wasiyyata li-warith'. He also includes subtle usul benefits and istidlal pointers, correcting Imam al-Bazdawi where needed. His sources include rare works like Muhammad ibn al-Hasan's 'al-Asl' and Mukhtasar al-Karkhi. A unique feature is that he often corrects other mukhrijin (like those of al-Hidaya) when they claim a hadith has no basis, pointing out its presence in other sources. The passage recommends consulting Qasim's takhrij works and Ibn al-Humam's Fath al-Qadir over limiting to Nasb al-Rayah. It proposes compiling all 14 of his takhrij books into one encyclopedia. Finally, it notes that in this usul book, he extracted over a thousand hadiths, a large number for a usul work.

Key Terms
التخريج (al-takhrij): The process of tracing and verifying hadiths, providing their sources and chains of transmission.
الاستدراك (al-istidrak): The act of correcting or supplementing a previous scholar's work, pointing out overlooked hadiths or errors.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

Key Takeaway
Allama Qasim's takhrij methodology combines brevity with expanded verification when needed, and corrects prior scholars, serving as a model for rigorous hadith work in Hanafi usul.

The Role of Takhrij in Hanafi Usul al-Fiqh
Describing the importance of Qasim's takhrij works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the function of takhrij in verifying hadiths for Hanafi usul and identify the key works of Qasim on this topic.

Core Idea
A hadith's chain is the backbone of Hanafi usul—takhrij ensures the ruling stands on sound evidence.

In Hanafi usul al-fiqh, many rulings are built upon hadiths. But not all hadiths are equally verified. Takhrij—the science of tracing and authenticating hadiths—is essential for any scholar or student who wants to rely on prophetic evidence. This lesson introduces the works of the Hanafi scholar Qasim, who dedicated fourteen books to this task.

Guided Path
1
Define takhrij and its role in usul al-fiqh
Understand that takhrij means tracing a hadith to its original sources and assessing its authenticity. In Hanafi usul, it is critical for determining the strength of dalil.
2
Identify key Hanafi texts requiring takhrij
Recognize that major works like Al-Hidayah and Al-Ikhtiyar have dedicated takhrij works. Qasim's works often correct other scholars' claims of 'no basis'.
3
Recognize Qasim's contribution
Note that Qasim authored 14 books on takhrij, extracting over 1000 hadiths in his usul work and 2016 in his work on Al-Ikhtiyar.
4
Understand his methodology when exact wording is missing
If the exact hadith wording is not found, Qasim uses the closest wording and indicates this. He usually grades the hadith but sometimes omits the ruling.
5
Appreciate the importance for students of usul
The passage emphasizes that anyone wanting to know Hanafi hadith evidence must consult Qasim's works and Fath al-Qadir, not just Nasb al-Raya and al-Diraya.

التخريج كمنية الألمعي، وإتحاف الأحياء والتعريف والإخبار بتخريج أحاديث الاختيار والتي استدرك بها على غيره من كبار الأئمة المحدثين الحفاظ المخرجين ، كمخرجي كتاب الهداية للمرغيناني، فإنه حين يقولون عند حديث لا أصل له كثيراً ما ينبري العلامة قاسم ويستدرك عليهم، أنه أخرجه فلان وفلان مما لم يقفوا عليه، وسبحان الوهاب. ويبين اقتراح لخدمة كتب العلامة قاسم في التخريج : وعلى هذا، فإنه ينبغي وبتأكد على من يريد معرفة تخريج أحاديث كتب الحنفية وأدلتهم أن ينظر في كتب العلامة قاسم في التخريج وهي كثيرة، وكذلك في كتاب شيخه الإمام ابن الهمام: «فتح القدير شرح الهداية، وألا يقتصر على نصب الراية والدراية. (() ألفها في وأقترح بالمناسبة هنا أن تُخدم مؤلفات العلامة قاسم التي التخريج، وتُطبع كلها بين دفتي كتاب واحد، ويُربط بينها بالفهارس، وتكون كالموسوعة ، ففي ذلك خدمة جليلة عظيمة للسنة النبوية، وإفادات وزيادات مهمة في تخريج الأحاديث والأدلة تهم طالب الفقه والمستدلَّ وطلاب السنة النبوية. وقد بلغ عدد كتبه التي ألفها في التخريج بين كبير في الحجم ومتوسط وصغير بلغت (١٤) كتابا، مع ما له من المؤلفات في فنون كثيرة: في العقائد وأصول الدين، والتفسير والفقه والفرائض، وأصول الفقه، والسيرة النبوية والشمائل وتزكية النفوس وغيرها. وصل عدد الأحاديث والآثار التي خرجها في هذا الكتاب تفصيلاً إلى أكثر من ألف، وهو عدد كبير بالنسبة لكتاب في أصول الفقه، أما في تخريجه لكتاب الاختيار»، وهو كتاب استدلال للفروع، فقد وصل عدد الأحاديث والآثار المخرجة إلى (٢٠١٦) حديثاً. ٩- إذا لم يجد المؤلف نص الحديث المذكور في أصول البزدوي الذي يريد تخريجه : فإنه يأتي بأقرب الألفاظ إليه، ويشير إلى ذلك. وأنبه هنا إلى قضية مهمة جداً في تخريج أحاديث الكتاب بشكل عام، وتخريج اللفظ نفسه الذي ذكره مؤلف الكتاب الإمام البزدوي، فالمخرج للحديث يذكر أحياناً عشرة مصادر للحديث أو أكثر، ولا شك أن هذه أصول الحديثية التي عزى إليها المخرج ليست متحدة في لفظ الحديث، بل قد تختلف نُسَخُ الكتاب الواحد وهذا طبيعي جدا حاصل في كل الكتب التي تُعنى بالتخريج وعزو الحديث إلى الأصول، وعلى رأسها: جامع الأصول لابن الأثير، والترغيب والترهيب للمنذري، والجامع الصغير للسيوطي، ونحوها ، وهو أمر يجب أن يتنبه إليه. الأصـ ١٠ - يبين المؤلف في الغالب درجة الحديث وحكمه فيه، وفي أحيان أخرى لا يذكر شيئاً. ١١ - للكتاب نسختان إحداهما بخط المؤلف، بتاريخ ٨٥٩هـ، ونسخة أخرى بخط تلميذ المؤلف محمد بن عمران الحنفي، بتاريخ ٨٦٤هـ، وفيها بلاغات بالمقابلة، وفي آخرها بخط المؤلف: أنه قرأ الكتاب عليه تلميذه الناسخ، وأنه أجازه بروايته عنه. والذي توصلتُ إليه من خلال مقابلة النسختين أن المؤلف في نسخة التلميذ قد صقل الكتاب وحرَّره حين قرأه عليه، وغيّر في بعض ألفاظه، وأضاف فيه زيادات على نسخته التي هي بخط يده، ومَلاً بعض البياضات التي تركها في نسخته ،وهذا كله يجعل نسخة التلميذ المجاز بها هي النسخة المعدلة المحررة المعتمدة، والله أعلم.
Takhrij as the wish of the brilliant, and joining the living and the definition and information by extracting the hadiths of Al-Ikhtiyar which he used to correct others from the great hadith scholars and preservers, like the extractors of Al-Hidayah by Al-Marghinani, for when they say about a hadith 'it has no basis', often the scholar Qasim rises and corrects them, that it was extracted by so-and-so which they did not come across. And the Giver is glorified. And he explains a proposal for serving the books of the scholar Qasim in takhrij. Upon this, it is strongly incumbent upon whoever wants to know the takhrij of hadiths of Hanafi books and their evidences to look into the books of the scholar Qasim on takhrij, which are many, and likewise in the book of his teacher Imam Ibn al-Humam: 'Fath al-Qadir Sharh al-Hidaya', and not to limit himself to Nasb al-Raya and al-Diraya. He authored them. And I suggest here that the works of the scholar Qasim on takhrij be compiled and printed in one book, connected by indexes, and be like an encyclopedia. In that is a great and magnificent service to the Prophetic Sunnah, and important benefits and additions in the takhrij of hadiths and evidences which concern the student of fiqh and the one who seeks evidence and the students of the Prophetic Sunnah. The number of books he authored on takhrij, between large in size, medium, and small, reached 14 books, along with his works in many arts: in creeds and principles of religion, tafsir, fiqh, fara'id, usul al-fiqh, prophetic biography, shama'il, purification of souls, and others. The number of hadiths and athars he extracted in this book in detail reached more than a thousand, which is a large number for a book on usul al-fiqh. As for his takhrij of the book 'Al-Ikhtiyar', which is a book of proofs for furu', the number of extracted hadiths and athars reached 2016 hadiths. 9- If the author does not find the text of the mentioned hadith in Usul al-Bazdawi which he wants to extract, he brings the closest wording to it and indicates that. And I draw attention here to a very important issue in the takhrij of hadiths of the book in general, and the takhrij of the exact wording mentioned by the author Imam al-Bazdawi. For the extractor of the hadith sometimes mentions ten sources for the hadith or more, and there is no doubt that these hadith sources that the extractor attributed to are not unified in the wording of the hadith. Rather, the copies of a single book may differ, and this is very natural and occurs in all books that deal with takhrij and attribution of hadith to sources, foremost of which are: Jami' al-Usul by Ibn al-Athir, al-Targhib wa al-Tarhib by al-Mundhiri, al-Jami' al-Saghir by al-Suyuti, and the like. This is something that must be paid attention to. 10- The author mostly clarifies the grade of the hadith and his ruling on it, and at other times he says nothing. 11- The book has two copies: one is the author's manuscript, dated 859 AH, and another copy in the handwriting of the author's student Muhammad ibn Imran al-Hanafi, dated 864 AH, containing collation notices, and at the end in the author's handwriting: that his student the copyist read the book to him, and that he gave him ijaza to narrate it from him. And what I have concluded through comparing the two copies is that the author polished and edited the book in the student's copy when he read it to him, changed some of its wordings, added increases over his own handwritten copy, and filled some blanks he had left in his copy. All this makes the student's copy, which is the one with ijaza, the revised, edited, and dependable copy, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and methodological introduction regarding the works of the scholar Qasim (likely Ibn Qutlubugha or Qasim al-Hanafi) on takhrij (verification and sourcing of hadiths). It emphasizes the importance of his works for Hanafi fiqh scholars, especially those studying usul al-fiqh. The text notes that his takhrij works are essential for verifying the hadiths used in Hanafi texts like Al-Hidayah and Al-Ikhtiyar, and that he often corrected other scholars by finding sources they missed. The author proposes compiling all of Qasim's takhrij works into a single encyclopedia for ease of reference. The passage provides statistical details: 14 books on takhrij, over 1000 hadiths extracted in his usul work, and 2016 in his work on Al-Ikhtiyar. It also describes his methodology: if the exact wording is not found, he uses the closest wording and notes it. He usually grades the hadiths but sometimes omits the ruling. The passage ends with important manuscript information: two copies exist—the author's autograph and a student's copy with ijaza. The student's copy is considered the authoritative version because the author edited and added to it during the reading sessions. This is a key point for textual criticism of the work.

Key Terms
تخريج (takhrij): The process of tracing a hadith or athar to its original sources, verifying its chain and grading its authenticity.
إجازة (ijaza): A license from a scholar to a student authorizing him to transmit the scholar's work.
نسخة (nuskha): A manuscript copy of a book.

Key Takeaway
Takhrij is a critical tool for Hanafi usul scholars, and Qasim's extensive works provide indispensable verification of hadith sources.

Manuscript Criticism in Hanafi Scholarship: The Case of Qasim's Takhrij Work
Describing manuscript details and textual criticism

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply principles of textual criticism to determine the authoritative copy of a classical work, using the example of Qasim's manuscript.

Core Idea
The author's edits in a student's copy can make it more authoritative than the autograph.

When studying a classical text, the physical manuscript matters. The same book may exist in multiple copies with differences. This lesson explores how the Hanafi scholar Qasim's own work went through revisions via his student, producing a final authoritative version.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two manuscripts
Note that there is an author's autograph dated 859 AH and a student's copy dated 864 AH. The student's copy contains collation notices and an ijaza from the author.
2
Observe the differences
The author polished, edited, changed wordings, added content, and filled blanks in the student's copy. This is more than a simple copy; it is a revised edition.
3
Understand the role of ijaza
The student read the book to the author, who then gave permission (ijaza) to transmit it. This implies the author approved the content of the student's copy.
4
Recognize the authoritative principle
The passage concludes that the student's copy is the revised, edited, and dependable version. The author's own copy is earlier and less refined.
5
Apply to other Hanafi texts
When studying any Hanafi work, check if there is a similar scenario: a student's copy with author annotations may be more reliable than the autograph.

التخريج كمنية الألمعي، وإتحاف الأحياء والتعريف والإخبار بتخريج أحاديث الاختيار والتي استدرك بها على غيره من كبار الأئمة المحدثين الحفاظ المخرجين ، كمخرجي كتاب الهداية للمرغيناني، فإنه حين يقولون عند حديث لا أصل له كثيراً ما ينبري العلامة قاسم ويستدرك عليهم، أنه أخرجه فلان وفلان مما لم يقفوا عليه، وسبحان الوهاب. ويبين اقتراح لخدمة كتب العلامة قاسم في التخريج : وعلى هذا، فإنه ينبغي وبتأكد على من يريد معرفة تخريج أحاديث كتب الحنفية وأدلتهم أن ينظر في كتب العلامة قاسم في التخريج وهي كثيرة، وكذلك في كتاب شيخه الإمام ابن الهمام: «فتح القدير شرح الهداية، وألا يقتصر على نصب الراية والدراية. (() ألفها في وأقترح بالمناسبة هنا أن تُخدم مؤلفات العلامة قاسم التي التخريج، وتُطبع كلها بين دفتي كتاب واحد، ويُربط بينها بالفهارس، وتكون كالموسوعة ، ففي ذلك خدمة جليلة عظيمة للسنة النبوية، وإفادات وزيادات مهمة في تخريج الأحاديث والأدلة تهم طالب الفقه والمستدلَّ وطلاب السنة النبوية. وقد بلغ عدد كتبه التي ألفها في التخريج بين كبير في الحجم ومتوسط وصغير بلغت (١٤) كتابا، مع ما له من المؤلفات في فنون كثيرة: في العقائد وأصول الدين، والتفسير والفقه والفرائض، وأصول الفقه، والسيرة النبوية والشمائل وتزكية النفوس وغيرها. وصل عدد الأحاديث والآثار التي خرجها في هذا الكتاب تفصيلاً إلى أكثر من ألف، وهو عدد كبير بالنسبة لكتاب في أصول الفقه، أما في تخريجه لكتاب الاختيار»، وهو كتاب استدلال للفروع، فقد وصل عدد الأحاديث والآثار المخرجة إلى (٢٠١٦) حديثاً. ٩- إذا لم يجد المؤلف نص الحديث المذكور في أصول البزدوي الذي يريد تخريجه : فإنه يأتي بأقرب الألفاظ إليه، ويشير إلى ذلك. وأنبه هنا إلى قضية مهمة جداً في تخريج أحاديث الكتاب بشكل عام، وتخريج اللفظ نفسه الذي ذكره مؤلف الكتاب الإمام البزدوي، فالمخرج للحديث يذكر أحياناً عشرة مصادر للحديث أو أكثر، ولا شك أن هذه أصول الحديثية التي عزى إليها المخرج ليست متحدة في لفظ الحديث، بل قد تختلف نُسَخُ الكتاب الواحد وهذا طبيعي جدا حاصل في كل الكتب التي تُعنى بالتخريج وعزو الحديث إلى الأصول، وعلى رأسها: جامع الأصول لابن الأثير، والترغيب والترهيب للمنذري، والجامع الصغير للسيوطي، ونحوها ، وهو أمر يجب أن يتنبه إليه. الأصـ ١٠ - يبين المؤلف في الغالب درجة الحديث وحكمه فيه، وفي أحيان أخرى لا يذكر شيئاً. ١١ - للكتاب نسختان إحداهما بخط المؤلف، بتاريخ ٨٥٩هـ، ونسخة أخرى بخط تلميذ المؤلف محمد بن عمران الحنفي، بتاريخ ٨٦٤هـ، وفيها بلاغات بالمقابلة، وفي آخرها بخط المؤلف: أنه قرأ الكتاب عليه تلميذه الناسخ، وأنه أجازه بروايته عنه. والذي توصلتُ إليه من خلال مقابلة النسختين أن المؤلف في نسخة التلميذ قد صقل الكتاب وحرَّره حين قرأه عليه، وغيّر في بعض ألفاظه، وأضاف فيه زيادات على نسخته التي هي بخط يده، ومَلاً بعض البياضات التي تركها في نسخته ،وهذا كله يجعل نسخة التلميذ المجاز بها هي النسخة المعدلة المحررة المعتمدة، والله أعلم.
Takhrij as the wish of the brilliant, and joining the living and the definition and information by extracting the hadiths of Al-Ikhtiyar which he used to correct others from the great hadith scholars and preservers, like the extractors of Al-Hidayah by Al-Marghinani, for when they say about a hadith 'it has no basis', often the scholar Qasim rises and corrects them, that it was extracted by so-and-so which they did not come across. And the Giver is glorified. And he explains a proposal for serving the books of the scholar Qasim in takhrij. Upon this, it is strongly incumbent upon whoever wants to know the takhrij of hadiths of Hanafi books and their evidences to look into the books of the scholar Qasim on takhrij, which are many, and likewise in the book of his teacher Imam Ibn al-Humam: 'Fath al-Qadir Sharh al-Hidaya', and not to limit himself to Nasb al-Raya and al-Diraya. He authored them. And I suggest here that the works of the scholar Qasim on takhrij be compiled and printed in one book, connected by indexes, and be like an encyclopedia. In that is a great and magnificent service to the Prophetic Sunnah, and important benefits and additions in the takhrij of hadiths and evidences which concern the student of fiqh and the one who seeks evidence and the students of the Prophetic Sunnah. The number of books he authored on takhrij, between large in size, medium, and small, reached 14 books, along with his works in many arts: in creeds and principles of religion, tafsir, fiqh, fara'id, usul al-fiqh, prophetic biography, shama'il, purification of souls, and others. The number of hadiths and athars he extracted in this book in detail reached more than a thousand, which is a large number for a book on usul al-fiqh. As for his takhrij of the book 'Al-Ikhtiyar', which is a book of proofs for furu', the number of extracted hadiths and athars reached 2016 hadiths. 9- If the author does not find the text of the mentioned hadith in Usul al-Bazdawi which he wants to extract, he brings the closest wording to it and indicates that. And I draw attention here to a very important issue in the takhrij of hadiths of the book in general, and the takhrij of the exact wording mentioned by the author Imam al-Bazdawi. For the extractor of the hadith sometimes mentions ten sources for the hadith or more, and there is no doubt that these hadith sources that the extractor attributed to are not unified in the wording of the hadith. Rather, the copies of a single book may differ, and this is very natural and occurs in all books that deal with takhrij and attribution of hadith to sources, foremost of which are: Jami' al-Usul by Ibn al-Athir, al-Targhib wa al-Tarhib by al-Mundhiri, al-Jami' al-Saghir by al-Suyuti, and the like. This is something that must be paid attention to. 10- The author mostly clarifies the grade of the hadith and his ruling on it, and at other times he says nothing. 11- The book has two copies: one is the author's manuscript, dated 859 AH, and another copy in the handwriting of the author's student Muhammad ibn Imran al-Hanafi, dated 864 AH, containing collation notices, and at the end in the author's handwriting: that his student the copyist read the book to him, and that he gave him ijaza to narrate it from him. And what I have concluded through comparing the two copies is that the author polished and edited the book in the student's copy when he read it to him, changed some of its wordings, added increases over his own handwritten copy, and filled some blanks he had left in his copy. All this makes the student's copy, which is the one with ijaza, the revised, edited, and dependable copy, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 78

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and methodological introduction regarding the works of the scholar Qasim (likely Ibn Qutlubugha or Qasim al-Hanafi) on takhrij (verification and sourcing of hadiths). It emphasizes the importance of his works for Hanafi fiqh scholars, especially those studying usul al-fiqh. The text notes that his takhrij works are essential for verifying the hadiths used in Hanafi texts like Al-Hidayah and Al-Ikhtiyar, and that he often corrected other scholars by finding sources they missed. The author proposes compiling all of Qasim's takhrij works into a single encyclopedia for ease of reference. The passage provides statistical details: 14 books on takhrij, over 1000 hadiths extracted in his usul work, and 2016 in his work on Al-Ikhtiyar. It also describes his methodology: if the exact wording is not found, he uses the closest wording and notes it. He usually grades the hadiths but sometimes omits the ruling. The passage ends with important manuscript information: two copies exist—the author's autograph and a student's copy with ijaza. The student's copy is considered the authoritative version because the author edited and added to it during the reading sessions. This is a key point for textual criticism of the work.

Key Terms
نسخة (nuskha): A manuscript copy of a book.
إجازة (ijaza): A license from a scholar to a student authorizing him to transmit the scholar's work.
مقابلة (muqabala): Collation of a manuscript against an original to ensure accuracy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) 864 AH

D) 14 AH

Key Takeaway
When a Hanafi scholar revises his work through a student's copy, that copy becomes the authoritative version, as seen in Qasim's takhrij manuscript.

Hanafi Creedal Stances Against Mu'tazilism
Concluding discussion on Hanafi creed and opposition to Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key Hanafi creedal positions that distinguish the school from Mu'tazilism and explain why the creation of the Quran issue leads to takfir.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school affirms that Allah creates all actions, rejects al-aslah, and holds that the Quran is uncreated — contradicting Mu'tazila.

This passage from al-Bazdawi's Usul summarizes the creedal commitments of the Hanafi imams. Understanding these positions is crucial because they form the theological foundation for how the Hanafi school approaches usul al-fiqh — especially concerning the authority of revelation and human capacity. The debate on the creation of the Quran, in particular, illustrates the school's firm stance against rationalist excess.

Guided Path
1
Identify the affirmations
Read the passage and list the five creedal affirmations mentioned: capacity with the act, actions created by Allah, rejection of al-aslah, no takfir for sin, and the realities of the Hereafter (vision of Allah, punishment of the grave, creation of Paradise and Hell).
2
Note the rejections
The passage explicitly rejects two Mu'tazili principles: the doctrine of al-aslah (that Allah must do what is best) and the idea of absolute human free will (by affirming that actions are created by Allah).
3
Understand the Quran debate
Focus on the report about Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa debating the creation of the Quran for six months. Their agreement that its proponent is a kafir shows the school's definitive opposition to the Mu'tazili view that the Quran is created.
4
Recognize the Jahmiyyah refutation
The report of Abu Hanifa telling Jahm ibn Safwan 'Get away from me, O unbeliever' indicates the school's stance against the Jahmiyyah, who denied divine attributes.
5
Summarize the Hanafi view on the Hereafter
The passage ends by affirming the reality of seeing Allah, punishment of the grave, and creation of Paradise and Hell — all based on the Book and Sunnah, rejecting allegorical interpretations.

Source Text

وأثبت الاستطاعة مع الفعل، وأن أفعال العباد مخلوقة بخلق الله تعالى إياها كلَّها، وردَّ القولَ بالأصلح.
وصنف كتاب: العالم والمتعلم، وكتاب: «الرسالة»، وقال فيه: لا يُكفَرُ أحد بذنب، ولا يخرج به من الإيمان، ويُترحم له. وكان في علم الأصول إماماً صادقاً.
وقد صح عن أبي يوسف رحمه الله أنه قال: ناظرتُ أبا حنيفة في مسألة خَلْقِ القرآن ستة أشهر، فاتفق رأيي ورأيه على أن من قال بخلق القرآن : فهو كافر.
وقد صح هذا القول عن محمد رحمه الله.
ودلَّت المسائلُ المتفرّقةُ عن أصحابنا في المبسوط وغير المبسوط على أنهم لم يميلوا إلى شيء من مذاهب الاعتزال، وإلى سائر الأهواء. وإنهم قالوا بحَقِّية رؤية الله تعالى بالأبصار في الدار الآخرة.
